# The Mahāyāna Sūtra The King of Samādhis, the Revealed Equality of the Nature of All Phenomena

> **84000 English, stored verbatim as a reference layer** (CC BY-NC-ND — do not excerpt or adapt for output; the shipped verse is our own translation, citing 84000). Tibetan source: `1-SOURCES/Text/bo-toh127.md`. Folio anchors `^F<folio>` align to the Degé Kangyur.

I pay homage to all the buddhas and bodhisattvas. [n1] ^F1b

Thus did I hear at one time: The Bhagavān was residing at Vulture Peak Mountain in Rājagṛha together with a great bhikṣu saṅgha of a full hundred thousand bhikṣus, and together with eighty quintillion [n2] bodhisattvas, [n3] all of whom had one rebirth remaining, were renowned for their higher cognitions, [n4] and had gathered there from the worlds in the ten directions; they had complete mastery [n5] of the dhāraṇīs [n6] and sūtras; they satisfied all beings with the gift of the Dharma; they were skilled in speaking of the wisdom of the higher cognitions; they had attained the highest perfection of all the highest perfections;  they were skilled in the knowledge of remaining in all bodhisattva samādhis and samāpattis; they had been praised, extolled, and lauded by all the buddhas; [n7] they were skilled in miraculously going to all buddha realms; they were skilled in the knowledge of terrifying all māras; [n8] they were skilled in the correct knowledge of the nature of all phenomena; they were skilled in the knowledge of the higher and lower capabilities of all beings; they were skilled in the knowledge of accomplishing the activity of offering to all the buddhas; they were unstained by any of the worldly concerns; they had perfectly adorned bodies, speech, and minds; [n9] they wore the armor of great love and great compassion; they had great undiminishing diligence throughout countless eons; they roared the great lion’s roar; they could not be defeated by any opponent; [n10] they were sealed with nonregression; and they had received the consecration of the Dharma from all buddhas. [n11] They were the bodhisattva mahāsattvas Meru, Sumeru, Mahāmeru, [n12] Meru­śikhara­dhara, [n13] Meru­pradīpa­rāja, Merukūṭa, Merudhvaja, Merurāja, [n14] Meru­śikhara­saṁghaṭṭana­rāja, [n15] Merusvara, Megharāja, Dundubhisvara, Ratnapāṇi, [n16] Ratnākara, Ratnaketu, Ratnaśikhara, Ratnasaṁbhava, Ratnaprabhāsa, Ratnayaṣṭi, Ratna­mudrā­hasta, Ratnavyūha, Ratnajāli, Ratnaprabha, Ratnadvīpa,  Ratiṁkara, Dharmavyūha, Vyūharāja, Lakṣaṇa­samalaṁkṛta, Svaravyūha, Svara­viśuddhi­prabha, Ratnakūṭa, Ratnacūḍa, [n17] Daśa­śata­raśmihutārci, [n18] Jyotirasa, Candrabhānu, Saha­cittotpāda­dharma­cakra­pravartin, and Śubha­kanaka­viśuddhi­prabha, the bodhisatta mahāsattva Satatam­abhayaṁdad, [n19] and all the bodhisattva mahāsattvas of the Good Eon, such as the bodhisattva mahāsattva Ajita, [n20] and the sixty with incomparable minds, [n21] such as Mañjuśrī, and the sixteen good beings, [n22] such as Bhadrapāla, [n23] and the Four Mahārājas and the other Cāturmahā­rāja­kāyika devas, and so on [n24] up until Brahmā and the other Brahmakāyika devas. In addition there were also devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, and nonhumans, who were all illustrious [n25] and renowned as being very powerful. [n26] ^F2b

They honored him, [n27] worshiped him, [n28] revered him, [n29] made offerings to him, [n30] praised him, [n31] and venerated him. [n32] The fourfold assembly and the worlds [n33] of devas also paid homage to him, [n34] made offerings to him, honored him, worshiped him, revered him, praised him, and venerated him.

Then the Bhagavān, encircled and esteemed by that assembly of many hundred thousands, taught the Dharma. He taught perfectly the spiritual conduct that is good in the beginning, good in the middle, and good in the end, that has a good meaning, that has good words, and is unalloyed, complete, pure, and wholesome.

At that time, within that gathered assembly there was a youth [n35] named Candraprabha, who had honored the jinas in the past, had planted roots of merit, could remember his previous lives, had the confidence of speech, had correctly followed the Mahāyāna, and who was dedicated to great compassion.

The youth Candraprabha rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee, with palms placed together bowed toward the Bhagavān and made this request: “If the Bhagavān will give me an opportunity to seek answers to them, I have a few questions for the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.” ^F3a

The Bhagavān addressed the youth Candraprabha, saying, “Young man, ask whatever question you wish of the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha, and I shall gratify you with answers to each and every question you have asked.

“Young man, I am omniscient. [n36] I am all-seeing. I have attained preeminence because of my strengths and fearlessness concerning all Dharmas. I possess the unobscured wisdom of liberation.

“Young man, there is nothing in the endless, infinite worlds [n37] that the Tathāgata does not know, has not seen, has not heard, has not understood, has not directly perceived, and about which he has not become completely enlightened.

“Young man, may you always have the opportunity to ask questions of the Tathāgata, and I will gratify you with answers for each of the questions you ask.”

The Bhagavān having given him this opportunity, the young man Candraprabha [n38] recited these verses to the Bhagavān:

“Lord of the World, Buddha,<br>Illuminator, bringer of benefit,<br>Elucidate what kind of practice<br>Will bring the attainment of inconceivable wisdom. {1}

“Lord of humans, speaker of the truth, preeminent among humans,<br>To whom humans and devas make offerings, how should one practice<br>In order to attain the unfathomable, [n39] supreme, highest yāna?<br>Lord who has supreme speech, answer this question. {2}

“I ask my question with a pure motivation.<br>There is no guile to be seen within me. [n40]<br>I have no witness [n41] to that<br>Other than you, sublime being. {3} ^F3b

“My prayer and my aspiration are vast.<br>Śākya lion, you know my conduct.<br>I will not be one who prizes words.<br>Lord of humans, quickly teach me the practice. {4}

“Which of the Dharmas included<br>In the vehicle of enlightenment are to be cherished? [n42]<br>Elucidate for me, great hero,<br>The summit of all Dharmas. {5}

“Teach to me, Lord, a beneficial Dharma,<br>Through the practice of which a person will have sharp wisdom,<br>Will become free of terrible fears, will be fearless,<br>Will never abandon the aggregate of correct conduct, {6}

“Will be without arrogance, desire, anger, [n43] and ignorance,<br>And will practice a conduct in which all faults have ceased. [n44] {6b}

“How does one not abandon correct conduct?<br>How does one not depart from dhyāna?<br>How does one stay in a solitary place?<br>How does wisdom increase? [n45] {7}

“How does one find joy in maintaining correct conduct<br>Within the vast teaching of the one with ten strengths?<br>How can the aggregate of correct conduct be flawless?<br>How does one examine the nature of the composite? {8}

“How can the wise be pure<br>In body and in speech,<br>And with an unafflicted mind<br>Seek the Buddha’s wisdom? {9}

“How can they have pure actions of the body?<br>How can they avoid faults in speech?<br>How can they have an unafflicted mind?<br>Best of men, give your answer to my questions.” {10}

The Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas will attain all those qualities and quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood if they have one quality. [n46] What is that one quality? Young man, it is the bodhisattva mahāsattvas’ evenness of mind toward all beings. They wish to benefit them, have no anger, and have no partiality. Young man, if bodhisattva mahāsattvas have that one quality  they will attain all those qualities and quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.” ^F4a

The Bhagavān then recited these verses to the youth Candraprabha:

“Having obtained one quality,<br>Those bodhisattvas, whoever they are,<br>Will attain these qualities<br>And quickly attain enlightenment. {11}

“Anger toward anyone does not arise in the mind<br>Of the bodhisattva who has a mind without anger.<br>Those who are not hardhearted or wicked<br>Will attain exactly what has been described. {12}

“As they remain in evenness of mind,<br>There will be an evenness of ripening results:<br>The soles of their feet will be even<br>And their range of conduct will be even. {13}

“They meditate with even minds that are without unevenness.<br>Without the fault of hardheartedness and devoid of craving<br>They have even soles and palms. [n47]<br>They are supremely bright and are seen as pure. {14}

“The bodhisattvas illuminate the ten directions,<br>Spreading splendor and light through a buddha realm. [n48]<br>When they attain the level of peace,<br>They establish many beings in buddha wisdom. {15}

“Young man, in that way the bodhisattva mahāsattva who has evenness of mind toward all beings, wishes to benefit them, and has no anger or partiality will attain the samādhi known as the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena.

“Young man, what is the samādhi called the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena?

“It is restraint of the body. [n49] It is restraint of the speech. It is restraint of the mind. It is purity of action. It is the transcendence of the mind’s perceptions. [n50] It is knowledge of the skandhas. It is the equality of the dhātus. It is the elimination of the āyatanas.

“It is the renunciation of craving. It is having the direct perception of birthlessness. It is engagement in activity. [n51] It is the illumination of causes. [n52] It is the non-dissipation of the results of karma. It is insight into phenomena. It is the meditation of the path. It is meeting the tathāgatas.

“It is sharp wisdom. It is penetrating into beings. [n53] It is knowledge of phenomena. [n54] It is the knowledge of engaging in discernment. It is the knowledge of the different kinds of letters and words. It is the transcendence of matter. It is the understanding of sounds. It is the attainment of joy. It is experiencing the joy of the Dharma. It is sincerity. [n55] It is tolerance. [n56] It is to be without deception. [n57] ^F4b

“It is to be without frowns. It is to be pleasant. [n58] It is to have correct conduct. [n59] It is to be friendly. [n60] It is to be gentle. [n61] It is having a smiling face. [n62] It is being courteous. [n63] It is to be welcoming. [n64]

“It is to be without laziness. [n65] It is having veneration [n66] for the guru. [n67] It is respect [n68] for the guru. It is being content with occurrences. It is never being satisfied with the good actions one has done. It is having a pure livelihood. It is not forsaking the solitary life.

“It is the knowledge of successive levels. It is always maintaining mindfulness. It is being wise concerning the skandhas. It is being wise concerning the dhātus. It is being wise concerning the āyatanas. It is making one’s higher cognitions manifest to others.

“It is the elimination of kleśas. It is ceasing engagement with propensities. [n69] It is having specific attainments. [n70] It is the natural result of meditation. [n71]

“It is skillfulness in eliminating transgressions. [n72] It is the prevention of the arising of bad actions. It is the elimination of attachment. [n73]

“It is transcending the existences. It is the memory of previous rebirths. It is being free from doubt concerning the ripening of karma.

“It is the contemplation of phenomena. It is seeking to hear the Dharma. It is having sharp knowledge. It is craving for wisdom. It is the realization of wisdom.

“It is the level of a noble being. [n74] It is having a mind like a mountain. It is being unshakable. It is being immovable. It is the knowledge of the nature of the level of irreversibility.

“It is having the natural result of good qualities. [n75] It is the abhorrence of bad qualities. It is being free of behavior caused by the kleśas. It is never abandoning the training.

“It is being established in samādhi. It is the knowledge of the thoughts of beings. It is the knowledge of the various rebirths of beings. It is knowledge of the infinite. [n76] It is the knowledge of the intended meaning of words. [n77]

“It is the rejection of living in a home. It is finding no joy in the three realms. It is having a motivation that is not discouraged. It is having no attachment to phenomena.

“It is having possession of the sacred Dharma. It is protecting the Dharma. It is conviction in the ripening of karma. It is skill in the vinaya. ^F5a

“It is the pacification of disputes. It is the absence of discord and the absence of quarrels. It is having reached the level of patience. It is maintaining patience.

“It is the equality of the different kinds of beings. [n78] It is skill in examining phenomena. [n79] It is skill in gaining certainty concerning phenomena.

“It is the knowledge of distinguishing between the words for phenomena. [n80] It is skill in the presentation of the words for phenomena. It is the knowledge of the skill of presenting the distinction between words that have meaning and those that do not have meaning. [n81]

“It is knowledge of the past. It is knowledge of the future. It is knowledge of the present. [n82] It is the knowledge of the equality of the three times. It is the knowledge of the purity of the three aspects of actions.

“It is the knowledge of the body’s condition. It is the knowledge of the mind’s condition. It is guarding conduct. It is having unshakable [n83] conduct. It is uncontrived conduct. [n84] It is engaging in conduct that is attractive. [n85]

“It is the knowledge of skill in what is beneficial and what is not beneficial. [n86] It is rational speech. [n87] It is knowledge of the world.

“It is unrestrained generosity. It is being openhanded. [n88] It is having a nongrasping mind.

“It is having a sense of modesty and self-respect. It is an abhorrence of negative aspirations. It is not forsaking the qualities of purification. It is maintaining correct conduct. It is joyful conduct.

“It is standing up to welcome gurus and presenting them with a seat. It is the elimination of pride. It is controlling the mind. It is the knowledge of generating enthusiasm.

“It is the knowledge of discernment. It is the realization of wisdom. It is being without ignorance. It is knowledge of the processes of the mind. It is the knowledge that realizes the nature of the mind. [n89]

“It is the knowledge of accomplishment and definite accomplishment. [n90] It is the knowledge of all language. It is the knowledge of presenting definitions. [n91] It is the knowledge of attaining certainty in meaning.

“It is abandoning that which is harmful. It is attending upon excellent beings. [n92] It is being together with excellent beings. It is avoiding bad beings.

“It is the accomplishment of dhyāna. [n93] It is not savoring [n94] dhyāna.

“It is the utilization [n95] of the higher cognitions. It is the knowledge that comprehends the nature of assigned names and designations. It is overcoming designations. It is disillusionment with saṃsāra. [n96]

“It is the absence of yearning for respect. [n97] It is indifference to lack of respect. [n98] It is not being motivated by material gain. It is not being disheartened when there is no gain. It is the absence of interest in honor. It is the absence of anger at dishonor.  It is the absence of attachment to praise. It is the absence of displeasure in response to criticism. It is the absence of attachment to happiness. It is the absence of aversion to suffering. It is not being acquisitive of composite things. It is having no attachment to renown. It is accepting the lack of renown. [n99] ^F5b

“It is not associating with householders and mendicants. [n100] It is avoiding that which is outside the scope of correct conduct. It is acting within the scope of correct conduct. It is a perfection of correct conduct. It is rejecting incorrect conduct. [n101] It is not dishonoring your family. [n102]

“It is preserving the teaching. It is speaking little. It is speaking softly. [n103] It is speaking slowly. [n104] It is skillfulness in answers. It is defeating opposition. It is arriving at the right time. It is not relying on ordinary people.

“It is not having contempt for those in suffering. It is giving them charity. It is not rebuking [n105] the poor. It is having compassion for those with wrong conduct. It is having that which will bring benefit to others. [n106] It is having a compassionate mind. It is benefiting others through the Dharma. It is giving away material things. It is the absence of hoarding.

“It is praising correct conduct. It is condemning incorrect conduct. It is unwaveringly [n107] attending upon those who have correct conduct. It is giving up all possessions. It is welcoming others [n108] with a higher motivation. It is doing exactly what one has said one will do. It is perpetual application. It is experiencing joy through veneration.

“It is the knowledge of using examples. It is being skilled in terms of past lifetimes. It is putting roots of merit first. It is skill in methods.

“It is the negation of attributes. It is rejecting identification. It is knowledge of the characteristics of things. [n109]

“It is the accomplishment of the sūtras. It is skill in the vinaya. [n110] It is certainty in the truth. It is the direct experience of liberation. It is the single teaching. It is not abandoning correct knowing and seeing. [n111] It is speech free of doubt. [n112]

“It is remaining in emptiness. [n113] It is remaining in the absence of attributes. [n114] It is understanding [n115] the nature of the absence of aspiration. [n116] It is the attainment of fearlessness.

“It is illumination by wisdom. [n117] It is excellent [n118] correct conduct. It is entering into samāpatti. It is the attainment of wisdom. [n119]

“It is delighting in solitude. It is knowledge of oneself. [n120] It is contentment with having no high reputation. [n121] ^F6a

“It is the absence of pollution in the mind. It is rejecting incorrect views. [n122] It is the attainment of mental retention.

“It is the entrance into knowledge. [n123] It is the knowledge of the basis, the ground, the foundation, and the practice. [n124]

It is the cause, [n125] the method, [n126] the way, [n127] the creation, [n128] the doorway, [n129] the path, [n130] the practice, [n131] the guidance, [n132] the explication, [n133] and the conduct of the instruction. [n134]

“It is appropriate patience. [n135] It is the level of patience. [n136] It is being free of impatience. [n137] It is the level of knowledge. It is the elimination of ignorance. It is being established in knowledge.

“It is the level of spiritual practice. [n138] It is the scope of practice of the bodhisattvas.

“It is attending upon wise beings. It is rejecting those who are not wise beings. It is the knowledge that analyzes and realizes the nature of all phenomena. [n139]

“It is the level of buddhahood taught by the tathāgatas. [n140] The wise rejoice in it. The foolish reject it. It is difficult for the śrāvakas to know. The pratyekabuddhas do not know it. It is not the level of the tīrthikas. The bodhisattvas possess it. It is realized by those who have the ten strengths. The devas make offerings to it. Brahmā praises [n141] it. The Śakras [n142] value it above all else. [n143] The nāgas pay homage to it. The yakṣas rejoice in it. The kinnaras praise it in song. The mahoragas laud it. The bodhisattvas meditate on it. The wise comprehend it.

“It is the highest wealth. It is immaterial generosity. It is a medicine for the sick. It is a treasure of wisdom. It is unceasing eloquence.

“It is the way of the sūtras. [n144] It is the domain [n145] of heroes. [n146] It is the comprehension of the entire three realms. It is a raft [n147] for crossing to the other shore. It is like a boat for those in the middle of a river.

“It is fame for those who wish for renown. The buddhas praise it. The tathāgatas laud it. Those who have the ten strengths praise it. ^F6b

“It is the quality of the bodhisattvas. It is the equanimity of those with compassion. It is the love that brings anger [n148] to an end.

“It is the delight of those with peaceful minds. [n149] It provides relief for those who follow the Mahāyāna.

“It is the diligent practice of those with a lion’s roar. It is the path of the wisdom of the buddhas. [n150]

“It is the seal upon all phenomena. It is the accomplishment of omniscient wisdom. [n151]

“It is the pleasure grove of bodhisattvas. It is that which terrifies the māras.

“It is the knowledge of those who have reached happiness. It is the benefit of those who accomplish benefit.

“It is the refuge for those among enemies. It is the subjugation of adversaries by those who have the Dharma.

“It is the expression of truth for those who have fearlessness. It is the correct search for the strengths. It is the omen for the eighteen unique qualities of a buddha. It is the adornment of the Dharma body. [n152] It is the natural result of bodhisattva conduct. [n153] It is the adornment of the bodhisattvas. [n154] It is the delight of those who desire liberation. It is the joy of the eldest sons. [n155]

“It is the completion of buddha wisdom. It is not the level of śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas.

“It is the purity of the mind. It is the purity of the body. It is the completion of the doorways to liberation.

“It is the wisdom of buddhahood’s freedom from the kleśas. [n156] It is the nonarising of desire. [n157] It is devoid of anger.

“It is not the level of ignorance. It is the arising of wisdom. It is the birth of knowledge. It is the elimination of ignorance.

“It is the contentment of those dedicated to liberation. It is the satisfaction of those dedicated to samādhi. It is eyes for those who wish for the view. It is higher knowledge for those who wish to perform miracles. It is miraculous power for those who wish for accomplishment. It is retentive memory for those dedicated to listening to the Dharma. [n158]

“It is unceasing mindfulness. It is the blessing of the buddhas. It is the skillful method of the guides. ^F7a

“It is subtle and difficult to know for those without dedication. [n159] Those who are not liberated cannot know it. [n160] It is beyond words and difficult to know through speech.

“It is known by wise beings. It is the knowledge of gentle beings. [n161] Those with few desires realize it. Those who have unceasing diligence possess it. Those who are mindful maintain it.

“It is the cessation of suffering. It is the birthlessness of all phenomena. It is the single teaching on all existing beings and lifetimes.

“Young man, this is the samādhi called the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena.”

When the Bhagavān gave this teaching of the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, in the past, eighty times a hundred thousand million [n162] devas and humans, who had previously generated the necessary karma, attained the patience of the birthlessness of phenomena, ninety-six times a hundred thousand million attained the corresponding patience, ninety-three times a hundred thousand million obtained the transmission of the teaching of that patience, and the entirety of the hundred thousand [n163] bhikṣus attained liberation of mind through the defilements not arising. Sixty times a hundred thousand devas and human beings became free of desire, without stains, and gained the pure Dharma sight of the Dharmas. Eighty thousand bhikṣuṇīs [n164] attained liberation of mind through the nonarising of defilements. Five hundred upāsakas attained the result of nonreturners. Six thousand upāsikās attained the result of once-returners. This universe of a thousand million worlds shook in six ways: it trembled, it trembled strongly, and it trembled intensely; it quivered, it quivered strongly, and it quivered intensely; it shook, it shook strongly, and it shook intensely; it shuddered, it shuddered strongly, and it shuddered intensely; it quaked, it quaked strongly, and it quaked intensely. The east sank and the west rose,  the west sank and the east rose, the north sank and the south rose, the south sank and the north rose, the perimeter sank and the center rose, and the center sank and the perimeter rose. An immeasurable radiance shone in the universe so that whatever darkness there was between the worlds was illuminated by it. The beings who were born there could see each other and they cried, “Ah! Other beings have been born here too!” This occurred even as far down as the great Avīci hell. ^F7b

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, I remember that in the past, when I was practicing the conduct of a bodhisattva, I became a cakravartin. I desired this samādhi and I desired to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. For many hundred thousand quintillions [n165] of eons on this Vulture Peak Mountain I served, venerated, revered, honored, worshiped, and made offerings to many countless, innumerable tathāgatas, arhats, perfectly enlightened buddhas with the presentation of many hundred thousand quintillions of every kind of jewel, and various kinds of beautiful flowers, incense, perfume, garlands, ointments, powders, parasols, banners, flags, music, musical instruments, flags of victory, and precious monasteries. [n166]

“Young man, I heard from those tathāgatas extensively the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. I obtained it, asked questions about it, preserved it, recited it to others, promoted it, meditated on it with an unadulterated meditation, promulgated it, and made it widely known to others.

“Young man, the last of all those tathāgatas was the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Śālendrarāja.  Young man, that Tathāgata Śālendrarāja had a saṅgha of a thousand trillion [n167] śrāvakas and bodhisattvas. Their lifespans were seven million, six hundred thousand [n168] years. I served and made offerings to the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Śālendrarāja for a hundred and eighty thousand million [n169] years and I built ten million monasteries made of sandalwood and precious materials. The Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Śālendrarāja’s lifespan was seven hundred and sixty thousand million [n170] years. I entered homelessness in the presence of the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Śālendrarāja and for a hundred and forty thousand million [n171] years I listened to the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. I obtained it, asked questions about it, preserved it, recited it to others, promoted it, meditated on it with an unadulterated meditation, promulgated it, and made it widely known to others.” [n172] ^F8a

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, if in that way you wish for this samādhi and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, then you too should dedicate yourself to making offerings to, serving, and being an attendant to all tathāgatas as I have done.

“Young man, why is that? The natural result of making offerings to, serving, and being an attendant to all tathāgatas is that it will not be difficult for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, let alone this samādhi, as their natural result.

“Young man, in that way you should never weary of making offerings to, serving, and being an attendant to all tathāgatas.” ^F8b

Then the Bhagavān taught extensively, as a praise in chanted verses, this chapter on the past lives of the youth Candraprabha:

“I remember  [n173] six hundred million of those who have the ten strengths, [n174]<br>Dwelling on Vulture Peak Mountain in the past<br>Who taught me, when I was practicing bodhisattva conduct, [n175]<br>This supreme peace of samādhi. {1}

“The last of all of them<br>Was the Lord of the World, the illuminator<br>Named Śālendrarāja,<br>And I asked him questions. {2}

“I had become of royal caste.<br>I was the principal king, the sovereign.<br>I had five hundred sons,<br>No less indeed than that. {3}

“For that buddha I built<br>Ten million monasteries<br>Made of special sandalwood,<br>And some of precious materials. {4}

“I was a king named Bhīṣmottara,<br>Beloved and adored by many beings.<br>For a hundred and eighty thousand million years<br>I made excellent offerings to that buddha. {5}

“The lifespan of the guide Śālendrarāja,<br>That jina, irreproachable,<br>Supreme among humans, [n176]<br>Was seven hundred and sixty thousand million years. {6}

“The saṅgha of that supreme man<br>Was composed of eight trillion śrāvakas<br>Who had the three knowledges, the six higher cognitions, and controlled senses,<br>Whose defilements had ceased, and who were in their last body. {7}

“At that time I always [n177] longed for this samādhi<br>In order to benefit the people of the world and the devas,<br>And so I made many kinds of offerings<br>To that [n178] jina, that supreme human. [n179] {8}

“I, with my sons and wives, [n180] entered homelessness<br>In the presence of Jina Śālendrarāja<br>And I asked questions about this samādhi for<br>A hundred and forty thousand million years. {9}

“I acquired from that sugata<br>The single chapter of this samādhi,<br>Which has eight thousand trillion verses<br>And moreover another hundred septillion. [n181] {10}

“Because I longed for this sublime samādhi<br>There was nothing that I had not previously offered:<br>Heads, hands, legs, [n182] wives and likewise sons,<br>An abundance of riches, and similarly food to eat. {11}

“I remember ten thousand million buddhas<br>And more, to the number of sand grains in the Ganges,<br>Residing on Vulture Peak Mountain<br>And teaching this supreme samādhi, this peace. {12} ^F9a

“All of them had the name Śākyaṛṣabha.<br>All of their sons were named Rāhula.<br>All their attendants were named Ānanda.<br>All were mendicants from places named Kapilavastu. [n183] {13}

“Their principal two students [n184] were Kolita and Śāriputra,<br>The names of all the saviors were the same,<br>The names of their worlds were the same,<br>And they all appeared in a time of degeneration. {14}

“While I practiced this bodhisattva conduct,<br>I honored all those lords of men.<br>While I longed for this samādhi,<br>There was nothing I did not offer to the jinas. {15}

“This samādhi is attained through practicing.<br>Its practice has been taught in many forms.<br>This samādhi is not difficult to attain<br>For those who are established in all good qualities. {16}

“This samādhi is not difficult to attain<br>For those who do not grasp pleasures, who have no cravings, [n185]<br>Who have no attachment to family, and are without envy,<br>Who are continually kind, and are without anger. {17}

“This samādhi is not difficult to attain<br>For those who do not desire honor or gain,<br>Whose subsistence is pure, who have nothing,<br>Whose conduct is pure, and who are without fear. {18}

“This samādhi is not difficult to attain<br>For those who are diligent, without lassitude,<br>And who are inclined to solitude, established in purification,<br>And continually remain in the patience of selflessness. {19}

“This samādhi is not difficult to attain<br>For those who are not agitated, who have a well-tamed mind,<br>Who remain within the conduct of mendicants and bodhisattvas, [n186]<br>And who are predisposed toward generosity and are without miserliness. {20}

“The primary and secondary signs, the eighteen qualities of a buddha,<br>The strengths, and the fearlessnesses that have been described by the Guide<br>Will not be difficult to attain for one<br>Who maintains this samādhi of peace. {21}

“If all the beings that a buddha can see<br>Were simultaneously to attain buddhahood,<br>And the length of each of their lives<br>Were to be countless tens of thousands of millions of eons, {22}

“And if each of them were to have heads<br>As numerous as the grains of sand in the ocean,<br>And if within each head there were tongues<br>As numerous as the number of heads, {23} ^F9b

“And if all their voices were to describe the benefit<br>Of possessing one verse from this samādhi,<br>They would not be able to describe even a fraction of it,<br>Let alone describe the benefit of studying it, or of possessing it. {24}

“Whoever has accomplished the practice and developed qualities<br>Will be adored by devas, asuras, and yakṣas.<br>The ones who maintain the samādhi of peace, difficult to attain,<br>Will have kings as their attendants. {25}

“The ones who maintain the samādhi of peace that is difficult to attain<br>Will be in the care of the jinas.<br>They will always be attended by devas and nāgas<br>And opponents will not be able to withstand their brilliance. {26}

“The ones who maintain the samādhi of peace<br>Will have infinite eloquence. [n187]<br>They will teach countless [n188] thousands of sūtras<br>Without the slightest interval. {27}

“Those in the future time of great terrors<br>Who hear this samādhi and keep it<br>Will see the guide, Buddha Amitābha,<br>And also the realm of Sukhāvatī. {28}

“I have revealed these benefits<br>And I, the self-arisen Teacher, request<br>That you uphold this pure samādhi<br>In the time after I have passed into nirvāṇa. {29}

“The buddhas who have passed into nirvāṇa,<br>Those who will come in the future and those who have appeared now, [n189]<br>All those jinas realize unstained, noncomposite enlightenment<br>Through the practice of this samādhi.” {30}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, therefore, if bodhisattva mahāsattvas wish to teach the buddha qualities as described by the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha, without any loss of meaning or words, and for all their words to come forth as those of the Buddha, then those bodhisattva mahāsattvas, young man,  should, for the sake of all beings, obtain [n190] this samādhi, understand [n191] it, preserve it, [n192] recite it to others, [n193] promote it, [n194] proclaim it, [n195] chant it, [n196] meditate on it with unadulterated [n197] meditation, promulgate it, [n198] and make it widely known to others. [n199] ^F10a

“Young man, what are the buddha qualities of a tathāgata?

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas, whether in solitude, at the foot of a tree, in the open air, or in an empty building, should learn well the following.

“The Bhagavān is thus: a tathāgata, an arhat, a fully enlightened buddha, one with perfect wisdom and conduct, [n200] a sugata, one who knows the world’s beings, an unsurpassable guide who tames beings, a teacher of devas and humans, a buddha, a bhagavān.

“The Tathāgata is the natural result of merit. He is the inevitable result of roots of merit. He is adorned by patience. He is the manifestation [n201] of a treasure of merit. He is beautified by the excellent primary signs of a great being. He has the blossomed [n202] flowers of the secondary signs of a great being. He is exemplary in his conduct. His appearance is never disagreeable. He brings joy to those motivated by faith. He is invincible in his wisdom. He has the invulnerability of the strengths. He is the teacher of all beings. He is the father of all bodhisattvas. He is the king of all noble individuals. He is the caravan leader for those beginning on their journey. He is immeasurable in his wisdom. He is inconceivable [n203] in his eloquence. He is pure in his voice. He is delightful in his speech. He is lovely in his physical form. He is unequaled in body. He is unstained by the desire realm. He is unsullied by the form realm. He is unadulterated by the formless realm. He is free from suffering. [n204] He is liberated from the skandhas. He is separated from the dhātus. He has restrained [n205] the āyatanas. He has cut through the knots. [n206] He is free from torment. [n207] He is released from craving. [n208] He has crossed over the great river. He is complete in his wisdom. He is established in the wisdom of the buddha bhagavāns of the past, future, and present. He does not remain in nirvāṇa. He resides at the summit of existence. He is on the level of seeing all beings. Young man, those are the buddha qualities of a tathāgata.  [n209] ^F10b

“If bodhisattva mahāsattvas who possess these buddha qualities and their praise, [n210] and who have continuous confidence of speech based upon this samādhi, teach correctly the buddha qualities and praises of the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha, there will be no loss of meaning or words and all their words will come forth as those of the Buddha.”

Then at that time the Bhagavān, in order to make the meaning clear, gave a detailed teaching by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha. [n211]

“It would not be easy to recite all the praises of the jinas<br>Even if one were to speak for many thousands of eons;<br>And the jinas attained their qualities<br>Through seeking this supreme samādhi of peace. {1}

“In the past, when I sought this supreme samādhi of peace<br>With a mind that was indefatigable,<br>I gave away a maiden adorned in jewelry,<br>Who was perfectly beautiful and desirable. {2}

“In the past, when I sought this supreme samādhi of peace<br>With a mind that was indefatigable,<br>I gave away male and female servants, riches and grain,<br>And also jewels, pearls, gold, and silver. {3}

“When I sought this supreme samādhi of peace<br>In the past, I gave to the guides<br>Various kinds of precious jewels, strings of pearls,<br>Beautiful clothes, and necklaces of conch and gold. {4}

“In countless, endless millions [n212] of eons<br>I developed the highest supreme aspiration,<br>And gave the best of perfumes and summer flowers<br>To the caityas of the jinas. {5} ^F11a

“Through my giving the gift of the Dharma [n213]<br>I developed a pleasing following;<br>But the thought did not arise in my mind<br>Of gaining renown through giving the gift of the Dharma. {6}

“I never felt any reluctance to give away<br>The loveliest things that gave me pleasure.<br>I gave the gift of Dharma numerous times, [n214]<br>And always my thoughts were of attaining buddha wisdom. [n215] {7}

“In the past, to attain the qualities of this training,<br>I remained always in excellent, quiet forests.<br>I had immense compassion throughout that time<br>And always my thoughts were of attaining buddha wisdom. {8}

“I had a distinct conduct [n216] that was gentle and sweet,<br>A smiling face, the memory of what I had heard, and affectionate speech.<br>My very sweet words were beloved by many<br>And all beings never had enough of looking at me. {9}

“I did not have any stinginess [n217] for even a moment.<br>Throughout myriad existences I had no envy. [n218]<br>I was always completely satisfied by alms.<br>I offered [n219] everything and left no remainder. {10}

“Those who remember just one four-line verse from this<br>Become very learned and remember all they have heard.<br>Through it the highest, perfect faith [n220] arose in me<br>And I always honored it. {11}

“I longed for the supreme peace of this samādhi<br>And made many offerings to the guides.<br>I gave to them an endless variety of gifts<br>And this maintained my correct conduct for a long time. [n221] {12}

“From remembering one verse from this samādhi<br>The merit will be vastly greater<br>Than from endlessly offering numerous, various worlds<br>That are all filled with precious jewels. {13}

“If those wishing for merit<br>Were to offer to the jinas [n222]<br>Whatever flowers and incense exist<br>For numerous, countless, endless eons, {14}

“And if those wishing for merit<br>Were to offer to the jinas<br>Every kind of music, light, food, and clothing<br>For numerous, countless, endless eons, {15}

“A person who develops the aspiration to enlightenment,<br>Wishing to become a self-arisen jina, a lord of Dharma,<br>Will have merit that will be vastly greater<br>Through remembering one verse of this meditation. [n223] {16} ^F11b

“The merit from possessing this samādhi is most vast.<br>One would not be able to conclude reciting<br>The description of its benefits even in as many eons<br>As there are grains of sand in the Ganges. [n224] {17}

“Therefore, having listened to<br>The excellent benefits of the buddhas,<br>You should quickly be one who has the transmission [n225]<br>Of this samādhi praised by the Buddha. {18}

“In my past lives I have honored<br>Seven hundred and thirty million buddhas.<br>All of those buddhas<br>Promulgated this sūtra. {19}

“The name of this sūtra<br>Is Entering Great Compassion.  [n226]<br>Buddha qualities will not be hard to attain<br>For the learned one who trains in it. {20}

“When the World’s Guide is in nirvāṇa,<br>In that future time there will be<br>Many undisciplined bhikṣus<br>Who have no interest in becoming learned. {21}

“They will utter praises of correct conduct<br>But will have no interest in correct conduct.<br>They will utter praises of samādhi<br>But will have no interest in samādhi. {22}

“They will utter praises of wisdom<br>But will have no interest in wisdom.<br>They will utter praises of liberation<br>But will have no interest in liberation. {23}

“It is like when someone<br>Speaks of the qualities of sandalwood,<br>Saying, ‘Sandalwood is like this,<br>It makes a pleasing incense.’ [n227] {24}

“Then another person asks<br>That man this question:<br>‘Do you have some of the sandalwood<br>That you have been praising?’ [n228] {25}

“The man answers him,<br>‘I speak the praises of that incense<br>And in that way make my living,<br>But I have never seen that incense.’ [n229] {26}

“In such a way, in future times<br>There will be those who have no correct conduct, [n230]<br>Yet they who do not engage in it<br>Will make their living by praising it. {27}

“In that way, in future times<br>There will be those who have no samādhi, [n231]<br>Yet they who do not engage in it<br>Will make their living by praising it. {28}

“In that way, in future times<br>There will be those who have no wisdom, [n232]<br>Yet they who do not engage in it<br>Will make their living by praising it. [n233] {29} ^F12a

“In that way, in future times<br>There will be those who have no liberation, [n234]<br>Yet they who do not engage in it<br>Will make their living by praising it. {30}

“When a certain poor person,<br>Despised by the populace,<br>Later finds a treasure<br>And becomes rich, he is respected by the people. {31}

“In that same way, not having attained the samādhi,<br>A bodhisattva is not esteemed<br>By gods [n235] or humans, kumbhāṇḍas or rākṣasas,<br>Just like the poor person who has no wealth. [n236] {32}

“Yet when the wise one attains the level<br>Of the unfathomable [n237] Dharma treasure, [n238]<br>Gods and humans will be attracted to him,<br>And he will give those beings the supreme wealth. {33}

“Therefore, having heard the Jina’s description<br>Of the perfect attainment of those benefits,<br>Forsake all happiness gained through reputation<br>And hold the transmission of this supreme peace of samādhi. {34}

“The buddhas in all directions who have passed away,<br>And those of the future, and those who are present,<br>All attain unequaled, inconceivable enlightenment<br>Through having trained in this samādhi.” {35}

The youth Candraprabha was overjoyed,<br>And in the presence of the Buddha he said these words:<br>“When the best of beings has passed into nirvāṇa,<br>I will uphold this sūtra in that very difficult time. [n239] {36}

“I will give up my body and my life<br>And whatever happiness [n240] there is in the world;<br>In that time of great terrors<br>I will hold this samādhi of supreme peace. {37}

“I will have compassion for many beings.<br>I will see beings suffering without a protector.<br>I will be endowed with love for them<br>And will uphold this supreme peace, this samādhi.” {38}

At that time, no less than five hundred people<br>Became holders of the samādhi.<br>The youth was their leader [n241]<br>In this vast holding of the supreme sūtra. {39}

Then the youth Candraprabha  rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee with palms placed together, he bowed toward the Bhagavān and made this request: “If the Bhagavān will give me an opportunity to seek answers to them, I have a few questions for the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.” ^F12b

The Bhagavān addressed the youth Candraprabha, saying, “Young man, the Tathāgata will always give you that opportunity. Ask whatever question you wish of the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.”

As the Bhagavān had given him the opportunity, the young man Candraprabha asked the Bhagavān, [n242] “The Bhagavān says, ‘samādhi, samādhi.’ What kind of Dharma does this word designate?”

The Bhagavān replied to Candraprabha, “Young man, when I say ‘samādhi, samādhi,’ it means the profound realization of the mind.

“[1] It is the absence of arising. [n243] [2] It is the absence of continuation. [n244] [3] It is the knowledge of continuation. [n245] [4] It is putting down [n246] the burden. [n247] [5] It is the wisdom of the tathāgatas. [6] It is having the preeminence of a buddha. [7] It is the healing of desire, the pacifying of anger, [n248] and the elimination of ignorance.  [n249]

“[8] It is engaging in what should be engaged in. [9] It is rejecting that which should not be engaged in. [10] It is the aspiration to good qualities. [n250] [11] It is the wish to be free from saṃsāra.

“[12] It is practicing with a higher motivation. [13] It is remaining awake. [n251] [14] It is not abandoning renunciation. [n252] [15] It is maintaining good qualities.

“[16] It is not relying on rebirth. [n253] [17] It is not accumulating karma. [18] It is not paying attention to the internal āyatanas. [n254] [19] It is not engaging with the external āyatanas.

“[20] It is not praising oneself. [21] It is not criticizing others. [22] It is having no attachment to family. [23] It is not placing one’s trust in ordinary people.  [n255]

“[24] It is the natural result of correct conduct.  [25] It is that which is difficult to approach. [26] It is great majesty. [n256] [27] It is self-knowledge. ^F13a

“[28] It is the absence of inconstancy. [29] It is maintaining perfect behavior. [30] It is the absence of malice. [31] It is the absence of aggression. [32] It is not harming others. [33] It is taking care of companions.  [n257] [34] It is guarding secret mantras.

“[35] It is being nonviolent. [n258] [36] It is not being harmful to those with correct conduct. [37] It is speaking gently.

“[38] It is not remaining anywhere in the three realms. [39] It is the patience that accords with the emptiness of all phenomena. [n259] [40] It is the aspiration to omniscient wisdom. [n260]

“That, young man, is what is meant by ‘samādhi.’ Young man, practicing those qualities and not practicing their opposite is what is meant by ‘samādhi.’ ”

Then the Bhagavān taught the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, and at that time gave a detailed teaching by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha. [n261]

“I have opened the door to the elixir.<br>I have explained what the nature of phenomena is.<br>I have taught what births are.<br>I have explained nirvāṇa and its benefits. {1}

“Always avoid sinful companions,<br>Be in the company of good companions,<br>Dwell in the forest, avoiding crowds,<br>And always meditate with a loving mind. {2}

“Always protect pure conduct,<br>Gain the prosperity of renunciation,<br>Be familiar with generosity and wisdom,<br>And this samādhi will not be difficult to attain. {3}

“This is not the level of the numerous śrāvakas.<br>When you have attained [n262] this level of peace,<br>You will have the direct perception of the Sugata’s Dharma<br>And you will attain the inconceivable buddha qualities. {4}

“When you see wise people who are worthy vessels,<br>Bring them to the aspiration for enlightenment,<br>Establish them in the highest knowledge,<br>And then this king of samādhis will not be difficult to attain. {5}

“This samādhi is not difficult to attain<br>For those who understand the natural results<br>That come [n263] to those who become envious of wealth [n264]<br>And to those who seek and enjoy it. [n265] {6} ^F13b

“The meditation of this king of samādhis, emptiness,<br>Is at the summit of pure conduct.<br>The continuous meditation on the nature of phenomena<br>Is unknown to the foolish who practice incorrectly. {7}

“Those who long for this samādhi of peace<br>Will never have fear arise in their mind. [n266]<br>Those who are on this level of peace<br>Will always see the supreme men. [n267] {8}

“Whoever brings to mind the image of the Tathāgata’s body,<br>Their senses will be at peace and their mind at peace.<br>Their minds, free of error, will always be at rest.<br>What they have heard and what they know will be like an ocean. {9}

“Remaining in this samādhi,<br>Wherever the bodhisattvas tread<br>They will see ten thousand million buddhas<br>And even more, as numerous as the Ganges sands. {10}

“Anyone aiming to take the measure<br>Of the Buddha’s Dharma will go insane.<br>One cannot measure that which is immeasurable;<br>The qualities of the guides in their entirety are inconceivable. {11}

“There is no being in the ten directions<br>Who can equal the Lord of the World, let alone be greater.<br>You should long for and attain the wisdom of the buddhas,<br>Who possess all the qualities of omniscience. {12}

“The Lord of the World is completely beautiful,<br>With a body that is the color of gold.<br>Bodhisattvas will rest in meditation<br>When their mind is focused upon that image. {13}

“The wise who understand the composite and noncomposite [n268]<br>Have ceased conceptualizing attributes. [n269]<br>They remain in that meditation of the absence of attributes<br>And know the emptiness of all phenomena. {14}

“Those who remain in the dharmakāya<br>Know that all things are nothing.<br>Those who have ceased conceptualizing things [n270]<br>Do not see the Lord of Jinas as a rūpakāya. {15}

“I proclaim to you and make it known to you<br>That to the extent that a person contemplates this,<br>To that extent their mind will be fixed upon it,<br>Through that contemplation that dwells upon it. {16}

“Those who remember in that way the appearance<br>And immeasurable wisdom of the Lord of Sages,<br>They will have their mind completely focused upon him<br>Through constant meditation on that recollection. {17} ^F14a

“When walking, sitting, or standing,<br>They desire the wisdom of the best of beings,<br>And pray for enlightenment, wishing to become<br>A jina who is unsurpassable in this world. {18}

“They will know the buddhas and see the buddhas;<br>They will realize the nature of the buddhas.<br>Remaining in this samādhi,<br>They will pay homage to the buddhas who have great might. [n271] {19}

“With serene body, speech, and mind,<br>They constantly recite praises to the buddhas.<br>In that way, through the mind’s continuum of meditation,<br>Day and night they see the Lord of the World. {20}

“When the time comes that they are sick and unwell<br>And experience the suffering of dying,<br>They will not lose their recollection of the Buddha,<br>And it will not be stolen away by the experience of suffering. [n272] {21}

“Having analyzed with wisdom in that way,<br>They know all present, past, and future phenomena [n273] to be empty.<br>They remain in that nature of phenomena<br>And perform bodhisattva conduct without being disheartened. {22}

“Therefore, having heard these benefits,<br>You should long for unequaled enlightenment.<br>It is difficult to see the sublime Sugata,<br>So do not have cause for regret in the future. {23}

“I have taught this excellent Dharma<br>But if you do not practice it well<br>You will be like a sick man holding a bag [n274] of medicine—<br>That alone will not cure his illness. [n275] {24}

“Therefore, the wise and the realized<br>Are always aspiring to this samādhi.<br>And if they practice correct conduct, learning, and generosity<br>It will not be difficult for them to attain this samādhi.” {25}

Then the Bhagavān again addressed the youth Candraprabha, saying, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should think that they are like someone whose hair and clothes are on fire, and they should cast off father, mother,  son, daughter, family, kinsmen, relatives, kindred, wife, and so on, as if they were fire, throw away all the pleasures of a kingdom as if they were a lump of phlegm, turn toward solitude, and depart from home. ^F14b

“Why is that? Young man, attaining the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood will not be difficult for a bodhisattva mahāsattva who turns toward solitude and departs from home, let alone one who has this samādhi.

“Therefore, young man, you should always train in having this thought: ‘I shall cast off friends, children, family, kinsmen, relatives, kindred, wife, and so on, as if they were fire, throw away all the pleasures of a kingdom as if they were a lump of phlegm, turn toward solitude, and depart from home.’

“Therefore, young man, you should understand this through the following teaching, too: [n276]

“Young man, in the past, countless, vast, immeasurable, inconceivable, innumerable, asaṃkhyeya eons ago, [n277] at that time and in those days, [n278] there appeared in the world the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, who was perfect in wisdom and conduct, a sugata, a knower of the world, an unsurpassable guide who tamed beings, a teacher of devas and humans, a buddha, and a bhagavān.

“Young man, at that time and in those days, in the first assembly of the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta’s śrāvakas, there were eight hundred million who were arhats. In the second assembly there were seven hundred million arhats. In the third assembly of śrāvakas there were six hundred million arhats.  There were also countless bodhisattva mahāsattvas who possessed the Dharma. ^F15a

“Young man, at that time and in those days, during the time of the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, the lifespan was forty thousand years. This Jambudvīpa continent had wealth, increase, happiness, excellent harvests, joy, and was filled with a great multitude of human beings.

“In this Jambudvīpa there were two kings named Dṛḍhabala and Mahābala. One ruled the half of Jambudvīpa that had wealth, increase, happiness, excellent harvests, joy, and was filled with a great multitude of human beings. The other ruled the other half.

“Young man, at that time, the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta appeared in the kingdom of King Mahābala.

“Young man, for a hundred thousand years King Mahābala provided the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, the saṅgha of bodhisattvas, and the saṅgha of bhikṣus with faultless, proper clothing, alms, medicine if they were ill, and monastic utensils for their use.

“Young man, at that time, the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, the saṅgha of bodhisattvas, and the saṅgha of bhikṣus received greatly renowned gifts and honors.

“Brahmins and householders who had faith also bestowed great gifts and honors on the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, the saṅgha of bodhisattvas, and the saṅgha of bhikṣus.

“Those brahmins and householders did this by following the example of King Mahābala,  dedicating themselves to bestowing great gifts and honors by making offerings of worldly material goods to the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, the saṅgha of bodhisattvas, and the saṅgha of bhikṣus. ^F15b

“Young man, the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta thought, ‘Alas! These beings who have adopted correct conduct and the poṣadha vows have come before the Tathāgata, have honored the Tathāgata, practice celibacy, have entered the homeless life, and have become fully ordained bhikṣus—they will go into decline. They are concerned about the happiness of their future lives.

“ ‘Why is that? It is because in their future lives their happiness will be from these offerings of worldly material things. The realms of the higher existences are the goal of these beings. They are concerned with this life. They are concerned with their  [n279] next life. They do not accumulate [n280] roots of merit for the final ultimate goal.’ [n281]

“Young man, what are the roots of merit for the ultimate goal? They are pure conduct and celibacy going toward the ultimate goal and reaching the ultimate goal.

“Bhagavān Ghoṣadatta thought, ‘I must teach those beings the Dharma so that they will make the unsurpassable offering of the Dharma and the practice of the Dharma as their offering to the Tathāgata.’ [n282]

“Then, young man, at that time the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, with the intention of creating revulsion toward saṃsāra, [n283] recited these verses to King Mahābala, the brahmins, and the laypeople:

“ ‘The service of someone making a gift to another<br>Is not a cause for holding each other in high esteem.<br>The wise ones who are free of negative propensities,<br>The buddhas, they do not praise that service. {1}

“ ‘Those who teach the Dharma for the benefit of beings,<br>They are those who accomplish great service.<br>Then there will form an unbreakable bond of friendship,<br>Which not even ten million māras will be able to break. {2} ^F16a

“ ‘The service of those who keep to worldly material things<br>Will all be for the benefit of the present life.<br>The immaterial service of the Dharma<br>Leads to the greatest benefit for humans. {3}

“ ‘Those who have a nonmaterialistic motivation<br>And teach the nonmaterial Dharma,<br>Those individuals who gain nonmaterial joy,<br>They will quickly attain buddhahood. {4}

“ ‘Those who are addicted to their desires,<br>Who crave for children and wives,<br>Who are addicted to their revolting homes,<br>Will not attain unsurpassable, highest enlightenment. {5}

“ ‘Supreme enlightenment will not be difficult to attain<br>For those who avoid desire as if it were a pit of fire,<br>Who abandon craving for children and wives,<br>And, frightened and terrified, leave their homes. {6}

“ ‘There have been no buddhas in the past,<br>Nor will there be any in the future or now in the present,<br>Who attain the highest, most supreme enlightenment<br>While living inside their homes. {7}

“ ‘Casting away a kingdom like a lump of phlegm,<br>Longing for solitude and living in the forests,<br>Eliminating the kleśas and defeating the māras,<br>They will realize stainless, noncomposite enlightenment. {8}

“ ‘People who, with a disenchanted mind,<br>Leave their homes, they are superior<br>To those who serve, for many millions of eons,<br>Heroic buddhas as numerous as the Ganges sands. {9}

“ ‘People who leave their homes and practice the Dharma,<br>Without serving the supreme humans, the jinas,<br>With food, drink, and Dharma robes,<br>With flowers, incense, and ointments— {10}

“ ‘Those who, longing for enlightenment,<br>Disillusioned with the composite, and for the benefit of beings,<br>Take seven steps in the direction of the forests—<br>They will have the superior merit.’ {11}

“Young man, King Mahābala heard what the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta said about leaving one’s home. Having heard this, he thought, ‘I have understood the Bhagavān’s teaching to mean that he does not praise the perfection of generosity,  but gives the highest, ultimate praise to the perfection of conduct. [n284] The Bhagavān has praised perfect purity, perfect celibacy, and perfect nirvāṇa.’ ^F16b

“He thought, ‘It is not easy to practice the unsurpassable Dharma and attain its goal while living in a home. I would decline in my practice of the unsurpassable Dharma. I shall cut off my hair and beard, wear the orange robes, and leave home for homelessness.’

“Then, young man, King Mahābala, accompanied by eighty thousand [n285] brahmins and laypeople, came before the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, bowed down to his feet, circumambulated the Bhagavān three times, and sat to one side.

“Young man, the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha, knowing the higher motivation of King Mahābala, taught this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena.

“Young man, on hearing this, King Mahābala was pleased, delighted, joyful, inspired, and happy. He shaved off his hair and beard, put on the orange robes, and with faith left home for homelessness. Having entered homelessness he learned this samādhi, and having learned it he understood it. He dedicated himself to the practice of keeping it, reading it, and meditating on it. Through that root of merit, he did not fall into the lower existences for a hundred million eons. He served two hundred million buddhas and heard this samādhi from all those tathāgatas. He learned this samādhi, and having learned it he understood it.  He dedicated himself to the practice of keeping it, reading it, and meditating on it. ^F17a

“Subsequently, through those roots of merit, after a hundred million eons had passed, and then another hundred thousand eons, he attained the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. He became the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha named Jñānaśūra. [n286] He benefited countless beings, and afterward he passed away into perfect nirvāṇa.

“Young man, the eighty thousand people who with King Mahābala came into the presence of the Bhagavān, the Tathāgata Ghoṣadatta all heard this samādhi also and were delighted, rejoicing, and joyful. Happy and joyful, they cut off their hair and beards, wore the orange robes, and with genuine faith they left home for homelessness. Having entered homelessness they learned this samādhi, and having learned it they understood it. They dedicated themselves to the practice of keeping it, reading it, and meditating on it. Through that root of merit, they did not fall into the lower existences for a hundred million eons. During all those eons, they served ten million buddhas and heard this samādhi from all those tathāgatas. They maintained this samādhi and comprehended it. They dedicated themselves to the practice of keeping it, reading it, and meditating on it.

“Through their previous roots of merit, after two hundred million eons had passed and a further hundred thousand eons, they attained the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. They all became bhagavāns, tathāgatas, arhats, perfectly enlightened buddhas named Dṛḍhaśūra. They benefited countless beings, and afterward they passed away into perfect nirvāṇa. ^F17b

“Therefore, young man, because of this teaching, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas cherish in this way this samādhi. They know that it is composed of the unsurpassable wisdom of omniscience.”

Then, at that time, the Bhagavān gave a detailed teaching by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha.

“I remember, countless eons ago<br>In the past, a supreme human, a great sage<br>Who benefited beings appeared in the world,<br>And he was known by the name Ghoṣadatta. {12}

“The first assembly of his students<br>Numbered eight hundred million. [n287]<br>The second was seven hundred million.<br>The third was six hundred million arhats. {13}

“All had eliminated defilements and were without kleśas.<br>All had attained the perfection of miraculous powers.<br>The lifespan was forty thousand years<br>And the realm was perfectly pure and beautiful. {14}

“The bodhisattvas of that protector<br>Were consecrated to immeasurably benefit others.<br>They were well established through their powers and levels.<br>They were near to buddhahood beneath the sacred tree. [n288] {15}

“In this Jambudvīpa there were kings<br>Named Dṛḍhabala and Mahābala.<br>One king ruled half the world,<br>The other was king over the other half. {16}

“The Buddha, to whom humans and devas made offerings,<br>Had appeared within the domain of King Mahābala.<br>The king gained faith in the Sugata<br>And attended him for a thousand years. {17}

“Many other beings, following his example,<br>Also honored the Tathāgata<br>With worldly goods and not through the Dharma. [n289]<br>They gave many things to the śrāvakas also. {18}

“The highest of beings had this thought:<br>‘I shall teach the Dharma to these who desire the Dharma<br>So that they will all give up desire<br>And enter into homelessness in my teaching.’ {19}

“The highest of humans taught in verses<br>The practice of following the Dharma of the sugatas,<br>The endless suffering and harm of living in a home,<br>And that practicing the Dharma is offering to the Dharma. {20} ^F18a

“When the king, the sovereign, had heard those verses,<br>That ruler of men contemplated entering solitude.<br>He thought that all who dwell at home<br>Are unable to make the supreme offering to the Dharma. {21}

“He cast away the kingdom like a lump of phlegm<br>And together with eighty thousand persons<br>He came into the presence of the Jina,<br>Bowed to his feet, and sat before him. {22}

“The Jina, knowing what they intended,<br>Taught this samādhi of peace that is difficult to see.<br>Happy, inspired, and joyful, they were satisfied.<br>Pleased and delighted, they entered homelessness. {23}

“Homeless, they possessed this samādhi.<br>They kept it, read it, and understood it.<br>For two hundred million eons<br>They did not fall into the lower existences. {24}

“Because of those roots of merit, [n290]<br>They all saw ten thousand million buddhas<br>And in the teaching of those jinas<br>They entered homelessness and meditated on this samādhi. {25}

“In later times they became buddhas<br>With infinite diligence, all named Dṛḍhaśūra.<br>They benefited many millions of beings<br>And after, like an extinguished flame, attained nirvāṇa. {26}

“The one who previously had been King Mahābala<br>Appeared in the world as Buddha Jñānaśūra.<br>He brought many billions of beings<br>To enlightenment, and then attained nirvāṇa. {27}

“Therefore you who, in later times, hear and possess<br>This sūtra that has been taught by the buddhas:<br>If you possess this treasure of the Dharma<br>You will quickly become a supreme human.” {28}

The Bhagavān now said to the youth Candraprabha, [n291] “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should cultivate this samādhi.

“Young man, what is the cultivation of this samādhi?  Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas with a compassionate mind are dedicated to making offerings to the tathāgatas, whether living or passed into nirvāṇa, of Dharma robes, alms, seat and bedding, medicines for when ill, and of monastic utensils, and of flowers, incense, perfume, garlands, ointments, aromatic powders, clothing, parasols, banners, and flags, and of music and musical instruments. They dedicate that root of merit to the attainment of samādhi. They do not make offerings to a tathāgata with the hope for anything at all—not with the hope for anything they desire, nor with the hope for any enjoyment, nor with the hope for a higher existence, nor with the hope for followers—but do so with the Dharma in mind. They do not even, with that wish, perceive the Tathāgata as the dharmakāya, let alone perceiving him as the rūpakāya. ^F18b

“Young man, it is in that way that an offering is made to the tathāgatas. It is done without seeing the tathāgatas, without focusing on the self, and without any desire for the ripening of karma. Young man, if an offering made to a tathāgata is purified of those three aspects of the action, this samādhi will be attained and the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood will be quickly reached.”

At this point the Bhagavān gave a detailed teaching on the cultivation of the samādhi by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha.

“Through offering incense to infinite wisdom<br>Beings will have an infinite aroma.<br>In ten million eons they will not go to the lower realms,<br>And no bad smells will come from them. {1}

“For ten million eons they will practice bodhisattva conduct<br>And make offerings to ten thousand million buddhas.<br>The aroma of wisdom will arise so that they<br>Will become buddhas with the aroma of supreme conduct. {2}

“If any beings know that the incense they offer,<br>Those to whom they offer it,<br>And the minds that offer incense  do not exist,<br>The ‘concordant patience’ they have is of lesser kind. {3} ^F19a

“But if a person maintains a patience that is great, [n292]<br>Even were they cut up, for ten million eons,<br>Into tiny pieces as numerous as the Ganges sands,<br>Their mind will never regress. {4}

“Why is this termed ‘patience’?<br>And why is it called ‘concordant’?<br>For what reason is it said to be ‘nonregressive’?<br>And why are they called ‘bodhisattvas’? {5}

“Their patience being for the selfless nature of phenomena,<br>Those who perceive selflessness have no kleśas.<br>They know that all phenomena are like space.<br>That, therefore, is what is termed ‘patience.’ {6}

“They train in accord with all the jinas.<br>Those wise ones do not practice non-Dharma.<br>They do not doubt the Buddha’s Dharma.<br>That is the patience that is ‘concordant.’ {7}

“Even if all the māras in the world transformed<br>Into buddhas and said to such practitioners,<br>‘Enlightenment is too difficult! So become a śrāvaka!’<br>They would not believe those words and would not regress. {8}

“If they know of the incorrect view of beings<br>They say, ‘This is not the path to deathlessness!’ [n293]<br>So that they reject the wrong path and are brought to the true path. [n294]<br>That is the reason why they are called bodhisattvas. [n295] {9}

“They remain upon the path of concordant patience<br>And are awake through the knowledge of selflessness.<br>Even in a dream they do not believe<br>In humans, persons, souls, or beings. {10}

“Even if as many millions of māras as there are Ganges sands<br>Came before them in the forms of buddhas,<br>And said to them that there is a soul within the body,<br>They would reply that it was not so and say, ‘You are not buddhas.’ [n296] {11}

“Through wisdom I know that the skandhas are empty.<br>Because I know that, I am unaccompanied by kleśas.<br>In my conduct I use mere words<br>But within this world remain within nirvāṇa, {12}

“Just as when a man has a son born to him<br>And gives him a name, saying, ‘This is his name!’<br>But that name cannot be found anywhere.<br>And that name did not come from anywhere. {13}

“In that way the name ‘bodhisattva’ is given,<br>But if one seeks for this ‘bodhisattva’<br>That name will not be found anywhere.<br>One who knows that is a bodhisattva. {14} ^F19b

“The bodhisattvas do not believe in the existence of a self<br>Any more than that a fire can burn in the middle of the ocean.<br>Since they have developed the aspiration for enlightenment<br>They have not had the view that there is a soul within. [n297] {15}

“There is no birth and there is no death<br>For beings, humans, [n298] the descendants of Manu.<br>Phenomena have an empty nature, like illusions;<br>The tīrthikas are unable to know that. {16}

“Also those who crave for food,<br>Who desire and cling to alms bowls and robes,<br>Who are arrogant and are haughty,<br>They cannot understand the Buddha’s enlightenment. {17}

“The lazy who are overcome by sleepiness and dullness,<br>Who have stubborn minds, [n299] and are shameless,<br>Who have no faith in the Buddha,<br>They are unable to understand [n300] sublime enlightenment. {18}

“The ordinary beings with incorrect behavior,<br>Those who do not have faith in the Dharma,<br>Who have no respect toward celibates,<br>They are unable to understand enlightenment. {19}

“Those with correct behavior, who have modesty and self-respect,<br>Who delight in the Dharma and the buddhas,<br>Who show great respect to the practitioners of celibacy,<br>They will attain the supreme, highest enlightenment. {20}

“Those whose conduct is performed with mindfulness,<br>Who sit upon their cushion with joy and delight,<br>With dhyāna as food and samādhi for drink,<br>They will attain the supreme, highest enlightenment. {21}

“Those who understand selflessness all day long,<br>Who are mindful of emptiness as they walk,<br>Who bear the beautiful aromatic flowers of the aspects of enlightenment,<br>Those dedicated ones will attain supreme enlightenment. {22}

“They who are skilled in bodhisattva conduct<br>Are not on the level of other beings,<br>Of śrāvakas, or of pratyekabuddhas.<br>Who would not aspire to that realization? {23}

“If I were to have a lifespan that continued<br>For as many millions of eons as there are sands in the Ganges,<br>I would not even be able to finish reciting the praises<br>Of as little of the Buddha’s wisdom as a tiny pore. {24}

“Therefore, having heard the benefits<br>That have been taught by the unsurpassable Jina,<br>You should quickly become instructed in this samādhi.<br>And then the attainment of supreme enlightenment will not be difficult.” {25} ^F20a

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should become skilled in the wisdoms of the three kinds of patience. They should know the first patience. They should know the second patience. They should know the third patience. They should become skilled in the differences between the three kinds of patience and skilled in the differences between the wisdoms of the three kinds of patience.

“Why is that? Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas become skilled in the differences between the three kinds of patience and become skilled in the differences between the wisdoms of the three kinds of patience, then at that time, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas will quickly attain this samādhi, and will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.

“Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood should learn this Dharma teaching on gaining the three kinds of patience. When they have learned it they should teach it widely to others. That will be of benefit to many beings, it will bring happiness to many beings, it will be a kindness to the world, it will bring fulfillment to a multitude of beings, and bring benefit and happiness to humans and devas.” [n301]

Then the Bhagavān taught this Dharma discourse on gaining the three kinds of patience by chanting the following verses to the youth Candraprabha.

“Those who do not argue<br>Or speak unbeneficial words<br>But always bring benefit and maintain the Dharma,<br>Such people are explained as having the first patience. {1} ^F20b

“Knowing that all phenomena are like illusions,<br>Not having a conceptual field of experience,<br>And not falling from the level of increasing wisdom<br>Are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {2}

“Being skilled in all the paths of the sūtras,<br>Being wise and attracted to the Buddha’s words,<br>And having the infinite awareness of the sugatas’ wisdom<br>Are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {3}

“Whatever Dharma taught by the Buddha they hear,<br>They have no doubt about the Buddha’s teachings<br>But aspire to the Dharma of all the jinas.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {4}

“They know the particular sūtra with the definitive meaning,<br>Such as the Sugata’s teaching on emptiness.<br>They know that all the Dharmas that teach<br>Of beings, individuals, and persons are provisional truth. {5}

“In this world there are many tīrthikas,<br>But they feel no anger toward them.<br>They are firmly established in compassion for them.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {6}

“The retentions [n302] become apparent to them<br>And they have no doubts concerning their appearance.<br>What they speak is in accord with the truth.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {7}

“The four elements of air and water,<br>Fire and earth may change into something else,<br>But they will never turn away from the enlightenment of buddhahood.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {8}

“Whatever skills there are in the world,<br>The bodhisattvas learn them all,<br>And no one sees anyone higher than them.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {9}

“They are unwavering through the power of śamatha,<br>And through vipaśyanā they are like a mountain.<br>Even all beings together would be unable to disturb them.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {10}

“In meditation they stand and talk;<br>Remaining in meditation they walk.<br>In meditation they master the perfections.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {11}

“In meditation they attain the five higher knowledges.<br>Teaching the Dharma they go to a hundred realms.<br>They do not lose their miraculous powers.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {12} ^F21a

“They remain in that kind of samādhi of peace.<br>They attain certainty of the mind,<br>And in their meditation there is no ‘being.’<br>These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {13}

“With buddha wisdom they teach the Dharma<br>To all of the beings who are in the world,<br>And they are able to remember all that they have taught.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {14}

“They see the lords of the worlds in all directions:<br>East, south, west, and north,<br>Above, below, and in the intermediate directions.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {15}

“They have a body that is the color of gold<br>And emanate countless manifestations,<br>Teaching the Dharma to many millions of beings.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {16}

“Each such bodhisattva appears throughout<br>This buddha realm of Jambudvīpa<br>And is renowned also among the devas and asuras.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {17}

“The bodhisattvas train in accordance<br>With the field of activity of the buddhas<br>And the conduct of the sugatas.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {18}

“If the beings that are in this world<br>Were to recite the praises of the bodhisattvas<br>And they were to take great joy in that<br>Then they would not be trained in the Buddha’s wisdom. {19}

“If all the beings that are in this world<br>Were to speak badly to the bodhisattvas,<br>And if they were to become angry toward them,<br>Then they would still not be trained in the Buddha’s wisdom. {20}
