“If they gain wealth it does not make them happy;<br>If they do not gain wealth it does not make them unhappy.<br>Their minds always remain like a mountain.<br>These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {21}

“These three patiences are taught to be the patience regarding what is spoken,<br>The patience that is beneficial for contemplation and meditation,<br>And the patience, from listening to the Dharma, regarding birthlessness.<br>These trainings are the path to enlightenment. [n303] {22}

“When the bodhisattvas attain<br>These three unsurpassable patiences,<br>They see the supreme humans, the sugatas, [n304]<br>And they give them the prophecy of their stainless enlightenment. {23} ^F21b

“When they have received that prophecy<br>The earth shakes in six ways,<br>The realm is illuminated by light,<br>And millions of devas send down a rain of flowers. {24}

“When they have received that prophecy<br>Countless quintillions of beings<br>Develop the aspiration to enlightenment,<br>Thinking, ‘We also shall become jinas, worthy of offerings.’ [n305] {25}

“When the bodhisattvas attain<br>These three unsurpassable patiences<br>They are not born, they do not die,<br>They do not pass away, and are not reborn. {26}

“When the bodhisattvas attain<br>These three unsurpassable patiences<br>They do not see beings born or dying,<br>But see all phenomena as remaining in the true nature. {27}

“In this way they know that they are untrue,<br>That phenomena are like illusions, that they are naturally empty.<br>Emptiness is not born and does not die. [n306]<br>All these phenomena are by nature empty. {28}

“Whenever someone shows them respect,<br>Attending to them, honoring them, and making offerings,<br>They take no pleasure in it,<br>For they know that phenomena have an empty nature. {29}

“Toward beings who revile, threaten, or beat them,<br>They feel no anger, nor pride.<br>They only feel constant love for them,<br>Wishing for those beings to be liberated. {30}

“Even when beaten and cut with sticks and stones,<br>Those wise ones will feel no anger,<br>Remaining in the patience of selflessness,<br>And not having unyielding anger or pride. {31}

“In this way they know the lack of reality,<br>That phenomena are like illusions, with an empty nature.<br>They remain in that knowledge of phenomena<br>And are venerated by this world and its devas. {32}

“Even toward beings holding weapons<br>Who cut into pieces their body and limbs,<br>They would have no anger,<br>And their love and compassion would not diminish. {33}

“Toward such beings, while they are cutting up their body and limbs,<br>This is what arises in their mind:<br>‘Until I can bring these beings to enlightenment<br>I will not pass into the peace of nirvāṇa.’ {34} ^F22a

“The bodhisattvas of great renown<br>Continuously meditate throughout millions of eons<br>With that kind of unsurpassable power of patience,<br>Resting in the equanimity of the patience of selflessness. {35}

“For even more eons, as many as Ganges sand grains,<br>They do not accomplish benefit through the knowledge of a buddha.<br>They do not reach enlightenment,<br>Let alone the wisdom of the tathāgatas. {36}

“Even if one were to speak for countless hundreds of eons,<br>It would be difficult to conclude the praises,<br>The endless descriptions, of the greatly renowned ones<br>Who are established in the patience of selflessness. {37}

“Therefore, the one who desires supreme, unsurpassable enlightenment,<br>The accumulated wisdom of buddhahood,<br>Should meditate on the patience praised by the jinas,<br>And then supreme enlightenment will not be difficult to attain.” {38}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should become skilled in the wisdom of the nonexistent nature of all phenomena.

“Young man, what is being skilled in the wisdom of the nonexistent nature of all phenomena? Bodhisattva mahāsattvas know that all phenomena have no existence, have no essence, have no attributes, have no characteristics, have no origin, have no cessation, have no words, are empty, are primordial peace, and are pure by nature.

“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas  know that all phenomena have no existence, have no essence, have no attributes, have no characteristics, have no birth, have no cessation, have no words, are empty, are primordial peace, and are pure by nature, then at that time, young man, those bodhisattva mahāsattvas have become skilled in the wisdom of the nonexistent nature of all phenomena. ^F22b

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have become skilled in the wisdom of the nonexistent nature of all phenomena do not have desire for any form, sound, smell, taste, or touch. They do not become angry. They are never ignorant.

“Why is that? It is because they do not see phenomena; there is no object to perceive. They do not see the phenomena of desire, the desire, or the desirer; that which angers, the anger, or one who is angry; nor that of which one is ignorant, the ignorance, or the one who is ignorant, and therefore there is no such object to perceive.

“Because there is nothing to be seen and there is no object to perceive, they have no attachment to anything in the three realms and they will quickly attain this samādhi, and quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.

“On this topic, it has been said:

“All phenomena have no existence;<br>They are all devoid of attributes and without characteristics,<br>Without birth and without cessation.<br>That is how you should [n307] perfectly understand phenomena.

“Everything is without existence, without words,<br>Empty, peaceful, and primordially stainless.<br>The one who knows phenomena,<br>Young man, that one is called a buddha.

“Therefore, the revealed nature of equality<br>Is that all phenomena in essence have no nature.<br>Whoever desires the mother of the sugatas<br>Will attain this mother of the jinas.

“Therefore, young man, that is what you should understand through this Dharma teaching. [n308]

“Young man, in the past, countless, vast, immeasurable, inconceivable, unfathomable, asaṃkhyeya eons ago, at that time, in that time, there appeared in the world the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Abhāva­samudgata, who was perfect in wisdom and conduct, a sugata,  a knower of the world, an unsurpassable guide who tamed beings, a teacher of devas and humans, a buddha, and a bhagavān. ^F23a

“Young man, what do you think? Why was that tathāgata named Abhāva­samudgata? [n309]

“Young man, as soon as he was born he rose in the air up to the height of seven palm trees, took seven steps, and said these words: ‘All phenomena have arisen from nonexistence. From nonexistence have all phenomena arisen.’

“Young man, the sound of those words was heard in all the worlds in the trichiliocosm. It resounded and was heard by everyone from the devas on the earth up to those in Brahmā’s paradise. ‘Oh, as soon as this tathāgata was born, he rose in the air up to the height of seven palm trees, took seven steps and said the word nonexistence. Therefore he will be Abhāva­samudgata (Arisen from Nonexistence).’ Thus it was that the name Abhāva­samudgata arose, and that he was given the name Abhāva­samudgata.

“When that bhagavān attained enlightenment, the words ‘arisen from nonexistence’ sounded from the leaves of all the trees, from all the grass, [n310] bushes, and forests, [n311] and from the summits of all the mountains.

“Every sound in that world was heard as the words ‘arisen from nonexistence.’

“Young man, at the time, attending the teachings of the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Abhāva­samudgata, there was a young prince by the name of Mahā­karuṇā­cintin, who had an excellent body and was handsome and good-looking.

“Young man, the prince went to the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Abhāva­samudgata and bowed his head to the Bhagavān’s feet. He circumambulated the Bhagavān three times and then sat down. Then the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Abhāva­samudgata, knowing the higher motivation of Prince Mahā­karuṇā­cintin, taught him this samādhi. When he had heard this he had complete faith in it. With complete faith he shaved off his hair and beard, put on the orange robes, and with such faith left home for homelessness. Having entered homelessness he learned this samādhi. He learned it, kept it, read it, understood it, and dedicated himself to the practice of meditation on it. Through that root of merit, he did not fall into the lower existences for two hundred million eons. He served two hundred million buddhas, and he heard this samādhi from all those tathāgatas. Having heard it, he learned it and understood it. He kept it, read it, propagated it, and repeatedly meditated on it with unadulterated meditation, remaining dedicated to that practice of meditation. ^F23b

“Through those roots of merit, after twenty eons had passed he appeared in the world as the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Suvicintitārtha. He ripened countless beings and benefited countless beings, and afterward, like an extinguished flame, he passed away into perfect nirvāṇa.

“Therefore, young man, this samādhi of that Dharma teaching should be cherished by bodhisattva mahāsattvas. It should be known to cause the unsurpassable perfect wisdom of buddhahood.”

Then at that time the Bhagavān gave a detailed teaching on the preceding chapter by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha:

“I remember that countless eons ago<br>In the past, there appeared a supreme human,<br>One who benefited the world, a great rishi,<br>And his name was Abhāva­samudgata. {1}

“As soon as he was born he rose into the air<br>And taught the nonexistence of all phenomena.<br>He was at that time given a corresponding name<br>And his words were heard throughout the trichiliocosm. {2} ^F24a

“All the devas, they all called out,<br>‘He will be a jina named Abhāva!<br>As soon as he was born he took seven steps<br>And the Jina taught the nonexistence of phenomena.’ {3}

“When the sage became a buddha, a Dharma king,<br>Who taught the nature of all phenomena,<br>From plants, trees, bushes, mountains, [n312] and rocks<br>There came the words ‘phenomena have no existence.’ {4}

“All the sounds there were in the world<br>Became the words ‘all are nonexistent.’<br>In that way there sounded<br>The words of the Guide of the World. {5}

“At that time there was a prince<br>Whose name had always been Karuṇāvicintin.<br>He had an excellent form and was handsome.<br>He came into the presence of that jina. {6}

“He bowed to the feet of the sage, that great being,<br>And respectfully circumambulated him.<br>In order to hear the stainless, unsurpassable Dharma<br>He sat there with a devout mind. {7}

“The heroic [n313] Jina, knowing his aspiration,<br>Gave the teaching of this samādhi.<br>Having listened to this stainless samādhi<br>He quickly entered homelessness in the supreme Jina’s teaching. {8}

“Having entered homelessness he possessed,<br>Read, and understood this samādhi.<br>For a full two hundred million eons<br>He did not descend to an unfortunate existence. {9}

“Through the good karma that he had made<br>He pleased two hundred million buddhas,<br>And in the presence of those jinas<br>He cultivated this samādhi. {10}

“He afterward became a buddha in the world<br>Who was always known as Sucintitārtha.<br>He benefited many millions of beings<br>And afterward attained nirvāṇa, [n314] like an extinguished flame. [n315] {11}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha,  “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood and liberate all beings from the ocean of existence should hear this king of samādhis, in which the equality of the nature of all phenomena is revealed, which is praised by all the buddhas and is the mother of the tathāgatas. They should obtain it, preserve it, understand it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others. ^F24b

“Why is that? Young man, this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, has given birth to all the tathāgatas, the arhats, the perfectly enlightened buddhas; all tathāgatas, śrāvakas, and pratyekabuddhas have come from it.

“Therefore, young man, you also should obtain this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, which is praised by all the buddhas and is the mother of the tathāgatas. [n316] It has been said:

“Therefore, those who wish for enlightenment and buddhahood,<br>And to liberate beings from the ocean of existence,<br>Should obtain this sūtra praised by the buddhas,<br>And then sublime enlightenment will not be difficult to attain.” [n317]

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish [n318] to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood should become skilled [n319] in the patience of profound Dharma. [n320]

“Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas become skilled in the patience of profound Dharma?

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas should know that all phenomena are like illusions.  They should know that all phenomena are like dreams, like mirages, like echoes, like optical illusions, like the moon on water, like hallucinations, [n321] like reflections, and like space. ^F25a

“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas know that all phenomena are like illusions, [n322] they are skilled in the patience of profound Dharma. Those who have the patience of profound Dharma have no desire for any phenomenon that causes desire, have no anger toward any phenomenon that causes anger, and have no ignorance regarding any phenomenon that causes ignorance. Why is that? It is because they do not see that phenomenon; they do not perceive that phenomenon. They do not see the phenomena and they do not perceive the phenomena of that which is desired, the desire, or the desirer; that which angers, the anger, or one who is angry; nor that of which one is ignorant, the ignorance, or the one who is ignorant. Because they do not see and do not perceive those phenomena they have no desire, they have no anger, they have no ignorance, their minds do not regress, and they rest in meditation. They are without conceptual elaboration. They have crossed over to the other side. They have reached dry land. They have reached safety. They have attained freedom from fear. [n323] They have correct conduct. They have knowledge. They have wisdom. They have merit. They have miraculous powers. They have memory. [n324] They have intelligence. They have realization. [n325] They have a sense of modesty. They have stability. They have bodhisattva conduct. They have the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy. They are unblemished. [n326] They have nothing. They are arhats. Their defilements have ceased. They have no kleśas. They have power. Their minds are liberated. Their wisdom is liberated. They are thoroughbred stallions. [n327] They are great elephants. [n328] They have done what had to be done. They have accomplished what had to be accomplished. They have put down their burden. They have reached their goals. They have ended engagement with existence. They have liberated their minds through true knowledge. They are mendicants who have attained all the perfect, highest, complete powers of the mind. They are brahmins. [n329] They are snātakas. [n330] They are masters of the Vedas. [n331] They know the Vedas. [n332] They are śrotriyas. [n333] They are children of the buddhas. They are children of the Śākya. [n334] They have crushed the thorns. [n335] They have not left the law behind. [n336] They have left the trench barrier behind. [n337] They have crossed over the trench barrier. [n338] They have extracted the splinters. [n339] They have no illness. [n340] They are bhikṣus. They are free from all bondage. They have been born as humans. They are good humans. They are supreme humans. They are great humans. They are human lions. [n341] They are human elephants. [n342] They are human stallions. [n343] They are human carthorses. [n344] They are human heroes. [n345] They are human strongmen. [n346] They are human flowers. [n347] They are human lotuses. [n348] They are human white lotuses. [n349] They are human tamers. [n350] They are human moons. [n351] They are extraordinary humans. They are stainless humans.” [n352] ^F25b

Then the Bhagavān, in order to give this Dharma teaching on entering the patience of profound Dharma, recited these verses:

“At one time a world appears,<br>And later the entire world becomes space.<br>As it was before, so it is afterward.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {1}

“All that there is in this world<br>Later dissolves into the mass of water below.<br>As it is below, so it is above.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {2} ^F26a

“Just as in a completely cloudless sky<br>In an instant a mass of clouds appears—<br>From where did they first originate?<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {3}

“If you think of a tathāgata who has passed into nirvāṇa,<br>His image will appear in your mind.<br>As he was before, so he is afterward.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {4}

“When a person sees a mass of foam<br>That is carried along in a river<br>And examines it, they see that it has no essence.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {5}

“When large drops of rain fall,<br>There appear separate bubbles of water.<br>They vanish as they appear; the bubbles have no existence.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {6}

“When a letter is sent to another town<br>With news of the good or bad that has been done,<br>A voice does not accompany the letter.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {7}

“When a man is intoxicated from alcohol,<br>He perceives the ground to be spinning,<br>But the earth is not moving or shaking.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {8}

“A woman sees her beautified face<br>On the surface of a mirror or a bowl of oil.<br>The fool feels passion for it<br>And runs in search for the desired. {9}

“The face was not transferred there.<br>The face will never be found in the reflection,<br>And yet fools have desire for it.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. [n353] {10}

“Just like optical illusions and fata morganas,<br>Just like dreams and just like illusions,<br>When their attributes are meditated on, their nature is empty.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {11}

“When the moon is in a clear sky,<br>Its reflection appears on the sea,<br>But the moon has not moved onto the water.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {12}

“A man who is inside a canyon [n354]<br>Sees no one but hears the echoes<br>Of singing, speaking, and laughter.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {13} ^F26b

“Echoes are produced<br>By songs, music, and weeping,<br>But the song that is heard does not exist.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. [n355] {14}

“Although pleasures are enjoyed in a dream,<br>When the person awakes they are not be seen.<br>The fool, though, becomes attached to those pleasures.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {15}

“A magician causes forms to appear,<br>Creating horses, elephants, chariots, and so on.<br>But though they appear they do not exist at all.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {16}

“In a young woman’s dream<br>She gives birth to a son and then sees him die.<br>She is happy when he’s born and sad when he dies.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. [n356] {18}

“In the night the reflection of the moon<br>Appears on clear, undisturbed water,<br>But it is empty of a moon and there is nothing to grasp.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {19}

“A thirsty person traveling<br>At noon during the summer<br>Sees a lake that is a mirage.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {20}

“The water that is a mirage cannot be found.<br>Foolish beings want to drink it,<br>But water that is not real cannot be drunk.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {21}

“When a person in search of its essence<br>Pulls apart the trunk of a green banana plant,<br>They find no essence either inside or outside.<br>Know that all phenomena are like that. {22}

“The eyes, the ears, and the nose are unreliable.<br>The tongue, the body, and the mind are unreliable.<br>If the senses could be relied upon,<br>What need would there be for the path of the noble ones? {23}

“These senses are unreliable.<br>Their nature is material and neutral.<br>Therefore those who wish for the path to nirvāṇa<br>Must follow the path of the noble ones. {24}

“If one examines the body back into the past,<br>There is no body and no conception of a body.<br>When there is no body and no conception of a body<br>This is called the lineage of the noncomposite. [n357] {25}

“There are no phenomena in the phenomena of nirvāṇa,<br>For if it is nonexistent there could never be an existence.<br>Those who conceptualize teach existence and nonexistence,<br>But practicing in that way will not bring an end to suffering. {26} ^F27a

“ ‘Existing,’ ‘not existing,’ and both are extremes.<br>‘Pure’ and ‘impure’ are also extremes.<br>Therefore, rejecting both extremes,<br>The wise do not even remain in the middle. {27}

“ ‘Existing’ and ‘not existing’ are in conflict.<br>‘Pure’ and ‘impure’ are also in conflict.<br>When there is conflict, suffering cannot be ended.<br>When there is no conflict, suffering ceases. [n358] {28}

“When fools speak about remaining in mindfulness [n359]<br>They become proud, saying, ‘I have witnessed it in my body.’ [n360]<br>But those who have witnessed it in their body have no pride;<br>They are those who are freed from all such pride. [n361] {29}

“When speaking of the four dhyānas,<br>The foolish claim they can experience dhyāna.<br>But those who know and realize that dhyāna<br>Is without kleśas or pride reject such arrogance. {30}

“When speaking of the four truths,<br>The foolish say that they see the truth.<br>But there is no pride when the truth is seen.<br>The Jina taught the truth that is without pride. {31}

“Do not be proud of maintaining correct conduct.<br>Do not become proud through listening to the Dharma.<br>When those with little wisdom become proud,<br>That is the root of increasing suffering. {32}

“The world’s guide, the omniscient one,<br>Taught that pride is the root of suffering.<br>To be puffed up with pride makes suffering grow;<br>To have no pride brings suffering to an end. {33}

“However much Dharma you have learned,<br>If you feel proud of your learning and let your proper conduct lapse,<br>Your misconduct will take you to the lower realms<br>And all that great learning will not protect you. {34}

“If you feel proud of being renowned for correct conduct<br>And do not dedicate yourself to listening to many teachings,<br>When the results of your correct conduct have been used up<br>You will afterward experience suffering. [n362] {35}

“If you meditate on a worldly samādhi<br>And do not eliminate the conception of a self,<br>Then the kleśas will arise once more,<br>As happened in the samādhi practice of Udraka. [n363] {36} ^F27b

“If one examines the Dharma of selflessness,<br>And if after examining, one meditates,<br>That will be the cause resulting in the attainment of nirvāṇa.<br>It is impossible for peace to come from any other cause. {37}

“If a man is being attacked by bandits<br>And, wishing to save his life, he tries to run away<br>But his legs will not move and he cannot run,<br>He will be captured and killed [n364] by the bandits. {38}

“In the same way, a stupid person without correct conduct<br>May try to escape from composite phenomena.<br>But without correct conduct he is not able to flee,<br>And will be killed by old age, illness, and death. {39}

“Just as many thousands of savages [n365]<br>Do you harm in various ways,<br>The kleśas will in many ways,<br>Like savages, destroy that which is good. {40}

“Those who have understood the skandhas to be without a self,<br>Even if insulted or beaten, will not be dismayed.<br>They will not fall under the power of the kleśa demons.<br>Those who know emptiness will never become agitated. {41}

“Many people teach the emptiness of the skandhas<br>But have not understood that selflessness;<br>When those who have not understood are contradicted by others,<br>They will be overpowered by anger and speak harsh words. {42}

“There was a man [n366] who was ill and suffering physically.<br>For many years he could not attain freedom from his illness.<br>For a long time he was tormented by his illness,<br>And in order to be cured he went in search of a physician. {43}

“Searching and searching, again and again,<br>He found a skilled and wise physician<br>Who had compassion for him<br>And said, ‘Take this medicine.’ {44}

“He gave him much excellent medicine,<br>But the sick man didn’t take the healing medicine.<br>That was not the fault of the physician or the medicine;<br>It was the fault of the sick person. {45}

“In the same way, those who have entered homelessness in this teaching,<br>Who know of the strengths, the dhyānas, and the powers<br>But do not dedicate themselves to meditation,<br>Are not endeavouring in what is correct, so how could they attain nirvāṇa? {46}

“All phenomena are always empty by nature.<br>The heirs of the jinas have eliminated all things.<br>The entirety of existence has always been empty.<br>The emptiness of the tīrthikas is limited. {47}

“The wise do not argue with fools,<br>They politely avoid them;<br>Thinking, ‘They come to me with malicious intent,’<br>They do not engage with the Dharma of fools. {48} ^F28a

“Knowing the nature and dispositions of fools,<br>The wise do not associate with fools.<br>Whenever they associate well with them<br>Those fools eventually turn into enemies. {49}

“The wise do not depend upon the foolish.<br>The wise and the foolish have different natures.<br>The nature of the foolish is naturally contrary,<br>So the wise do not have ordinary people as friends. {50}

“They may speak with words about the Dharma<br>But do not believe it, showing their anger and aggression.<br>Such is the Dharma of fools, and knowing this to be so<br>The wise do not rely on it. {51}

“The foolish are in accord with other fools<br>Like impurity with other impurities.<br>The wise are in accord with other wise people<br>Like butter [n367] is with ghee. {52}

“They do not examine the faults of saṃsāra;<br>They pay no attention to the ripening of karma;<br>They have no faith in the words of the buddhas:<br>Those fools will be sliced and cut into pieces. {53}

“They have obtained a human life that is difficult to obtain,<br>But they have not become skilled in any craft.<br>They have become poor without any wealth.<br>In order to have a livelihood they become mendicants. {54}

“Having become mendicants in this teaching of the Buddha,<br>They become attached to their robes and alms bowls.<br>They fall under the influence of bad companions,<br>And they do not practice the teaching of the Sugata. {55}

“They are not observant of their own conduct.<br>Such fools do not perceive the states of their minds.<br>Day and night they do not follow the discipline,<br>And they do not abhor the path of bad actions. {56}

“They do not restrain their body and mind.<br>There is nothing that they will not say.<br>They are always looking for faults in others,<br>And criticize any mistake they make. {57}

“Such fools have attachment to food.<br>They know no limit to their eating.<br>They obtain their food through the Buddha’s merit,<br>But these fools do not keep that in mind. {58}

“When they find food that is delicious and pleasing,<br>They consume [n368] it without engaging in the discipline.<br>For them that food becomes poison,<br>Like an unclean lotus stem [n369] for an elephant calf. [n370] {59} ^F28b

“The wise, the sagacious, the realized<br>Also eat food that is pure and pleasing,<br>But they have no attachment to it.<br>They eat without clinging, maintaining the discipline. {60}

“The wise, sagacious, and realized<br>Say ‘welcome’ when the foolish come,<br>Bringing them closer with pleasant words,<br>And maintaining compassion for them; {61}

“They are kind and helpful to them.<br>But the foolish are happy when harm comes to the wise.<br>Because of such faults, the wise avoid the foolish<br>And live alone like deer in the forest. {62}

“The wise, knowing these kinds of defects,<br>Do not associate with fools.<br>They think, ‘If I depend on those who have no wisdom,<br>There will be no higher rebirth, let alone the attainment of enlightenment.’ {63}

“The wise reach enlightenment by putting into practice<br>The samādhi of dwelling in love,<br>Of dwelling in compassion, of acting with joy,<br>And with constant equanimity toward all existences. {64}

“They attain the enlightenment that is peace, free of misery.<br>They perceive beings afflicted by illness and aging. [n371]<br>They have compassion toward them,<br>And give them the teachings of ultimate truth. {65}

“Who can know the true nature of the jinas<br>And the truth of the sugatas, which is beyond description? [n372]<br>It is they who hear this kind of Dharma<br>And attain the immaterial patience of the noble ones.” {66}

The Bhagavān then said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, you should be someone who makes practice essential, and always trains in that way. Why is that? Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who make practice essential will not even find it difficult to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, not to mention attaining this samādhi.”

Then the youth Candraprabha rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee,  with palms placed together, bowed toward the Bhagavān and exclaimed, “Bhagavān, that teaching and instruction that the bhagavāns have taught well, presented well, and explained well to the bodhisattva mahāsattvas, the entire bodhisattva training that they have explained well and presented well is marvelous. ^F29a

“Bhagavān, this is the scope of activity of the tathāgatas, not of the śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, let alone the tīrthikas.

“Bhagavān, I, too, will make practice essential, and without care for life or body I shall train as the tathāgatas have. Why is that? Bhagavān, I wish to train as the tathāgatas have. Bhagavān, I wish to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. Bhagavān, I wish to eliminate the evil māras. Bhagavān, I wish to free all beings from all fear and all suffering. [n373] I pray that the Bhagavān will place his right hand upon my head.”

He said to the Bhagavān:

“You have an excellent body, like a clear sky.<br>You are the son of wisdom, who has no body or attributes.<br>You are a deep ocean of qualities, and have compassion.<br>You who are without equal, place your hand upon my head.” [n374] {i}

The Bhagavān placed upon Candraprabha’s head his right hand, which was adorned with many characteristics that were the result of many roots of merit, and which was of the color of divine gold.

As soon as the Bhagavān placed his right hand upon Candraprabha’s head, in that very instant, more indescribable than indescribably many hundred thousand quintillions of samādhi entranceways that arise from the perfection of wisdom were revealed to Candraprabha, such as the heroic, [n375] the treasury of space, [n376] the vajra-like, [n377] the speed of the mind, [n378] the revealing of all forms, [n379]  the ultimate absence of obscurations, the revealing of all tathāgatas, [n380] the consecration of all emptiness, [n381] and so on. Many entranceways to dhāraṇīs and liberations [n382] were revealed. He attained the knowledge of the joy and happiness that is described by the noble ones, of the countless vast number of beings in the deva realms, and the scope of experience of the buddhas and bodhisattvas. ^F29b

It was said:

The Bhagavān placed upon the head of the youth Candraprabha<br>The hand that for many millions of eons had given away jewels,<br>Which was beautified by being webbed, and had markings of a vase and hook,<br>A knot of eternity, a wheel, a victory banner, a flag, and fishes. {ii}

Then Candraprabha, full of joy and happiness and the knowledge of the countless, vast number of beings in the deva realms, and the scope of experience of the buddhas and bodhisattvas, rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee, with palms placed together, he bowed toward the Bhagavān and recited these appropriate verses of praise:

“I pay homage to you, the unsurpassable provider of freedom from fear.<br>I pay homage to you, a loving friend of beings who benefits others.<br>I pay homage to you, who possess the power of truth and the ten strengths.<br>I pay homage to you, who are the equal of the unequaled tathāgatas. {iii}

“I pay homage to you, the Lord who has the highest compassion.<br>I pay homage to you, the hero who has subjugated the four enemies. [n383]<br>I pay homage to you, who know the benefits of sublime diligence.<br>I pay homage to you, the Lord [n384] who has the supreme dharmakāya. {iv}

“I will always go for refuge to you, Lord,<br>The Jina who is a sun shining in the center of the vast sky of wisdom,<br>Dispelling darkness with the light of love and compassion,<br>And who is the teacher of the extremely profound Dharma of the ultimate truth.” {v} ^F30a

When the youth Candraprabha had recited these appropriate verses of praise to the Bhagavān, he said to him, “Bhagavān, so that you may show me your compassion I pray that you, with your saṅgha of bodhisattvas and saṅgha of bhikṣus, will assent to eat your meal tomorrow at my home.

“I pray to the Lord of men and your sons<br>That you eat a pure meal at my home.<br>Lord of sages, in order to show me your compassion,<br>Chief of devas, give your assent.” {vi}

The Bhagavān, because of his compassion, by remaining silent assented to eat a meal together with his saṅgha of bodhisattvas and saṅgha of bhikṣus at the home of the youth Candraprabha.

The youth Candraprabha, knowing that the Bhagavān had assented by his silence, rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, bowed his head to the Bhagavān’s feet, circumambulated the Bhagavān three times, and departed from the Bhagavān’s presence.

The youth Candraprabha then went down from Vulture Peak Mountain, and at that time he perfectly adorned the entire road in between Vulture Peak Mountain and the great city of Rājagṛha.

As an offering to the Bhagavān he cleared a great, wide roadway so that it was free of grass, tree stumps, thorns, stones, pebbles, and gravel, and spread pure sand over it, so that it was as soft and pleasant to the touch as down, and made a pleasant sound. He covered it with flowers from all seasons, such as divine blue lotuses, red lotuses, night lotuses, white lotuses, water lilies, kachnar flowers, sambac jasmines, magnolias, bignonias, star jasmines, sesame flowers, ironwood flowers, and aśoka flowers. Parasols, banners, flags, flags of victory, precious arches, [n385] and canopies were set up along the road.  There were precious censers from which flowed the smoke of black agarwood. [n386] Arranged in different places were dancers and performers skilled in performing divine songs, dance, and music. Beautifully adorned men, women, boys, and girls were arranged holding paṇava drums, [n387] one-stringed lutes, [n388] lutes, flutes, mṛdaṅga drums, [n389] mukunda drums, [n390] and muraja drums. [n391] On both sides of the road tall palm trees were adorned with various divine jewels and a jingling network of bells made from Jambu River gold. [n392] There were many hundred thousand quintillions of pillars made of precious materials, and different kinds of trees of various heights and thicknesses made from the seven jewels, and on which were arranged the leaves, flowers, and fruits of all seasons. ^F30b

The road was excellently adorned in various ways.<br>Canopies, parasols, and flags were erected.<br>The sound of music was perfectly played,<br>And similarly there was the beautiful sound of songs. {vii}

That perfect road was excellently adorned<br>By many women performing dances,<br>Many millions of various excellent cloths,<br>And beautiful, excellent garlands of flowers. {viii}

“The Buddha, the moon of sages, the compassionate one<br>Is coming to this pure excellent city.”<br>On hearing that, young Candraprabha with great faith<br>Perfectly adorned a great, vast road. {ix}

He spread out pure, divine sand<br>And scattered perfect, beautiful flowers.<br>He also set up precious pillars<br>And made the road as beautiful as a divine city. {x}

Young Candraprabha, with immense joy,<br>Perfectly adorned the road in various ways.<br>Devas, asuras, and nāgas, upon seeing it<br>Were astonished and cried out, “Ha ha ha!” {xi}

To the left and right of the road there were placed<br>Tall, excellent, round palm trees made of Jambu River gold,<br>Decorated and beautified by a network<br>Of numerous jingling, precious bells. {xii}

Similarly arranged were million of precious trees<br>Adorned by blossomed flowers of all seasons,<br>Which were beautiful adornments for that vast road,<br>Like a blissful park in the deva realms. {xiii} ^F31a

Pillars that were made from precious materials,<br>With beautiful strings of beads that shone like light—<br>An indescribable sight, huge and vast—<br>Were set up and arranged on the left and right of the road. {xiv}

The Buddha, the Lord of the three worlds,<br>Traveled on that road to the capital city.<br>That great road was adorned in that way<br>So that it was beautiful in every way. {xv}

On the right and left, precious censers were hung.<br>They were filled with black agarwood.<br>From all the censers there formed a cloud of smoke,<br>With divine, pleasant aromas of various kinds. {xvi}

The youth Candraprabha, for the sake of the Jina,<br>Arranged vast, incalculable ornaments of divine materials,<br>From the entrance to the water well of the city<br>Up to the king of mountains, Gṛdhrakūṭa. {xvii}

Young Candraprabha adorned the road with many different precious arrangements. [n393] Then young Candraprabha descended from Vulture Peak and went to the great city of Rājagṛha, to his tall, vast, great, divine home. He reached there and he entered his home. He spent that night preparing a great amount of excellent, delicious [n394] food and drink, and creating food that had a hundred flavors. Then he sprinkled well the ground in the great city of Rājagṛha and swept it clean, scattered flower petals, perfumed it with incense, put up canopies, hung ribbons and wreaths of silk, and set up parasols, banners, and flags.

In that way he made the main road of Rājagṛha up to the town free of stones, pebbles, and gravel, scattered it with various flowers, and sprinkled it with sandalwood powder. He adorned the windows, porticoes, doors, [n395] roofs, [n396] lattices, [n397] and the crescent moons, [n398] and perfumed them with sandalwood. In that way he adorned the city of Rājagṛha with countless displays  and adorned his own house, too, with a variety of many adornments. He hung it with many precious strings of beads. He adorned it with the raiment of the Tuṣita deities and also beautified the grounds. He had many kinds of garlands and wreaths put up as adornments. He arranged a hundred thousand precious seats. In order to make offerings to the Bhagavān he placed in their center a lion throne of divine materials that surpassed the work of devas and humans. In the four directions he hung censers made of various precious materials, from which flowed the smoke of black agarwood. In that way the youth Candraprabha arranged his excellent home so that for the enjoyment of the Bhagavān there was the sound of divine songs, performances, and music; pure parasols and banners were erected; an audience of a hundred thousand devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, and nonhumans thronged it; and it was filled with many various kinds of precious flowers. ^F31b

Candraprabha perfectly, extensively adorned<br>His vast and excellent home.<br>In the center he placed a lion throne of divine materials<br>Where the lamp of the world would sit. {xviii}

He perfectly set out countless millions<br>Of extremely precious, beautiful seats<br>Where the saṅgha of the lamp of the world,<br>The Lord of jinas, would sit. {xix}

Censers made of all kinds of precious materials,<br>Completely filled with agarwood,<br>Were hung in all directions,<br>And from them a beautiful aroma spread. {xx}

Candraprabha, in order to attain the ten strengths,<br>Spread throughout the entire excellent grounds of the house<br>Various kinds of beautiful, precious flowers—<br>A multitude of excellent, aromatic flowers. {xxi}

The sound of dancers, singers, and of music<br>Filled the entire excellent house with sound.<br>He erected also parasols and banners<br>So that the house was intensely beautiful, like that of a deity. {xxii} ^F32a

The vast excellent home of the youth Candraprabha<br>Was adorned by a multitude of young people.<br>It was filled with many nāgas, yakṣas, and asuras,<br>And was gazed upon by many hundreds of devas. [n399] {xxiii}

The young man Candraprabha, having adorned the great city of Rājagṛha and having perfectly beautified his own home, after the night was over, in the early morning, departed, accompanied by the music of hundreds of various kinds of instruments, with many millions of parasols, banners, and flags held high, and with an encircling vanguard of a great assembly of eight million quintillion bodhisattvas, their cupped hands filled with divine coral tree flowers. Among them were bodhisattvas with one life remaining, such as Avalokiteśvara, Mahā­sthāma­prāpta, Gandhahasti, Ratnaketu, Dundubhisvara, [n400] Durabhisambhava, Mañjuśrī Kumārabhūta, Vīrasena, Subāhu, Ratnakusuma, Amoghadarśin, Maitreya, and others, accompanied by many adorned horses and elephants without riders that were being led along, with an assembly of countless people of the country, his own cupped hands filled with divine coral tree flowers; and they were accompanied by the enchanting, beautiful, harmonious sound of the laughter of the deities as they cried, “Oh, the bodhisattva’s great power! The bodhisattva’s great miracles! The bodhisattva’s great manifestations! The bodhisattva’s—a la la!”

He came out through the hot springs gateway [n401] of the great city of Rājagṛha and went toward Vulture Peak Mountain, and to the Bhagavān.

When he arrived, he bowed his head to the Bhagavān’s feet, circumambulated the Bhagavān three times, [n402] sprinkled the divine coral tree flowers that filled his cupped hands over the Bhagavān, and went to sit down to one side.

Maitreya and the other  bodhisattva mahāsattvas bowed their heads to the Bhagavān’s feet, circumambulated the Bhagavān three times, sprinkled the divine coral tree flowers that filled their cupped hands over the Bhagavān, and also sat down to one side. ^F32b

Then the youth, who had sat to one side, rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee, with palms placed together bowed toward the Bhagavān and said, “It is midday, Bhagavān, the time to eat. If the Bhagavān considers the time has come, then together with the saṅgha of bodhisattvas, the saṅgha of bhikṣus, and the devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, rishis, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas, kumbhāṇḍas, pretas, pūtanas, humans, and nonhumans who have great power, who are widely renowned for their great power and have great influence, come to the great city of Rājagṛha, as the time has come to eat the midday meal in my garden. Sugata, it is midday. [n403]

“I have adorned well the entire, excellent city,<br>And similarly, Lord, my garden.<br>I have prepared and laid out divine food with a hundred flavors.<br>As it is midday, I pray to the Sugata to arise. {xxiv}

“Supreme Rishi, you who hold the qualities of the ten strengths in your hands,<br>Encircled by the assembly of your sons, come to the city.<br>I pray that you, the illuminating sun who dispels darkness, will arise.<br>Bhagavān, the time has come for the midday meal in my garden. {xxv}

“I pray that you come, with your sons, to my garden.<br>You will benefit an assembly of many beings.<br>Just as Dīpaṃkara granted a prophecy to you,<br>Grant me likewise a direct prophecy in this world. {xxvi}

“When I have heard that prophecy in this world,<br>I will also develop a vast and perfect aspiration,<br>And all these beings will become buddhas.<br>There are no unworthy beings present here. {xxvii} ^F33a

“Arise, arise, Lord who has the ten strengths.<br>Benefit me and come to my garden.<br>Just as you come to my garden,<br>In that way I will go to the supreme tree of enlightenment. {xxviii}

“When I have gone to the foot of the supreme tree of enlightenment,<br>I will remain there unshakable and unwavering.<br>I will defeat with love the māras and their claws,<br>And just as you attained it, I, too, will attain enlightenment.” {xxix}

Then the Bhagavān, who had known what the youth Candraprabha would request, addressed these lines of verse to him:

“Arise Candraprabha, son of the jinas!<br>Arise, you who are joyful in generosity, you supreme being!<br>Arise, you who have compassion and firm conduct!<br>Let us go to the meal! [n404] Let us proceed [n405] to your home.” {xxx}

After speaking these lines, [n406] the Bhagavān arose from his seat. He put on his lower robe, picked up his Dharma robe and alms bowl, and with the great saṅgha of a hundred thousand bhikṣus, and accompanied by a multitude of bodhisattva mahāsattvas, he proceeded. Many hundreds of thousands of devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, rishis, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas, kumbhāṇḍas, pretas, pūtanas, [n407] humans, and nonhumans made offerings to him and praised him. Through his great buddha powers, his great buddha miracles, his great buddha manifestations, and his buddha conduct he radiated many quintillions [n408] of light rays. He emanated flocks of melodious, soft, and beautiful birds of many different shapes and colors, such as geese, cranes, ruddy shelducks, swans, partridges, peacocks, rollers, [n409] parrots, [n410] mynas, cuckoos, avadavats, [n411] and snipe, so that like devas in the sky, each with its own song, they emitted the sound of music. [n412] ^F33b

The yakṣa lords Surūpa, Indraketu, Vikaṭa, Bakula, Pāñcika, Śākyavardhana, and many quintillions of yakṣa lords holding pestles [n413] with both hands, offered many quintillions of huge, vast censers made of various divine precious materials, with handles of beryl, sapphire, crystal, and white coral, filled with uragasāra sandalwood, gośīrṣa sandalwood, vetiver, yellow sandalwood, Malaya sandalwood, red sandalwood, agarwood, and so on, and from which smoke flowed.

There were the superior kings of great power, renowned as having great power, from their own regions, accompanied by many divisions of perfectly adorned horses and elephants being led without their riders, chariots, and infantry, [n414] in lines marching in front, holding in their hands many streamers and precious garlands. The horses and elephants, even though they were being led along without riders, were proceeding magnificently and emitting beautiful cries.

The Bhagavān was accompanied on his right-hand side by Brahmā, who was making offerings to him and attending upon him, and on his left-hand side by Śakra, lord of the devas, and by countless devas with great power, who were renowned for their great power, who were mighty and illustrious, and whose bodies were adorned by excellent divine crowns, ornamented anklets, earrings, bracelets, flowers on their ears, bejeweled necklaces, and flower garlands. Their forms were made visible and they were holding coral tree flowers, asters, orchids, hibiscus, amaranths, magnolias, karnikara flowers, aśoka flowers, [n415] bignonias, kachnar flowers, blue lotuses, medlar flowers, [n416] sambac jasmine, star jasmine, ironwood flowers, red lotuses, night lotuses, white lotuses, water lilies, precious garlands, precious agarwood, and precious fruit. They were playing hundreds of thousands of different kinds of musical instruments, waving millions of pieces of cloth, crying out, “Ha! Ha! Ha!” and sending down a great rain of flowers. In order to make offerings to the Bhagavān they filled the entire sky without leaving any space and sent down a great rain of flowers, incense, garlands, perfumes, powders, and jewels. ^F34a

The Bhagavān entered at midday the great city of Rājagṛha through the hot springs gateway. The nature of this is described in these verses: [n417]

The Tathāgata Buddha, knowing it was time,<br>That hero adorned with all qualities,<br>Who illuminates countless realms,<br>The Bhagavān, the lion of men, set forth. {xxxi}

Avalokiteśvara, Mahā­sthāma­prāpta, [n418] and Amoghadarśin; [n419]<br>Gandhahasti, Ratnakusuma, [n420] and Ratnabāhu; [n421]<br>And Ratnaketu, Durabhisambhava, [n422] Vīrasena, [n423]<br>And others followed in the Jina’s footsteps. [n424] {xxxii}

On his right was Ajita, who is named Maitraka, [n425]<br>Who has the wealth of infinite qualities,<br>Who will become the following buddha<br>And has completed the accumulation of merit and wisdom. {xxxiii}

He is one who has cultivated [n426] love, rejoicing, and equanimity.<br>He is a great being of the Dharma who has developed compassion.<br>He understands the infinite qualities, the qualities of the Lord of sages. [n427] {xxxiv}

He followed behind [n428] the compassionate Sugata<br>And was followed by those [n429] who will be<br>Those with great realization in the Good Eon:<br>The thousand buddhas less four, {xxxv}

Who were preceded by Maitraka.<br>And also he who in the past, in this city of Rājagṛha,<br>While born in divine bodies that were like beautiful moonlight,<br>Made infinite offerings to jinas throughout eons, {xxxvi}

That hero Candraprabha was also present at the front.<br>To the left of the one with supreme compassion<br>Was Mañjuśrī, [n430] along with many thousands of millions [n431]<br>Of heroes who have sublime qualities of miraculous powers, [n432] {xxxvii}

Who traveled to endless hundreds of realms.<br>Following him were those in the śrāvaka saṅgha:<br>Śārisuta, [n433] Maudgalyāyana, [n434] Kāla,<br>Kāśyapa, Subhūti, Nanda, and Kapphiṇa; {xxxviii}

Bhadrikarāja, [n435] and similarly Kauṇḍinya;<br>Ānanda, and similarly Sthavira Rāhula;<br>And Svāgata, Kañcika, [n436] Pūrṇa, Udāyin,<br>Revata, Kauṣṭhila, [n437] Upāli, and Aniruddha. {xxxix}

A full nine thousand [n438] of those with matted hair<br>Followed behind the śrāvaka saṅgha.<br>They were all mighty ascetics who knew the Vedas and the rituals, [n439]<br>And had mastered curses, renunciation, and beneficial incantations. [n440] {xl} ^F34b

Self-controlled rishis with peaceful minds,<br>With disciplined minds, bowing with palms together,<br>Followed behind the Buddha, the lamp of the world,<br>The lion of men, endowed with compassion, {xli}

The liberator of thousands of beings, as he proceeded.<br>Like the completely pure lord of the host of stars,<br>The full moon of the last month of autumn, [n441]<br>The Teacher who is without equal was encircled {xlii}

By many hundred thousands of Brahmās.<br>As he stepped on the threshold of the city’s gateway,<br>The earth and its thick forests shook.<br>The devas, asuras, [n442] and mahoragas {xliii}

Scattered excellent flowers and supreme incense. [n443] {xliv}

The moment the Bhagavān placed his right foot, adorned by a precious wheel from the accumulation of countless roots of merit, upon the threshold of the gate, this universe of a thousand million worlds shook in six ways. It trembled, trembled strongly, and trembled intensely; it quivered, quivered strongly, and quivered intensely; it shook, shook strongly, and shook intensely; it shuddered, shuddered strongly, and shuddered intensely; it quaked, quaked strongly, and quaked intensely; the east sank and the west rose, the west sank and the east rose, the north sank and the south rose, the south sank and the north rose, the perimeter sank and the center rose, and the center sank and the perimeter rose. A great radiance shone in the world, and countless, numberless other amazing, wonderful, miraculous manifestations appeared. [n444]

The nature of this is described in these verses:

When the Guide came to that supreme city<br>And placed his supreme foot upon the gateway’s threshold,<br>That magnificence caused this earth to shake,<br>And the beings in this supreme city were overjoyed. {1}

When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold<br>The people who were hungry and thirsty<br>At that time became free of the need to eat or drink.<br>They became free of hunger and thirst. {2} ^F35a

When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold<br>All those people who were blind,<br>Deaf, and had no protector and little merit<br>Were all able to see and hear. {3}

When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold<br>All the pretas in the realm of Yama,<br>Suffering greatly and eating snot and spit,<br>Were touched by light and became happy. {4}

When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold<br>The supreme trees—the sal and the karnikara—<br>At the summit of crags and on mountaintops,<br>They all bowed toward the Buddha. {5}

When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold<br>The entire ground shook in six ways<br>Throughout the villages and towns as far as the ocean,<br>Without causing harm to anyone. {6}

Devas, humans, kumbhāṇḍas, and rākṣasas—<br>Wherever beings lived, there was happiness and joy.<br>They developed faith in supreme, sublime enlightenment<br>And held a parasol for the guide of the world. {7}

When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold,<br>Thousands of musical instruments sounded without being played;<br>Hearing the beautiful sound of music,<br>All beings were filled with joy. {8}

Hundreds of thousands of trees bowed down,<br>And all flowers blossomed at that time.<br>Hundreds of thousands of devas in the sky<br>Made nonhuman offerings to the Jina. {9}

When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold,<br>Hundreds [n445] of bulls [n446] lowed with joy.<br>The kings of horses and elephants [n447] raised their bodies;<br>The lions, the kings of animals, roared. {10}

The kings, the rulers, however many there were,<br>Came from the cardinal and intermediate directions.<br>When they saw the glorious majesty of the Jina,<br>With minds filled with joy they bowed to him. {11}

Some praised the Lord of the World;<br>Some scattered a rain of flowers on the Jina;<br>Some placed their ten fingers together in homage,<br>And they cried, “Oh, the Jina, compassionate one!” {12}

Some scattered excellent strings of pearls<br>And various ornaments that give rise to joy,<br>And some scattered clothing and jewels.<br>They developed the supreme, unequaled aspiration to enlightenment. {13} ^F35b

Some scattered excellent meshes of gold;<br>Some also scattered mukhaphullaka adornments.<br>Some scattered excellent ornaments of gold,<br>And some, likewise, scattered anklets. [n448] {14}

Some scattered excellent bracelets, [n449]<br>Some scattered armlets inset with jewels,<br>And some aspired to enlightenment, scattering excellent<br>Pieces of cloth, [n450] saying, “May we become buddhas!” {15}

When the Lord of the World stood in the gateway,<br>Some people scattered golden necklaces.<br>Some with minds filled with faith scattered excellent crest jewels; [n451]<br>Some scattered networks of jewels. {16}

Those beings who were in extreme suffering,<br>Tormented by many kinds of miseries,<br>All attained happiness through the majesty<br>Of the Guide, the supreme human. {17}

Cuckoos, mynas, and peacocks,<br>And similarly cranes and other water birds [n452]—<br>All the flocks of birds were in the sky<br>Emitting their beautiful, perfect songs. {18}

Desire, anger, and ignorance<br>Ceased in whoever heard<br>The sweet, beautiful songs<br>Of those flocks of joyous birds. {19}

The millions of beings who heard that joyful sound<br>All attained the patience that is concordant with the Dharma.<br>The Sugata gave them all this prophecy:<br>“You will in the future become buddhas.” {20}

At that time the kleśas did not arise,<br>And everyone was respectful to the Dharma king. [n453] {21}

At that time, when they saw the form of the Guide’s body, [n454]<br>They developed the aspiration for the supreme wisdom of buddhahood.<br>They wondered, “When will we attain this kind of wisdom?”<br>And the Jina, knowing that, gave them their prophecies. {22}

From each pore of the Sugata<br>There shone hundreds of thousands of light rays<br>And more, as many as there are sand grains in the Ganges—<br>It would not be possible to perceive all their attributes. {23}

At that time, the sunlight did not shine.<br>Nor was there light from jewels, fire, or the devas.<br>There was no other light at that time<br>When there was the splendor of the Buddha entering the city. {24} ^F36a

When with that great assembly the Sugata proceeded on the path,<br>Wherever the feet of the one with the ten strengths trod<br>There appeared from the ground a hundred thousand lotuses<br>That were pure and had ten thousand million petals. {25}

When the Guide entered the supreme city,<br>At that time there was no dirt or refuse.<br>Throughout the entire city there arose<br>The lovely aroma of the most fragrant incense. {26}

The entire city and its streets were purified.<br>They had no stones or gravel and were sprinkled with perfume<br>And bestrewn with the petals of various kinds of flowers.<br>That is the kind of merit the one with ten strengths had. {27}

When a hundred thousand yakṣas with ferocious minds<br>Saw the Buddha, the Lord of men who was like gold,<br>They felt an immense love for the Guide<br>And took refuge in the Buddha, Dharma, and Saṅgha. {28}

All of the million millions [n455] of devas<br>Who had come to see the Lord of men [n456]<br>Let fall a rain of flowers on the Sugata.<br>They scattered flowers while in the middle of the sky. {29}

The flowers scattered by humans for the Jina<br>Formed a parasol of flowers in the sky.<br>The flowers scattered by the devas<br>Were strewn on the ground as divine flowers. {30}

The devas, humans, kumbhāṇḍas, and rākṣasas<br>Never tired of gazing upon him.<br>When they saw the Lord [n457] with the ten strengths,<br>They were overjoyed and felt the highest delight. {31}

When they saw the body of the supreme being,<br>All beings were overjoyed and delighted;<br>They did not even think of the divine flowers,<br>Which did not seem at all wonderful. [n458] {32}

Brahmā upon the right of the one with ten strengths,<br>Śakra, the king of the devas, on his left,<br>And the many millions of deities in the middle of the sky<br>Showed great veneration to the supreme being. {33}

Devas and asuras encircled the Jina,<br>Who eclipsed all the majesty of devas and humans.<br>With the soles of his feet making patterns on the ground,<br>The invited Bhagavān entered into the city. {34}

His body was beautified by excellent primary signs,<br>Like the firmament filled with stars.<br>The Buddha shone upon the king’s road [n459]<br>Like the full moon in the sky. {35} ^F36b

Just as an excellent, pure, precious jewel<br>That is free of all impurities shines<br>So that a pure light goes in all directions, [n460]<br>In that way the Jina illuminated the entire world. {36}

Devas and asuras encircled the Jina.<br>The supreme human who entered Rājagṛha<br>With the soles of his feet leaving patterns on the ground,<br>The Buddha, came to the home of the youth Candraprabha. {37}

The supreme city was perfectly adorned,<br>Millions of banners had been erected,<br>The entire ground was anointed with the best perfumes,<br>And beautiful summer flowers were scattered. {38}

When the Sugata spoke to teach<br>With compassion for the people in the streets,<br>The Jina manifested emanations<br>That taught to them the excellent Dharma of the Buddha. {39}

[The Jina manifested emanations;<br>Bodies that were like gold were manifested.<br>The Buddha, the Jina, through his emanations,<br>Remained in emptiness, peace, the enlightenment of buddhahood.] [n461] {40}

When the hundreds of thousands of beings heard that,<br>They prayed for the supreme wisdom of the Buddha,<br>Wondering, “When will I attain this kind of wisdom?”<br>Knowing their thoughts, the Jina prophesied to them.  [n462]{41}

There were those who aspired to attain<br>That inconceivable supreme attainment.<br>They had invited the Jina, the Lord of men,<br>And there was no limit to the offerings they made.  [n463] {42}

There were those who developed an excellent aspiration,<br>Thinking, “I will tomorrow invite the compassionate one,<br>He who wishes to benefit beings,<br>Whom it is difficult to see in saṃsāra.” [n464] {43}

Some who were upon the roofs<br>Developed the sublime, supreme aspiration to enlightenment<br>And they scattered divine flowers on the handsome,<br>Beautifully adorned body of the one with the ten strengths. {44}

Some developed the supreme, highest aspiration<br>And scattered garlands of magnolias,<br>Kachnar flowers, the scents of summer,<br>And wreaths of silken ribbons. {45}

Some stood, holding excellent flowers,<br>Their bodies perfectly beautified by their raiment.<br>They held various flowers and wreaths of silk<br>That they cast in the direction of the Jina with great power. [n465] {46}

Some scattered red lotuses, night lotuses,<br>Blue lotuses, and excellent golden flowers.<br>Some scattered precious flowers, [n466]<br>And some scattered sandalwood powder. {47} ^F37a

When the Guide entered the supreme city<br>The wonders that appeared were uncountable,<br>Unequaled, impossible to describe,<br>And they brought many millions of beings to buddha wisdom. {48}

Those in Avṛha, Atapa, who had seen the truth,<br>The devas of Sudṛśa and Sudarśana,<br>And those in Akaniṣṭha, who are free of desire—<br>They all came to see the Lord of humans. {49}

Similarly, countless Parī­ttaśubha [n467] devas,<br>Apramāṇaśubha [n468] devas, filled with joy,<br>And countless millions of Śubhakṛtsna devas<br>Came to see the Guide, the great Rishi. {50}

Countless Apramāṇābha devas,<br>And similarly the Parī­ttābha devas,<br>And countless millions of Ābhāsvara devas<br>Came to see the Lord of the World. [n469] {51}

Many hundreds of thousands of Brahmā’s entourage, [n470]<br>And similarly the faithful Brahmapurohita devas<br>And many hundreds of Brahmakāyika devas,<br>All came so as to see the Guide. {52}

Also the Para­nirmita­vaśa­vartin [n471] devas,<br>And the pure beings who dwell in Nirmāṇaratin,<br>And the joyful devas of Tuṣita and Yāma<br>All came to pay homage to the Buddha. {53}

Śakra, king of the devas, and the Trāyastriṃśa [n472] devas  [n473]<br>Came with hundreds of millions of apsarases<br>And they sent down a rain of flowers,<br>Having come to see the Buddha, the Lord of sages. {54}

Also the world guardians of the four directions<br>Vaiśravaṇa, Dhṛtarāṣṭra the nāga king, [n474]<br>Virūḍhaka, and Virūpākṣa, their minds filled with joy,<br>All came in order to praise the Lord of men. {55}

Ailavila, the powerful king of the yakṣas,<br>With a delighted mind and encircled by a hundred yakṣas,<br>Was in the middle of the sky and joyfully<br>They sent down a rain of numerous various flowers. {56}

Also the Sadāmatta [n475] and Mālādhāra devas,<br>Holding various kinds of incense and flowers,<br>With their retinues, all joyful,<br>Made offerings there to the supreme individual. {57} ^F37b

Also numerous Karoṭapāṇi yakṣas<br>And adorned yakṣa maidens<br>Made offerings to the Buddha<br>With hundreds of compositions of<br>The beautiful, melodious music of the yakṣas. {58}

Druma, the king of the kinnaras,<br>With thousands of kinnara maidens skilled<br>In sweet and melodious songs and music,<br>Arrived from Gandhamādana to make offerings to the supreme Jina. {59}

Śambara, Bala, Vemacitra, and Rāhu,<br>Together with an entourage of thousands of asura maidens,<br>And together with crowds of other powerful asuras,<br>Came and sent down a rain of jewels. {60}

From countless trillions of rākṣasas<br>A thousand million rākṣasas honored him.<br>They respectfully scattered a multitude of various<br>Flower petals upon the supreme individual.  [n476] {61}

The nāga king Girivalgu,<br>With a great entourage came before the Tathāgata,<br>Holding great numbers of perfect, precious flowers,<br>And bowed down at the Sugata’s feet. [n477] {i}

The nāga lords Padma and Mahāpadma,<br>And also Vāsuki, Ananta, and Phanaka, [n478]<br>Came before the great leader<br>And respectfully bowed to the Sugata. {ii}

The nāga king Maṇi, filled with joy,<br>Came before the feet of the great leader<br>Holding fragrant, perfect nāga flowers<br>And sat before the Sugata at no great distance. {iii}

Also the nāga king Anavatapta,<br>With perfectly trained nāga maidens<br>Playing a hundred thousand musical instruments and drums,<br>Came and made offerings there to the Lord of the World. {62}

The five hundred sons of Anavatapta,<br>Encircled by their kindred and filled with joy,<br>Seeking the highest, vast wisdom,<br>Came to make offerings to the self-arisen one. {63}

Similarly, the nāga king Apalāla,<br>Palms together, bowed to the supreme individual<br>Holding beautiful, excellent nāga pearls.<br>He remained in the sky, making offerings to the king of sages. {64}

Similarly, the nāga king Mucilinda,<br>With great happiness and filled with joy,<br>Holding various jewels and pearls,<br>Came and scattered them for the Guide. {65} ^F38a

Similarly, the nāga king Kālika<br>Came before the Tathāgata.<br>Joyful and holding perfect, beautiful strings of jewels,<br>He made offerings to the supreme individual. [n479] {66}

He [n480] felt great veneration as he thought<br>Of the qualities of the Tathāgata.<br>Encircled by his many nāga kindred,<br>He recited many praises of the Guide. {67}

Similarly, the nāga kings Nanda and Upananda—<br>Similarly, also, Takṣaka and Kṛṣṇagautama—<br>Came there gazing upon the Jina<br>And bowed down to the Sugata’s feet. {68}

The nāga king Elapatra<br>Came weeping, encircled by a hundred nāgas.<br>He remembered the supreme sage Jina Kāśyapa<br>And saw what an unfavorable rebirth he himself had obtained. {69}

“Alas! I had doubts in the past.<br>In the past I cut down an elapatra [n481] bush, [n482]<br>And therefore I obtained this unfavorable rebirth.<br>It is not easy to know the Dharma of the Jina. {70}

“I forsake this rebirth into a nāgī’s womb,<br>And this birth in an extremely detestable body.<br>I will realize the Dharma, the state of peace,<br>That the best of men realized in the Bodhimaṇḍa.” {71}

Sāgara, the nāga cakravartin king,<br>Accompanied by an entourage of thirty million nāgas,<br>And the majestic Varuṇa, holding necklaces of jewels,<br>Came in order to make offerings to the Bhagavān. [n483] {72}

The yakṣa of Rājagṛha who caught<br>While he was in the sky<br>The rock thrown at the Buddha<br>Was respectfully present before the Sugata. {73}

The entire domain of the king of Alakavatī [n484]<br>Became empty, with no yakṣa remaining there.<br>They had all promised each other<br>To come and see the Lord of the World. {74}

In the same way, Kharakarṇa and Sūciromā,<br>The terrifying yakṣas of the forests,<br>And the yakṣa Gardabhaka, who lives in the snow mountains,<br>Had come into the presence of the self-arisen Jina. [n485] {75}

Indraketu, Vikaṭa, and Surūpa,<br>Bakula, Pañcika, and Śākyavardhana, [n486]<br>And a thousand other yakṣa lords<br>Came holding censers of incense. [n487] {76} ^F38b

Many with ugly, misshapen bodies,<br>Many kinds of bodies, destitute of adornment,<br>In their hundreds of thousands<br>Came into his presence, holding yakṣa flowers. {77}

Gautama, Rishi Bṛhaspati, and Jahnu,<br>Kauśika, Kāśyapa, and Markandeya,<br>Viśvāmitra, Parāśara, and Gargā,<br>They all came to pay homage to the Buddha. {i}

And similarly, there were the joyous and enraptured Nārada,<br>And the rishis Vyāsa, Kutsa, and Aṅgiras,<br>And Manu, Bhṛgu, Vātsyāyana, and Vaśiṣṭha,<br>Who came to pay homage to the Buddha. {ii}

Jaimini, Vāmana, [n488] and Vaiśampāyana,<br>Jamadagni and supreme rishi Vālmīki,<br>Durvāsa, and also Cyavana<br>Came to the supreme city to see the Guide. {iii}

When they saw the Rishi, the rishis were overjoyed<br>And they bowed down to the feet of the king of sages.<br>They paid homage to the lamp of the world and praised him,<br>Standing before the Hero with palms placed together. {iv}

The entire multitude of rishis in the world<br>Came in order to see the Lord of men.<br>When they saw him they made vast offerings<br>And stood before him with palms placed together. {v}

The garuḍas that live at the ocean’s shore<br>Came, having transformed into the appearance of brahmins.<br>Holding various beautiful kinds of crowns<br>And positioned in the sky, they paid homage to the Sugata. {78}

All of the devas that dwell in Jambudvīpa,<br>Whether in hundreds of towns or in its forests,<br>And all the goddesses of the towns<br>Came and made offerings to the Lord. {79}

The countless devas of the forests<br>And all the mountain devas came,<br>And also the countless devas of rivers [n489]<br>Arrived to make offerings to the Guide. {80}

The hundreds of devas of desert wildernesses,<br>All the devas of mountain peaks,<br>The devas of lakes, springs, and ponds,<br>And the devas of the ocean came into the Buddha’s presence. {81}

Assemblies of devas, asuras, and nāgas,<br>Yakṣas, kinnaras, mahoragas, and garuḍas,<br>And similarly, a multitude of pretas and pūtanas<br>Showed their respect to the supreme being. {82} ^F39a

They made offerings to the supreme Jina<br>When the Guide entered the supreme city.<br>The kings of the devas, asuras, nāgas, and yakṣas<br>Could not get their fill of looking at him. {83}

In previous existences the Lord of the World<br>Had made perfect offerings to the jinas of the past.<br>This was the ripened result of that merit.<br>The beings could not stop looking at the Lord of humans. {84}

When the Jina shone light through the buddha realm,<br>Meru, and similarly Sumeru and Cakravāla<br>The Himagiri and Gandhamādana<br>Could not obscure the Jina’s light. {85}

All of the oceans in this buddha realm<br>At that time all became land,<br>And the entirety of this buddha realm<br>Became equally scattered with flowers. {86}

Countless hundreds of thousands of light rays<br>Came from the soles of the King of Dharma’s feet.<br>All the beings in the hells were cooled<br>And, freed from suffering, experienced happiness. {87}

The one with the ten strengths taught the Dharma<br>So that the sight of devas and humans was purified.<br>Countless hundreds of thousands of beings<br>All gained certainty in the Buddha’s wisdom. {88}

The numerous miracles manifested by the Sugata<br>Could not easily be described in ten million eons.<br>When the Guide entered the supreme city<br>All beings rejoiced at the Jina, the Sugata. [n490] {89}

These qualities of the Sugata are immeasurable.<br>They are the supreme human’s perfection of qualities.<br>They have transcended all unique qualities.<br>Bow your heads to the realm of the Buddha’s merit! {90}

The Bhagavān came to the street on which was the home of the youth Candraprabha, and soon arrived at the home of the youth Candraprabha. Once he had arrived, he sat on the seat prepared for him. The saṅgha of bodhisattvas and the saṅgha of bhikṣus also sat on the appropriate seats that had been arranged for each of them.

Then the youth Candraprabha, knowing that the Bhagavān, the saṅgha of bodhisattvas, and the saṅgha of bhikṣus were seated,  himself presented and served a series of great offerings: numerous excellent foods, with hundreds of flavors to savor as they chewed, licked, sucked, and drank. ^F39b

When he saw that the Bhagavān had concluded his meal, which was signaled by his setting down his alms bowl, [n491] he offered for the Bhagavān’s body two lengths of cloth [n492] of the value of a trillion silver coins, [n493] and also to each of the bodhisattvas, and he offered three dharma robes to each one in the saṅgha of bhikṣus.

Then the youth Candraprabha rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder and, casting toward the Bhagavān a divine coral tree flower, he made offerings and uttered praises. Then, his palms placed together, he bowed toward the Bhagavān and praised him with these appropriate verses: [n494]

“You are unborn and unceasing;<br>Without a body, inconceivable,<br>You have the perfect body and primary signs.<br>I pay homage to you who are an ocean of qualities. {i}

“You are a hero who has been born from wisdom.<br>You possess the power of methods and strengths.<br>You are a buddha who is the same as space.<br>I pay homage to you who have perfected patience. {ii}

“Your conduct is to remain in constant mindfulness.<br>The Tathāgata’s bed is joy and happiness.<br>Your drink is samādhi and your food is supreme dhyāna.<br>I pay homage to you who reside in the solitude of emptiness. {iii}

“O Inconceivable Buddha,<br>The Guide for the whole world!<br>When the beings of this world make offerings to you<br>They advance toward supreme nirvāṇa.” {iv}

Thus did he praise the one unequaled Lord, and then the youth said, with a joyous mind, “Unequaled Buddha, who has an inconceivable body, you have consumed the meal. Through this may I also become a buddha like you, the god of gods!” ^F40a

In that way, therefore, the youth Candraprabha provided divine food with a hundred flavors to the Bhagavān. He offered divine coral tree flowers to the Bhagavān, and praised him with appropriate verses.

Now, placing his palms together in homage toward the Bhagavān, in his mind he addressed him with these verses:

“Whatever the wise bodhisattvas do,<br>They always follow the nature of the Dharma.<br>I pray to the Guide to teach what actions are performed<br>When those with wisdom engage in actions. {1}

“In what way, Guide, are past lives remembered?<br>In what way is rebirth in a womb avoided?<br>In what way does the community not become divided?<br>In what way does one gain endless eloquence? {2}

“You know the activities of all beings.<br>You have the knowledge of all phenomena.<br>You are the invincible, supreme human.<br>I have asked my questions; give me your elucidation. {3}

“You know that nonexistence is the nature of phenomena;<br>You put into words that which cannot be described.<br>Just as a lion overpowers all jackals, [n495]<br>That is how the Buddha overpowers the tīrthikas. {4}

“You know the conduct of all beings.<br>You have the wisdom of all phenomena.<br>You have wisdom without attachment, and activity that is pure.<br>Lord of the Dharma, elucidate those for me. {5}

“You know the past and also the future.<br>You also know what is happening in the present.<br>You have unimpeded knowledge of the three times.<br>Therefore I have asked you my questions, lion of the Śākyas. {6}

“You, Dharma king, know the true nature<br>That is the nature of the jinas of the three times.<br>You are skilled in the nature of phenomena, self-arisen one.<br>Therefore, ocean of wisdom, I have asked you my questions. {7}

“You do not have any quality of error.<br>Therefore you have a mind of complete elimination—<br>You have eliminated the fetters and the rigidity of ignorance.<br>Lord of humans, teach me the conduct of a bodhisattva. {8}

“You, Jina, know the characteristics of phenomena.<br>Teach me the characteristics of phenomena.<br>When I have understood those characteristics of phenomena<br>I shall practice the conduct of enlightenment that has those characteristics. {9} ^F40b

“The conduct of beings is infinitely different.<br>How do they engage in practicing their conduct?<br>Teach to me how conduct is engaged in<br>So that from your words, I may know the conduct of beings. {10}

“Different characteristics are characteristic of the nature of phenomena.<br>Their essence [n496] is empty and their nature [n497] is pure.<br>I pray that you teach me the way of phenomena<br>That a bodhisattva directly perceives. {11}

“In this there is the perfect knowledge of all phenomena.<br>There is skill in all the words of the teaching.<br>There is no doubt; all doubt and uncertainty have been cut through.<br>Teach me the enlightenment of buddhahood.” {12}

The Bhagavān, knowing the thoughts that were in the mind of the youth Candraprabha, said to him, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas will attain all these qualities, and they will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, if they possess just one quality. What is that one quality? Young man, it is when the bodhisattva mahāsattvas know the nature of all phenomena.

“Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas know the nature of all phenomena? Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas know that all phenomena are nameless; they have no names. They know that all phenomena have no vocalization, they have no expression in speech, they have no letters, they have no birth, they have no cessation, they have no characteristics of cause, they have no characteristics of conditions, [n498] they are devoid of characteristics, they have the one characteristic of having no characteristics, they are devoid of attributes, they cannot be conceived of, they have no thought, and they have no mentality.”

Then the Bhagavān taught this in the following verses:

“The single teaching on phenomena<br>Is that phenomena have no characteristics.<br>That is the teaching of supreme wisdom<br>From having true, correct knowledge. {13} ^F41a

“The bodhisattvas who know<br>That teaching on phenomena<br>Will not cease from elucidation [n499]<br>Even though they teach ten million sūtras. {14}

“Through the blessing of the Guide<br>The ultimate truth is known.<br>When the ultimate is known<br>There is nothing to be taught. {15}

“Through one thing, everything is known.<br>Through one thing, everything is seen.<br>However much they teach<br>They will not become proud. {16}

“With their minds they have ascertained<br>The selflessness of all phenomena,<br>And as they are trained in teaching using terms,<br>They speak with words that are correct. {17}

“Whatever sound they hear,<br>They know its past. [n500]<br>Knowing the past [n501] of that sound<br>They are not captivated [n502] by that sound. {18}

“Just like the past [n503] of a sound,<br>So are the characteristics of phenomena.<br>Knowing phenomena to be like that<br>They will not be reborn in a womb. {19}

“They know that all phenomena are unborn<br>And that they have no origin.<br>Knowing this teaching on birth [n504]<br>They always remember their previous lives. {20}

“When they remember those lives<br>They perform their actions.<br>For those who perform those actions<br>Their community of followers remains united. {21}

“The bodhisattvas who know<br>The emptiness of phenomena<br>Will never be without that knowledge.<br>It is the summit of nothingness. {22}
