“When the foolish think about<br>The summit of nothingness<br>They continue in saṃsāra<br>For millions of eons. {23}

“If they are able to understand it<br>Just as the Guide knows it,<br>Then they will have no suffering<br>And they will not go to the lower realms. {24}

“All ordinary individuals<br>Are ignorant of this nature.<br>They reject this kind of Dharma<br>That brings the cessation of suffering. [n505] {25}

“Phenomena are perceived when<br>No phenomena can be found.<br>Recognize that perception<br>When that perception occurs. {26}

“The foolish conceptualize<br>Through consciousness and perception.<br>The wise do not become ignorant<br>In conceiving of phenomena. {27} ^F41b

“The unpolluted phenomena of emptiness<br>Are within the field of experience of the bodhisattvas. [n506]<br>This level of those who are wise<br>Is not within the field of experience of the foolish. {28}

“This level of the bodhisattvas<br>Is that of bodhisattva practice.<br>It is the adornment of the Buddha’s Dharma.<br>It is the peace and emptiness that has been taught. {29}

“When the bodhisattvas<br>Eliminate their propensities<br>They remain in the family of the buddhas<br>And are not captured by form. {30}

“All phenomena are without location;<br>They have no location that can be known.<br>For the one who knows this about their location,<br>Enlightenment is not difficult to attain. {31}

“Generosity, conduct, learning, and patience,<br>And relying upon a good friend: [n507]<br>Those who know these activities<br>Will quickly attain enlightenment. {32}

“Devas, nāgas, yakṣas, and asuras,<br>Mahoragas and gandharvas, will always honor them.<br>All the kings of the garuḍas, kinnaras,<br>And rākṣasas  [n508] will make offerings to them. {33}

“Millions of buddhas will recite their praises<br>Continuously for many millions of eons.<br>It is not possible to reach the end<br>Of such praise for one who teaches this Dharma. {34}

“The bodhisattvas who know emptiness<br>Benefit many millions of beings.<br>They kindly teach the Dharma to assemblies [n509]<br>And those who hear it are delighted and respectful.{35}

“They gain vast knowledge<br>So that they see the supreme humans.<br>They see the beautiful display of their realms<br>And the lords of the worlds teach them the Dharma. [n510] {36}

“Know that all phenomena are like illusions;<br>Know that just as space is naturally empty,<br>Phenomena are also naturally like that.<br>In that way there will be no attachment in any kind of activity. {37}

“With unimpeded wisdom, benefiting others,<br>Performing supreme bodhisattva conduct in the world,<br>With wisdom examining all phenomena,<br>They send emanations to other realms. {38}

“Those emanations accomplish buddha activities.<br>They go naturally, just as is their nature.<br>The beings who remain in the aspiration to enlightenment<br>Will attain whatever goals they wish for. {39} ^F42a

“Those who are steadfastly within the buddha family<br>Will always honor the buddhas.<br>Their bodies will shine brightly,<br>Adorned by the thirty-two excellent signs. {40}

“They will attain the conduct that is within the supreme samādhi<br>And an endless multitude of other benefits.<br>They will always have great, unshakable strength<br>And a majesty that outshines that of kings. {41}

“The wise who practice the Buddha’s Dharma<br>Will have an excellent appearance and great beauty.<br>Their merit and majesty and splendor will increase.<br>Their majesty will outshine even that of the devas. {42}

“Those who steadfastly remain in the aspiration to enlightenment<br>Will always be friends to all beings.<br>There will never be any darkness<br>In their teaching of the enlightenment of buddhahood. {43}

“The nature of phenomena is like that of space,<br>Inexpressible, beyond speech and words.<br>Those who know that supreme nature<br>Will have an unceasing confidence in teaching. {44}

“Even though they teach a hundred thousand sūtras,<br>They know the finest details of the past.<br>The wise will always have unimpeded speech,<br>Knowing the subtlety of the nature of phenomena. {45}

“They will be skilled [n511] in hundreds of ways.<br>They will have mastered the many kinds of words and definitions.<br>They have certainty in the ripening [n512] of actions and results.<br>They become distinctively preeminent in that way. {46}

“They will possess unimpaired power.<br>They are great wise ones, the heirs of those with the ten strengths.<br>Knowing the subtle nature of phenomena,<br>They will always have a completely pure memory. [n513] {47}

“Because they know the subtle nature of phenomena,<br>They will never hear an unpleasant sound.<br>They always hear pleasant and melodious sounds<br>And their words are always pleasant. {48}

“Because they know the very subtle nature of phenomena,<br>They have memory, understanding, wisdom, and realization.<br>Similarly, their minds are clear and unpolluted<br>And they teach many hundreds of sūtras. {49}

“They are learned in the categories of letters and words.<br>They know many different kinds of sounds,<br>And they are skilled in meanings and letters.<br>They have these qualities through knowing the nature of phenomena. {50} ^F42b

“Because they know the subtle nature of phenomena<br>They are always attractive and charming<br>To devas, humans, nāgas, [n514] and rākṣasas,<br>Asuras, mahoragas, and kinnaras. {51}

“Because they know the subtle nature of phenomena<br>They never perceive as frightening<br>The extremely terrible and flesh-devouring<br>Crowds of spirits, pretas, and rākṣasas. {52}

“Those who hear the vast [n515] teaching of the wise<br>Experience vast joy and their hairs stand on end.<br>They develop a vast attraction to the buddhas,<br>And gain a vast, inconceivable benefit. [n516] {53}

“Even by speaking for many thousands of eons<br>It is not possible to describe the power of the merit<br>That comes from memorizing this Dharma treasure of the sugatas.<br>It is immeasurable, infinite, and unquantifiable. {54}

“The jinas to whom offerings have been made in the past,<br>The countless buddhas of the future,<br>And the buddhas who are present in the ten directions,<br>Are so by having memorized this supreme samādhi of peace. {55}

“If a person who wishes for merit,<br>With immeasurable affection for them<br>Serves compassionate ones with the ten strengths<br>For countless endless millions of eons, {56}

“And if a second person who wishes for merit<br>Memorizes, during future times,<br>One verse from this way of the ultimate truth,<br>Then the previous person’s merit will not even be a fraction of that. {57}

“This will be the supreme offering to the buddhas.<br>During the future dreadful times<br>Hearing one of these four-line verses<br>And memorizing it will be an offering to all the buddhas. {58}

“They will always obtain the best provisions.<br>They will always eat the best alms of the land. [n517]<br>As the best senior heirs of the one with ten strengths,<br>They will for a long time make offerings to many jinas. {59}

“They will also see myself here on Vulture Peak Mountain.<br>And I, in buddha wisdom, will thus prophesy to them.<br>Also, after my passing away, there will be Maitreya, [n518]<br>Who at that time will also prophesy to them. {60}

“Similarly, Buddha Amitāyus also<br>Has taught many other kinds of benefits:<br>‘All will enter my Sukhāvatī,<br>And go to Abhirati and see Buddha Akṣobhya.’ [n519] {61} ^F43a

“For countless hundreds of thousands of eons<br>They will never have the fear of downfalls.<br>In this supreme practice of bodhisattva conduct<br>They will always experience happiness. {62}

“In that way it has been taught that this,<br>Which is preeminent, has the most excellent merit.<br>May I learn every single word,<br>And in future times be a keeper of this sūtra.” [n520] {63}

“Young man, those are the qualities and benefits that bodhisattvas who know the nature of all phenomena will have. They will describe the true, excellent qualities of the tathāgatas. They will not falsely say that which is untrue about the tathāgatas. Why is that? It is because they know perfectly that nature, which is the nature through which a tathāgata comes to be. [n521] They know the infinite qualities of a buddha. Why is that? Young man, the qualities of a buddha are infinite, inconceivable, beyond thought. They cannot be conceived or measured. Why is that? The mind, young man, is taught to be without a nature of its own, [n522] to be without form. [n523] Young man, that nature of the mind is also the nature of the qualities of a buddha. That nature of the qualities of a buddha is also the nature of the tathāgatas, and that is the nature of all phenomena.

“Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who know correctly that teaching on the nature of all the qualities are, young man, called bodhisattva mahāsattvas with profound comprehension. They are skilled in emancipation. They know perfectly emancipation from the three realms. They have perfect knowledge, do not teach that which is erroneous, and do not say that which is anything other than true.  Their conduct is in line with what they teach. They have no attachment to the three realms. They have transcended the three realms. They have transcended the level of desire, the level of form, the level of formlessness, the level of the kleśas, the level of names, and the level of language. They are skilled in the way of letters and words. They know freedom from letters. [n524] They have mastered the inexpressible Dharma. They know letters. They are skilled in letters. They are skilled in the knowledge of the categories of letters and words. They are skilled in the knowledge of the detailed categories of letters and words. They are skilled in the knowledge of the categories of all the words [n525] of the Dharma. They are skilled in the knowledge of the detailed categories of all the words [n526] of the Dharma. They are skilled in the knowledge [n527] of the presentation of all the Dharma. They are endowed with the certainty of understanding, so that all the evil māras and all the devas in their entourages cannot overcome them.” ^F43b

At that time, when this Dharma teaching was given, ninety-eight times a hundred thousand million devas and human beings who had created the karma in previous lifetimes, [n528] had accumulated [n529] a trillion retentions, [n530] were unobscured, and had insight into the Dharma, all attained patience. [n531] The Bhagavān prophesied to them all that after four million, eight hundred thousand countless eons they would attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. He prophesied to each of them their separate names, their identical lifespans, and the individual buddha realms where they would attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.

It was said:

“The wise bodhisattvas who seek to attain<br>The highest, supreme enlightenment,<br>Who are skilled in meaning and the Dharma,<br>Practice the nature of phenomena. {1}

“They say nothing that is untrue<br>About the unique qualities of the buddhas.<br>The heroes, free of all doubt,<br>Know the nature of the jinas. {2}

“They know that all phenomena have but a single meaning,<br>And that is solely emptiness.<br>They do not have different meanings.<br>They become adept in that single meaning. {3}

“The wise know that they are without thought,<br>Are devoid of thought, and that there is no object.<br>They have eliminated without remainder<br>Every conception of cessation and noncessation. {4} ^F44a

“They do not see the one with ten strengths as form,<br>But see the lion of men as the dharmakāya.<br>Neither do they conceive of attributes<br>Because they have eliminated all error. {5}

“The qualities are inconceivable, beyond thought.<br>They have the nature of complete peace.<br>With this knowledge they thus see<br>The buddhas as the supreme among humans. {6}

“Just as they know their own conceptions to be,<br>Thus they direct their understanding of everything.<br>All phenomena have that nature,<br>Which is as completely pure as space. [n532] {7}

“Nothing arises to their conceptual mind.<br>They know emancipation [n533] from all phenomena.<br>They are liberated from the three realms<br>And they have no aspiration for them. [n534] {8}

“They are those who see correctly and do not say<br>Anything to the contrary or any untrue words.<br>All the words that they speak<br>Come forth through the power of the jinas. {9}

“They transcend the level of desire,<br>And the levels of kleśas, form, and formlessness.<br>Their minds have no attachment to phenomena.<br>They practice with joy, benefiting beings. {10}

“They have transcended the level of words;<br>Their knowledge of language is obtained from its nature.<br>For however long they speak<br>They know those words have no basis. {11}

“There is no activity of conceptualization;<br>Incorrect views have completely ceased.<br>Their understanding is completely assured.<br>It has a stability like that of space. {12}

“Even though quintillions of māras<br>Come to disturb their mind,<br>They overcome all the māras<br>And do not fall under their power. {13}

“They have rejected the net of the māras.<br>They have pure, untroubled conduct.<br>They aspire to the bliss of dhyāna<br>And know the world to be empty. {14}

“Even though it is said the world is an aggregate,<br>They know it to be empty,<br>And that all phenomena are like space,<br>Without birth and without cessation. {15}

“They have forsaken the self, but not the conduct [n535]<br>Or listening to the teaching of the one with ten strengths. [n536]<br>They have attained perfect conduct<br>And will be reborn wherever they pray to be. {16} ^F44b

“They go to the buddha realms.<br>They see many millions of buddhas.<br>They have no desire for the deva realms<br>And they do not pray to be there. {17}

“While they are practicing the Dharma,<br>Their diligence does not waver for an instant.<br>They are highly praised by<br>The buddhas in the ten directions. {18}

“Therefore, young man, when you have received<br>This Dharma teaching of the samādhi,<br>Rejecting the profits of the intellect,<br>Teach this Dharma to the people. {19}

“One who wishes for the numerous qualities<br>Possessed by the self-arisen buddha<br>Should train in this goodness<br>And become a buddha with the ten strengths.” {20}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should be skilled in teaching this samādhi.

“Young man, what is the teaching of this samādhi? It is the true nature of all phenomena; it is equality; it is the absence of inequality; it is devoid of notions; it is devoid of concepts; it is devoid of creation; it is devoid of arising; it is devoid of production; it is devoid of cessation; it is the termination of notions, concepts, and assumptions; it is devoid of an object for the mind; it is devoid of a focus of the mind; [n537] it is the termination of designations; it is the termination of concepts from analysis; it is the termination of desire, anger, and ignorance; it is without a limited or limitless focus of the mind; it is the termination of any focus of the mind; it is the knowledge of the nature of the skandhas, dhātus, and āyatanas; it is the state of accomplishing the field of activity that is the performance of the conduct of mindfulness, understanding, comprehension, conscience, and stability; it is the level of freedom from corruptions; [n538] it is the level of peace; it is the termination of all conceptual elaboration; it is the training of all bodhisattvas; it is the field of activity of all tathāgatas;  and it is the perfection of all good qualities. ^F45a

“Young man, that is what the teaching of samādhi is said to be. Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are established in this teaching of samādhi become inseparable from samādhi—their minds become free of delusion, they become endowed with great compassion, and they accomplish the benefit of countless beings.”

Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:

“The level of unequaled samādhi [n539]<br>Is peaceful, subtle, and difficult to see.<br>All conceptions have been eliminated.<br>Therefore it is called samādhi. {1}

“There are no notions, there are no concepts,<br>There is nothing to be grasped, there is nothing to be shown,<br>And there is no object for the mind.<br>Therefore it is called samādhi. {2}

“When in a state of meditation<br>There is no pride concerning any phenomenon.<br>That very absence of pride—<br>That is what is called samādhi. {3}

“There does not exist [n540] even an atom of phenomena.<br>That which is called ‘an atom’ does not exist.<br>There are no phenomena as objects for the mind.<br>Therefore it is called samādhi. {4}

“ ‘The mind has no object’<br>Is also itself a concept.<br>When there are no concepts of phenomena,<br>Then that is known as samādhi. {5}

“A word indicates a meaning.<br>That word is not a thing.<br>A word is like an echo,<br>Like the space of the sky. {6}

“These phenomena are not present;<br>There is no presence to be perceived.<br>The nonpresence is through the word ‘presence.’<br>Its nature is that there is nothing to be found. {7}

“One says ‘going’ and ‘passing away,’<br>But that ‘going’ does not exist.<br>Through the word ‘going’ there is the absence of going.<br>That is given the name samādhi. {8}

“Saying ‘I am not meditating’ is called pride. [n541]<br>‘I am meditating’ is a second kind of pride. [n542]<br>Practicing for enlightenment without pride, [n543]<br>And attaining [n544] the absence of pride is the highest enlightenment. [n545] {9}

“This unequaled equality is the level of peace; [n546]<br>It is śamatha and vipaśyanā, [n547] devoid of attributes.<br>Relying upon this peace, the level of buddhahood,<br>Is engaging in the meditation [n548] of samādhi. {10}

“It is not possible through words to enter<br>Into the understanding of the meaning.<br>When all sounds and words are abandoned<br>There will be meditation without pride. {11} ^F45b

“When there is the fire of the eon’s end in this world<br>That fire does not burn the supreme mountain in its center,<br>Just like space that has never been burned in the past,<br>Even though the fire burns for many hundreds of eons. [n549] {12}

“The bodhisattvas who remain engaged<br>In this samādhi as it has been taught,<br>And know that phenomena are the same as space,<br>Will also not be burned by fire. [n550] {13}

“If the buddha realm were burning<br>And in this samādhi they prayed<br>For the burning to completely cease,<br>Though the earth was destroyed it would be unchanged. {14}

“They will have infinite miraculous powers.<br>They will travel through the air unimpeded.<br>The bodhisattvas will have these qualities<br>By remaining in samādhi just as they have been taught. {15}

“Though one is born and though one dies,<br>There is no birth and there is no death.<br>For the one who understands that<br>This samādhi will not be difficult to attain. {16}

“The Lord of the World has taught<br>That there is no death and there is no birth.<br>Just as the Lord of the World knew that,<br>You should also know it through this samādhi. {17}

“Unstained by the world,<br>They have no attachment to worldly phenomena.<br>With a body free of impediment<br>They go to the buddha realms. {18}

“They constantly see in those realms<br>The perfect buddhas, the guides of the world.<br>They listen there to the Dharma<br>That is taught in the realms of the buddhas. [n551] {19}

“They will never be in ignorance.<br>They will teach the essence of phenomena.<br>They always know the way of phenomena,<br>Which is composed [n552] of the essence of phenomena. {20}

“Even though they teach for ten million eons,<br>Their confidence in speech will not decline.<br>They emanate many other bodhisattvas<br>Who have wisdom. {21}

“The emanated bodhisattvas<br>Travel from realm to realm.<br>They are seated, cross-legged,<br>Upon lotuses that have a thousand petals. {22}

“They teach the enlightenment of buddhahood,<br>Wonderful dhāraṇīs and sūtras,<br>And ten million other sūtras,<br>While meditating peacefully in samādhi. {23} ^F46a

“They establish in irreversibility<br>Countless multitudes of beings,<br>And teach the enlightenment of buddhahood<br>Without their confidence in speech ever declining. {24}

“They go to a pinnacled hall<br>That is adorned with jewels<br>And scatter aromatic<br>Flowers upon the guides. {25}

“They also sprinkle scented<br>Powders upon the guides.<br>They all make vast offerings<br>In order to attain enlightenment. {26}

“Those countless qualities<br>Are the refuge of the bodhisattvas.<br>When they are free of kleśas<br>They attain those miraculous powers. {27}

“Because the kleśas are not created<br>They are clear, pure, and bright.<br>The field of activity of the bodhisattvas<br>Is noncomposite and inviolate. {28}

“They have perfect peace, complete peace;<br>They have no kleśas, and they have no misery. [n553]<br>They have no conceptualization, are free of conceptualization,<br>And have transcended conceptualization. {29}

“This characteristic of phenomena<br>Is beyond the scope of words. [n554]<br>It is difficult [n555] to know through language [n556]<br>And therefore it is called samādhi. {30}

“It is unending; it is complete peace;<br>It is effortless, and it cannot be shown.<br>The field of activity of all the buddhas<br>Is the completely pure summit of the truth. {31}

“The training of all the buddhas<br>Is in the nature of all phenomena.<br>The perfect buddhas, having trained in it,<br>Have reached the perfection of qualities. [n557] {32}

“Without any concepts of the past,<br>Of this side and the further side,<br>In that way all those buddhas<br>Have reached the perfection [n558] of qualities. {33}

“Knowing the nature of phenomena<br>As having no coming or going,<br>They have reached the perfection<br>That is nonconceptual and effortless.” {34}

Then the youth Candraprabha rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee,  with palms placed together he bowed toward the Bhagavān and said to him, [n559] “Bhagavān, it is marvelous that the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha has taught the equality that is the nature of all phenomena, which is the samādhi that all bodhisattvas train in. ^F46b

“Bhagavān, it was thus, in this training, that the Bhagavān trained for a long time, and accomplished the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. Bhagavān, that gives me confidence to speak. [n560] Sugata, it gives me confidence to speak.”

The Bhagavān said, “Young man, if you think the time has come, be confident to speak.”

Since the Bhagavān had granted the youth Candraprabha this opportunity, Candraprabha spoke the following verses of praise directly to the Bhagavān.

“You saw beings tormented by suffering, [n561]<br>Constantly overpowered by desire and anger,<br>And developed the aspiration to attain enlightenment:<br>‘May I become a buddha who liberates beings!’ {1}

“Hero, [n562] for many millions of eons, constantly,<br>You practiced generosity, self-restraint and self-control,<br>Patience, correct conduct, and similarly diligence,<br>And your acts of generosity were vast and infinite. {2}

“Without ever any sadness in your mind<br>You gave away your legs, arms, and even your life,<br>And similarly, without attachment you gave away<br>Gold, silver, sons, wives, and your kingdom. {3}

“Your conduct was stainless and pure.<br>You made a gift of yourself without ruining your conduct.<br>You controlled well your body, speech, and mind.<br>Sugata who has a self-restrained mind, I pay homage to you. {4}

“Delighting in patience, residing on the path of patience,<br>Even though your body was cut into pieces you were not angered; [n563]<br>Through your meditation on love, milk flowed from you.<br>Marvelous Sugata, I pay homage to you. {5}

“You possess the strength of the ten strengths.<br>With wisdom free of attachment you know all phenomena.<br>With compassion, Lord of Dharma, you benefit the world.<br>Through your kindness you wish to benefit beings. {6} ^F47a

“You know emptiness and that there are no such beings,<br>And likewise you see that the world’s beings have lost that path.<br>You have realized that the nature of phenomena is selfless<br>And that though you bring beings to liberation, there is no such liberation. {7}

“With discrimination you reject all carelessness.<br>You have conquered the infinite, powerful māras.<br>Enlightened at buddhahood, you have vast, infinite wisdom.<br>You teach the supreme Dharma of completely pure peace. {8}

“The sky with its moon and the stars may fall,<br>The earth with its mountains and towns may be destroyed,<br>The element of space may change into something else,<br>But you will never speak an untrue word. {9}

“You have seen the suffering of beings<br>Who take joy in the perception of objects.<br>You teach the profound peace, emptiness,<br>In which there is no perception of objects. {10}

“Great hero, you trained<br>For countless millions of eons<br>In the training of nonperception,<br>And so you are free of error. {11}

“Just as you have trained in the Dharma,<br>In that way you teach the Dharma.<br>Yours is not the level of foolish beings,<br>And neither is it the level of all the tīrthikas. {12}

“Those who have the conception of a self,<br>They are unwise beings who are in error.<br>You know that phenomena have no self,<br>And so you are free of any error. {13}

“You speak the truth, great hero;<br>You are established in the true Dharma.<br>Lord, you remain within truth, within veracity,<br>And you speak words that are true. {14}

“Your conduct has been true,<br>Just as you have prayed for.<br>You have the consequence of that true conduct<br>And you speak words that are true. {15}

“You have perfected true conduct.<br>You have trained in the summit of truth.<br>You have truly practiced with a true motivation.<br>I pay homage to you who have true wisdom. {16}

“There is no equal to your wisdom.<br>Your words of wisdom illuminate.<br>You have attained unique wisdom.<br>I pay homage to you who speak words of wisdom. {17}

“You have meditated on kindness<br>And become a friend to all beings.<br>You are as unshakable as Sumeru.<br>You are completely stable and unwavering. {18} ^F47b

“Teacher, your following is vast.<br>You have attracted these followers.<br>Sugata who has profound wisdom,<br>Make your voice resound within this assembly. {19}

“The voice of the Buddha is a lion’s roar.<br>You walk with the gait of a lion.<br>You defeat all the tīrthikas<br>Like a lion defeats jackals. {20}

“Hero who subdues the unsubdued,<br>The unsubdued are subdued by you.<br>They become friends who are reliable,<br>Inseparable, and pleasant to be with. {21}

“You see the beings who are suffering<br>Because they maintain the view of a self. [n564]<br>You teach the Dharma of no-self<br>In which there is neither like nor dislike. {22}

“The foolish who are untrained<br>Take up the wrong paths.<br>You show them the path<br>That the guides have followed. {23}

“Whoever holds to the concept of a self,<br>They will remain in suffering.<br>They do not know selflessness,<br>Within which there is no suffering. {24}

“You teach the Dharma with words that are without error.<br>Lord of the World, you make no error.<br>You are one who speaks words that are never incorrect.<br>I pay homage to you, who bring freedom from suffering. {25}

“In the sky there are many quintillions<br>Of devas, nāgas, and yakṣas.<br>They all feel joy in the Guide<br>When they hear the meaningful words of the Bhagavān. {26}

“Your words are mild, gentle, and pleasing,<br>Timely, melodious, appropriate, and beloved.<br>You have the countless qualities of speech<br>That benefit and bring liberation to many beings. {27}

“Countless hundreds of thousands of musical instruments<br>Are all played melodiously and simultaneously,<br>But the Sugata with one word eclipses them all<br>With his unique, divine, beloved voice. [n565] {28}

“Avadavats [n566] and flocks of birds [n567] with beautiful songs,<br>With their beautiful songs that are pleasing to everyone—<br>All of the songs of these many flocks of birds [n568]<br>Cannot equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech. {29} ^F48a

“Deva maidens with beautiful voices<br>And with melodious music and songs,<br>And the sound of lutes, paṭaha [n569] drums, bherī drums, [n570] and conches,<br>Cannot equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech. [n571] {i}

“The songs of cuckoos, parrots, and mynas,<br>Of cranes, peacocks, and kinnaras—<br>All these beautiful, melodious sounds<br>Cannot equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech. [n572] {30}

“Delightful, melodious, beautiful, enjoyable,<br>Exquisite, peaceful voices singing praises—<br>All such voices singing simultaneously<br>Are not as delightful as the Tathāgata’s perfect speech. {31}

“The light from all luminous beings,<br>From devas, [n573] humans, kings, and asuras, [n574]<br>And from all beings in the three existences,<br>Are eclipsed by one light ray from the Sugata. {32}

“The Sugata’s body is like a blossomed flower<br>With the various adornments of all the special signs.<br>A pure and clear accomplishment of hundreds of merits,<br>The body of the Jina shines on the entire world. {33}

“The sound of conches and of paṇavas, [n575]<br>And the sound of bherī drums [n576] and kimpalas [n577]—<br>All those beautiful and delightful sounds<br>Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. {34}

“The sounds of quintillions of musical instruments,<br>Clear and beautiful voices like those of the devas, [n578]<br>And the delightful voices of male and female devas [n579]<br>Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. [n580] {35}

“Flocks of a multitude of birds—cranes, peacocks,<br>Shelducks, cuckoos, geese, and snipe—<br>May simultaneously sing their songs, but they<br>Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. [n581] {36}

“The voices of nāgas, yakṣas, asuras, mahoragas,<br>Devendra, [n582] Brahmā, and the lords of the devas—<br>All the lovely and beautiful voices in the three existences<br>Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. {37}

“The light of Brahmā and lords of the devas,<br>The light of the sun and precious jewels,<br>The many different kinds of light—<br>All those lights are eclipsed by the brilliance of the Jina’s light. [n583] {38}

“Your body, speech, and mind are perfectly pure.<br>The purity of your wisdom is unstained by the three existences.<br>Lord of men, you have the wealth of qualities, precious qualities.<br>Self-arisen one, through all your qualities, you are without equal.” {39} ^F48b

In that way the youth spoke those words with great joy,<br>Praising the one with ten strengths, the speaker of truth.<br>He said, “By offering to the measureless, [n584] unquantifiable Buddha<br>May I also become a buddha like Śākyamuni!” {40}

Knowing his perfect conduct, the Sugata,<br>The Lord of humans, the one with wisdom free of attachment, smiled.<br>Maitreya, the senior son of the one with ten strengths, asked him,<br>“For what reason did the Guide smile? {41}

“The earth has shaken in six ways.<br>The devas and nāgas in the sky are filled with joy.<br>They are gazing at the Buddha with great delight and happiness.<br>I pray to the unconquerable Sugata that you elucidate this to them. {42}

“You have a supreme being’s wisdom,<br>Which is not the level of the Bhagavān’s śrāvakas.<br>You who have pure wisdom beyond examples, wise one,<br>Tell [n585] us the entire reason, Jina, why you smiled. [n586] {43}

“You are the Śākya lion, possessor of the ten strengths, the Guide,<br>The chief of humans, the one who has reached the perfection of wisdom. [n587]<br>You have eliminated intractable desire, anger, and ignorance.<br>To you who shine with intense light, I ask this question: {44}

“Seeking the supreme, highest enlightenment,<br>You, the Guide, practiced for millions of eons<br>As numerous as the grains of sand in the Ganges.<br>For what reason did you show a smile? {45}

“Seeking the supreme, highest enlightenment,<br>You, the Teacher, gave away your arms and legs.<br>You gave away sons, wives, companions, and relations.<br>Sage, for what reason did you show a smile? {46}

“You gave away horses, elephants, and chariots, [n588]<br>Slaves, jewels, silver, and pearls. [n589]<br>When you practiced the sublime conduct<br>There were no jewels or wealth that you did not give away. {47}

“You have the supreme wisdom in the three existences.<br>You know the conduct of all beings.<br>You are skilled in knowing their natures, minds, and aspirations.<br>For what reason did you smile? {48} ^F49a

“Who made the offering to you, best of men?<br>For whom has vast merit been created?<br>Who has gained that excellent conduct?<br>Sage, for what reason did you smile? {49}

“The earth has shaken in six ways.<br>Millions of lotuses have appeared on the ground. [n590]<br>They shine and have millions of excellent petals.<br>They are the color of gold, beautiful and delightful. {50}

“Present here are the heart sons of the Jina<br>Who show the greatest bodhisattva miracles.<br>Many [n591] dharmabhāṇakas have gathered here.<br>Guide, I ask my question for their sake. {51}

“The sound of bherī drums, [n592] conches, and gongs, [n593]<br>Of quintillions of instruments has resounded.<br>That music was heard coming from the sky,<br>But compared to that the Sugata’s speech is inconceivable. {52}

“Many flocks of birds have gathered,<br>Cranes, [n594] geese, avadavats, [n595] and cuckoos.<br>They have sung their perfect, beautiful songs,<br>But they do not equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech. {53}

“Who in the past with generosity, self-restraint, and self-control<br>Has served well for many millions of eons?<br>Who has made offerings to you, supreme among men?<br>For what reason did you smile? {54}

“Who in the past, having shown you the greatest veneration,<br>Asked you, supreme among men, the question,<br>‘How can I attain the enlightenment of buddhahood?’<br>For what reason did you smile? {55}

“Those with the ten strengths in the past,<br>The sugatas of the present and the future,<br>And you, supreme among men, know all.<br>Therefore for the benefit of beings I ask this question. {56}

“You know the thoughts in the minds of beings<br>And all beings’ infinite ways of conduct;<br>You know the aspirations that humans have.<br>Therefore I ask this question to you, supreme among men. {57}

“Those who are practicing the supreme conduct,<br>Who are adept in causes, reasons, and discipline,<br>They ask, ‘How does one attain the Buddha’s wisdom?’<br>Therefore, supreme human, I ask this question. {58}

“There are those who meditate on the field of experience of those with the ten strengths:<br>The subtle Dharma that is difficult to perceive,<br>And emptiness and peace that is unequaled and inconceivable.<br>For their sake, Guide, I ask you this question. {59} ^F49b

“Those who meditate on love and compassion<br>For all the countless beings in the world,<br>Without their having the concept of beings—<br>Supreme human, for their sake I ask this question. {60}

“Those who have inconceivable, unequaled wisdom,<br>They are never known to have any grasping.<br>They have reached the perfection of the mind’s field of activity.<br>Lord, it is for their sake that I ask this question. {61}

“You have reached the perfection of conduct and wisdom’s qualities.<br>You have unequaled knowledge of the three times.<br>You will never make an error.<br>For what reason did you smile? {62}

“Śāriputra, Aniruddha, and Kolita,<br>And the other śrāvakas of the Sugata,<br>Do not have that wisdom.<br>It is the unsurpassable field of activity of the buddhas. {63}

“You have reached the perfection of power over all phenomena.<br>You have ascended through the practice of the training.<br>Guide, you have developed compassion.<br>You who know the ultimate truth, release your voice! {64}

“You have had, in the past for many millions of eons,<br>The goal of being the ultimate refuge and protector,<br>And have inquired, supreme human, with just that intention;<br>Guide, tell us the result of that today. {65}

“Yakṣas, rākṣasas, kumbhāṇḍas, and guhyakas<br>Are gazing upon the supreme among humans.<br>They are all respectful, their palms together in homage,<br>In order to listen to the elucidation from the great being. {66}

“Many bodhisattvas with miraculous powers<br>Have come from millions of buddha realms.<br>These senior sons, born form the minds of the sugatas,<br>Are all respectfully present, their palms together in homage. {67}

“Gandhahasti with millions of bodhisattvas<br>Has come into your presence from the east,<br>From the famous world of Akṣobhya’s realm<br>For this question, Lion of the Śākyas, supreme human. {68}

“Avalokiteśvara and Mahā­sthāma­prāpta<br>Have come before you with millions of bodhisattvas<br>From the supreme realm of Sukhāvatī<br>For this question, Lion of the Śākyas, supreme human. {69} ^F50a

“In the past for many millions of eons<br>They have served countless sugatas<br>As numerous as the sand grains in all the oceans,<br>Seeking this supreme sublime wisdom. {70}

“Mañjughoṣa is present, his palms together in homage.<br>He has been praised and extolled by all the buddhas.<br>He has reached the perfection of all good qualities<br>And is renowned throughout the worlds in all directions. {71}

“They have practiced in millions of buddha realms.<br>It is very rare to see such beings.<br>They have the qualities of sons of the buddhas and excellent training,<br>And are all present, with their palms together respectfully in homage. {72}

“There is no one here other than worthy recipients.<br>That is what these wise ones [n596] are like,<br>The holders of the Dharma treasures of all teachers.<br>Guide, release your gentle speech. [n597] {73}

“The jinas, the guides, the supreme humans<br>Have never been seen to smile without a reason.<br>Grant us your supreme speech, which is like the beat of a drum.<br>What is the reason that we saw you smile? {74}

“The supreme beings resound like thunder, [n598]<br>Geese, cuckoos, peacocks, and swans, [n599]<br>And they emit the melodious music of the devas.<br>Liberator of beings, elucidate with your words. {75}

“You develop kindness, you increase joy,<br>You teach wisdom, you eliminate ignorance,<br>You realize the meaning, you expand wisdom,<br>And you have purified for quintillions of eons. {76}

“You have realized the nature of things with certainty,<br>You have taught the meaning in words that end suffering.<br>You have routed the teachings of all tīrthikas.<br>You meditate on emptiness, the absence of being, and the absence of a soul. {77}

“You are adorned by thousands of merits.<br>You have practiced with hundreds of thousands of buddhas,<br>Are praised by hundreds of thousands of devas,<br>And hundreds of thousands of Brahmās pay homage to you. {78}

“Yakṣas, rākṣasas, and kumbhāṇḍas have faith in you.<br>You have liberated nāgas, mahoragas, and garuḍas.<br>You are constantly without any attachment.<br>Speak the words [n600] that are the result of good actions. {79} ^F50b

“All the jinas that have passed into nirvāṇa,<br>Those who will live in the future, and those now present,<br>You know them all without impediment.<br>Guide, you are sublime because of all your qualities. {80}

“This earth that supports beings, with its mountains<br>And oceans, has been shaken in six ways.<br>The devas have thrown down flowers from the sky.<br>There has arisen the beautiful aroma of the incense of the devas. {81}

“Desire, anger, and darkness of the mind have been completely eliminated.<br>Conduct has become completely pure and the mind has become completely pure.<br>There is delight in complete peace, emptiness, and the absence of attributes.<br>There is the sound of the lion’s roar, the sound of the compassionate ones. {82}

“You have the confidence of speech, and great renown.<br>You have perfected wisdom, the wisdom of the jinas.<br>Compassionate one, there is no one like you in this world.<br>Tell us, for what reason did you smile? {83}

“The songs of peacocks, cuckoos, and avadavats,<br>And likewise the beautiful song of the partridge, [n601]<br>All those pleasant sounds simultaneously<br>Do not equal a fraction of the Sugata’s speech. {84}

“Bherī drums, mṛdaṅgas, and similarly paṇavas;<br>Conches, flutes, and similarly lutes:<br>The simultaneous sound of a thousand instruments<br>Does not equal a fraction of the Sugata’s speech. {85}

“The divine, sublime sound of thousands of instruments<br>And the beautiful songs of deva maidens,<br>The excellent songs that bring delightful sounds to the mind,<br>Do not equal a fraction of the Sugata’s speech. {86}

“With one sound you benefit the world<br>As it resounds to those with different aspirations,<br>Each person thinking, ‘The Jina is speaking to me.’<br>For what reason did you smile? {87}

“The music of the devas and the music of the nāgas,<br>And also the melodious music of the kinnaras,<br>Are never able to pacify the kleśas.<br>The Buddha’s speech always dispels the kleśas. {88}

“You create joy but not joy in desire.<br>You create love and not a mind of anger.<br>You create wisdom and not a mind of stupidity.<br>The Buddha’s speech eliminates all stains. {89} ^F51a

“The sound of your voice does not go beyond your followers.<br>It cuts through everyone’s hundreds of doubts.<br>It is never too quiet nor too loud.<br>The Sage’s voice teaches everyone equally and easily. {90}

“This earth with its mountains and forests may perish,<br>And so may the waters of the ocean.<br>The moon and the sun may fall to the earth,<br>But the Jina’s speech will never change. {91}

“Your voice has all the qualities of pure speech.<br>Your beautiful voice is a gentle lion’s roar.<br>Compassionate one, you have the voice of Brahmā.<br>For what reason did you smile? {92}

“You know the minds and conduct<br>Of all the beings in the world,<br>Those in the past, the future, and the present.<br>Tell us the reason why you smiled. {93}

“All of the jinas, the compassionate ones,<br>They who have reached the perfection of power and wisdom,<br>The jinas whose faces are like stainless moons,<br>Have never smiled without a reason. {94}

“If for millions of eons one were to describe your unequaled qualities,<br>Which are as numerous as the sands of the Ganges,<br>One would not be able to describe them fully.<br>Teach us the reason why you smiled.” [n602] {95}

At that time the Bhagavān spoke these appropriate verses to Bodhisattva Maitreya:

“This youth, Candraprabha,<br>Has praised the Buddha with unequaled joy.<br>He described the unique superior qualities of the buddhas.<br>All the time he is reciting their praises. [n603] {1}

“In this very city of Rājagṛha in the past<br>He has seen ten thousand million buddhas.<br>In the presence of all those jinas<br>He asked about this supreme samādhi of peace. {2}

“He has always been my son,<br>Practicing this supreme bodhisattva conduct.<br>He has always had the confidence of speech,<br>And always he has been practicing celibacy. {3} ^F51b

“In the very fearful future times<br>You, Ajita, will be my witness. [n604]<br>Always remaining in a state of celibacy,<br>He will make this samādhi widespread. {4}

“Those who seek entry into this sublime samādhi,<br>Through that path will attain enlightenment.<br>He will be adopted by many millions of buddhas<br>And he will make supreme offerings to those guides. {5}

“I prophesy that, remaining in wisdom,<br>Candraprabha’s conduct will be exceptional.<br>In the future times there will be no obstacle<br>To his celibacy or to his life. {6}

“He will know millions of buddhas as clearly<br>As five myrobalan plums in the palm of the hand.<br>And he will make offerings in the future to even more,<br>As numerous as sand grains in the Ganges. {7}

“Eight hundred million devas and nāgas,<br>And seven hundred billion yakṣas,<br>In future times will be zealous<br>And make offerings to the supreme among humans. {8}

“He will make offerings to the supreme human<br>And will practice this unsurpassable wisdom.<br>In a future time he will become a Lord of the World,<br>A jina by the name of Vimalaprabha.” [n605] {9}

The young man was overjoyed<br>On hearing this prophecy about himself.<br>Candraprabha floated up to the height of seven palm trees<br>And remaining in the sky he made this declaration: {10}

“O Jina, you who teach the supreme Dharma,<br>You have the power of a lord of liberating wisdom.<br>You remain in the certainty of supreme wisdom<br>And cannot be defeated by adversaries. {11}

“You have abandoned attachment and reached liberation.<br>You have no attachment to existence, which is devoid of things.<br>You have no conceptualization whatsoever.<br>You have the wisdom of nonattachment toward the three existences. {12}

“You are unstained by any conceptualization.<br>You are free of all conceptualized views.<br>You have meditated perfectly on the path that has no location.<br>You cannot be defeated or hindered [n606] by anyone. {13}

“You have no residence in the three realms.<br>You are free from the floods [n607] and the knots. [n608]<br>You have cut through the bondage of the creepers of craving. [n609]<br>You are free of existence and are devoid of existence. {14} ^F52a

“You know the nonexistence that is the nature of phenomena.<br>You make understood in words that which cannot be described.<br>Just as the lion destroys the jackal,<br>You defeat the unwise tīrthikas. {15}

“I have obtained today the highest treasure,<br>The treasure of the Dharma taught by the Sugata.<br>I am freed from falling into any of the lower existences.<br>I will never have doubts that you are my guide. {16}

“He placed upon my head his hand,<br>Which was shining, beautiful, the color of gold.<br>He gave me the consecration to be a supreme leader of humans,<br>With the world and its devas as witnesses.” {17}

The Bhagavān then said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas thus wish to liberate all beings from all the suffering of existence. They wish to establish beings in the noble, unsurpassable bliss and joy of samādhi. Therefore they should hear this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, obtain it, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others.

“Why is that? Young man, this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, causes one to transcend all lower existence and be freed from all illness.

“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas hear this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, obtain it, and meditate on it, then, young man,  those bodhisattva mahāsattvas liberate all beings from all the sufferings of existence. They will establish them in the noble, unsurpassable bliss and joy of samādhi, this samādhi will be quickly attained, and the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood will be quickly attained.” [n610] ^F52b

Thereupon the Bhagavān, in order to teach this meaning to Candraprabha, repeated what he had previously said by explaining it in the following verses.

“I remember that, as I was practicing in the past,<br>In the teaching of Sugata Siṃhadhvaja<br>There was a wise bhikṣu, a dharmabhāṇaka<br>Whose name was Brahmadatta. {1}

“At that time I was Prince Mati.<br>I was tormented by the pain of an illness.<br>The dharmabhāṇaka Brahmadatta<br>Became my teacher at that time. {2}

“More than five hundred physicians<br>Diligently sought to cure that illness,<br>But they were unable to cure me of my disease.<br>Everyone in my family was in suffering. {3}

“The bhikṣu heard about my illness,<br>And he came to me and asked about it.<br>Brahmadatta felt great pity for me,<br>And he taught me this supreme samādhi. {4}

“When I had heard this sublime samādhi<br>I experienced a noble, nonworldly joy.<br>I understood the essential nature of phenomena<br>And at that time I was healed of my disease. {5}

“That wise dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu was Dīpaṃkara<br>While he was practicing bodhisattva conduct,<br>And I was Prince Mati, who was freed from illness<br>Through the wisdom of the samādhi. {6}

“Therefore, young man, in the future<br>Remember past declines like that.<br>Tolerate the bad things the foolish will say<br>And keep and recite [n611] this samādhi. {7}

“In future time, there will be many bhikṣus<br>Who will be covetous, [n612] malicious, and without restraint. [n613]<br>They will enjoy bad actions and be attached to alms bowls and robes,<br>And they will reject completely this samādhi. {8} ^F53a

“They will be unstable, distracted by their senses, and envious,<br>Attached to families [n614] and desiring gain.<br>They will always be engaged in familiarity with them<br>And they will reject completely [n615] this samādhi. {9}

“They will strike with their hands and feet.<br>They will always engage in fun and play.<br>They will embrace each other and hold hands,<br>And will do other kinds of laypeople’s activities. [n616] {10}

“They will have the signs of inappropriate activity.<br>They will always desire the daughters of others. [n617]<br>They will be excited and captivated by bodies,<br>And roam through the villages, towns, and regions. {11}

“They will always be engaged in eating and drinking,<br>And similarly in dance, song, and music.<br>They will always be dedicated to buying and selling.<br>Attached to drinking, they will cast aside their shame. {12}

“They will carry letters, engaging in inappropriate activity,<br>And likewise discard correct conduct and the pure path. [n618]<br>They will break the rules through dwelling with families,<br>And having broken them continue engaging in incorrect conduct. {13} [n619]

“They will be fraudulent with weights and measures,<br>Always engaging in actions that the buddhas have rejected.<br>Through doing those actions that are sinful and defiled,<br>They will have bad karma and will go to the lower realms. {14}

“They will enter homelessness, forsaking home,<br>Conches, gold and jewels, and great wealth;<br>But having entered homelessness within the Buddha’s teaching,<br>They will continually engage in bad actions. {15}

“They will see wealth and grain as essential.<br>They will be attached to dairy cows, [n620] cattle, and carriages.<br>These people who do not follow the training,<br>Why will they have shaved their heads? {16}

“In the past I practiced bodhisattva conduct,<br>Which was extremely difficult, for thousands of eons.<br>I did so seeking this samādhi of peace,<br>But they will laugh when they hear of it. {17}

“For a long time they will lie and will not be celibate.<br>Always enjoying what is harmful, they will descend to the lower realms.<br>They will hold up the banner of celibacy,<br>But will have bad conduct and what they teach will not be the Dharma. {18}

“They will be divided against each other.<br>They will yearn for that which is acquired inappropriately.<br>They will say unpleasant things to each other,<br>And when they die they will go to the level of the lower existences. {19} ^F53b

“It will be hard to find among a hundred, a thousand, [n621]<br>One who has the power of patience.<br>Therefore there will be many who are deeply involved in quarreling.<br>They will explain elaborately, having rejected patience. {20}

“They will say the words, ‘I am a bodhisattva,’<br>And those words will spread in every direction.<br>They will become conceited [n622] through their arrogant, false words, [n623]<br>But how can there be enlightenment for someone whose conduct has gone astray? {21}

“I have never heard of, nor have I seen,<br>Someone whose motivation is not pure<br>And who has no patience for these phenomena,<br>Attaining enlightenment after discarding the Dharma. {22}

“It is through fear and anxiety they will have abandoned their homes<br>And held firmly to the homeless life.<br>But having acute desires they will proceed toward destruction,<br>Forsaking the way of the supreme humans. {23} [n624]

“They will have inferior wisdom and be devoid of good qualities,<br>And they will always be criticizing the supreme yāna.<br>They will always be talking about the hundreds of faults<br>Of that in which they have taken refuge. {24} [n625]

“Many will have entered homelessness because they had no livelihood.<br>They will have no wish at all for the enlightenment of buddhahood.<br>Those foolish ones will maintain the view of a self<br>And become afraid when they hear of emptiness. {25}

“They will quarrel with each other [n626]<br>And develop intractable evil malice.<br>They will say unpleasant things to each other<br>And find great joy in having done bad things. {26}

“Those who have correct conduct will have good qualities.<br>They will always remain loving and be skilled in patience.<br>They will be perfectly gentle, kind, and controlled—<br>Yet they will be the ones despised at that time. {27}

“Those who have wicked minds,<br>Who are dreadful, and accomplish terrible, very low actions,<br>Those whose conduct is not that of the Dharma and who enjoy fighting:<br>They will have offerings made to them at that time. {28}

“I declare this, I know this.<br>Young man, if you have faith in me,<br>Remember this teaching by the Sugata<br>And never depend on those others. {29}

“They will have strong desire and strong anger.<br>They will have strong ignorance and be conceited and arrogant.<br>They will have unrestrained bodies and unrestrained speech<br>And unrestrained minds, and will descend to the lower existences. {30} ^F54a

“I have recited the praises of those qualities<br>But the bhikṣus will not practice these qualities.<br>Enlightenment is not attained by mere words.<br>For one who is dedicated to practice, enlightenment will not be difficult to attain.” {31}

When the Bhagavān had finished speaking, the bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya, who was seated there, in his mind recited this verse to the Bhagavān. [n627]

“I am going, Tathāgata, [n628] to the king of mountains,<br>Gṛdhrakūṭa, which is always the residence of the buddhas.<br>When I have gone there, lamp of the world, [n629]<br>I will make inconceivable offerings to you.” {i}

The Bhagavān knew the thoughts that were in the bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya’s mind, and from his own mind sent this verse to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya:

“Go, Ajita, you who have conquered the māras, [n630]<br>To the king of mountains where jinas reside.<br>There you will quickly accomplish<br>A great unsurpassable benefit for beings.” {ii}

So the bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya, having received in his mind that verse from the Bhagavān, paid homage to the Bhagavān in his mind and, again in his mind, circumambulated him three times. He then left the assembly and went to Gṛdhrakūṭa, the king of mountains, which has been the residence of countless buddhas, as numerous as the grains of sand in the ocean, and where there is a great caitya.

The moment he arrived there, for the enjoyment of the Bhagavān, he magically transformed the king of mountains to become level and vast, without any tree stumps, thorns, stones, pebbles, or gravel, and with a surrounding wall made of the seven jewels. The ground was composed of countless shining sapphire jewels and was adorned by divine adornments and jewels, all of them beyond compare, and beautified by an array of innumerable, different kinds of jewels. All the area was decorated by the clothing of Tuṣita devas,  pervaded by the aroma of incense from a variety of censers, adorned by garlands and wreaths, scattered with various flowers; it resounded with the sound of divine music, was filled with erect and fluttering banners and flags, and over it canopies were suspended. ^F54b

In the center of this area a divine lion throne made from the seven jewels was emanated. It was draped in cloth that was not woven, and covered with divine clothing from Tuṣita that was as soft and pleasant to the touch as down. A central awning hung above, and there were two red cushions placed upon it. It was a yojana wide and a yojana high.

Its beautiful footstool, made of Jambu River gold, transcended that of humans and devas. It was covered with a net of strings of pearls, and it was draped in divine, precious cottons.

Strung upon the lion throne were strings of divine, precious bells from which came clear, beautiful, gentle sounds. In all directions there were great shining jewels. And there was emanated a precious, vast parasol, with a handle made of a great, precious jewel of stainless beryl.

The bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya now emanated an inconceivable, adorning array of various jewels on Gṛdhrakūṭa, the king of mountains, and in its entire environs. Then, in an instant, he returned to the home of the youth Candraprabha.

Once he was back there, in his mind he paid homage to the Bhagavān, and in his mind circumambulated him three times. He then sat on his seat.

It was said:

He manifested the mountain as a divine, vast place<br>With excellent, beautiful jewel flagstones—<br>Inconceivable, divine, formed from the mind—<br>And he placed in the center a precious lion throne. {iii}

Jinaputra Ajita also manifested<br>A divine, splendid parasol that emitted delightful sounds<br>With great shining jewels all around,<br>And a handle of pure, beautiful beryl. {iv}

Maitreya, the hero, having emanated<br>A variety of jewels on the mountain,<br>And a precious seat that was a krośa in size,<br>In one instant returned to the house. [n631] {v} ^F55a

Then the Bhagavān taught the Dharma to the great assembly that was like an ocean. He inspired them, he filled them with joy, and he guided them. Then he rose from his seat and departed. And with the miraculous power of a buddha he emerged through Rājagṛha’s gate of the hot springs and proceeded toward Gṛdhrakūṭa, the king of mountains. When he arrived he went to the site created by Maitreya, and having arrived there he sat upon the great lion throne that Maitreya had manifested. [n632]

He was encircled by the assembly of bhikṣus, and the saṅgha of bodhisattvas gazed upon him from the front. The devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, rishis, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, and nonhumans paid homage to him. Within the ocean-like assembly, he taught the Dharma.

Then the youth Candraprabha arrived together with a hundred thousand quintillion beings, and many millions of bodhisattva mahāsattvas who had come from other worlds. They were holding flowers, incense, and garlands; playing musical instruments and percussion; holding parasols, banners, and divine flags; and holding great garlands as offerings.

In order to make this offering to the Bhagavān they left the great city of Rājagṛha through the gateway of peace, [n633] and went to Gṛdhrakūṭa, to the Bhagavān. They bowed down their heads to the Bhagavān’s feet, circumambulated him three times, made a great offering to him of flowers, incense, perfume, garlands, ointments, powders, clothes, food, parasols, banners, and flags, playing music and percussion, and then they sat down in one place. In order to ask about the Dharma they sat in that place with veneration and with respect while the youth Candraprabha, kneeling on his right knee, with palms placed together, bowed toward the Bhagavān [n634] and said to him, “If the Bhagavān will give me an opportunity to seek answers to them, I have a few questions for the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.” ^F55b

The Bhagavān addressed the youth Candraprabha, saying, “Young man, the Bhagavān will always give you the opportunity. Ask whatever question you wish to the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.”

The Bhagavān having given him this opportunity, the young man Candraprabha asked, “Bhagavān, it is through possessing what qualities that bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena?”

The Bhagavān replied to Candraprabha, “Young man, if bodhisattva mahāsattvas possess four qualities, they will attain the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena.

“What are those four qualities? Young man, one is that bodhisattva mahāsattvas are calm, and pleasant company. They have self-restraint, and have attained a level of self-restraint such that when others abuse them or insult them, they will be patient with the abuse and the insults that are spoken, for it is their nature to have endurance; they have the view of karma, have overcome pride, and their desire is for the Dharma. Young man, if bodhisattva mahāsattvas have this first quality, they will attain this samādhi. [n635]

“Another, young man, is that bodhisattva mahāsattvas have correct conduct. They have pure conduct, conduct that is not impaired, conduct that is free of faults, conduct that is unshakable, conduct that is unstained, conduct that has not declined, conduct that is unattached,  conduct that is inviolate, conduct that is beyond conceptualization, conduct that is praised by the āryas, and conduct that is praised by the wise. Young man, if bodhisattva mahāsattvas have these two qualities, they will attain this samādhi. [n636] ^F56a

“Another, young man, is that bodhisattva mahāsattvas are frightened of the three realms. They are terrified of them, saddened by them, [n637] do not value them, take no delight in them, [n638] and have no attachment or clinging to them. [n639] Because they are distressed by the three realms they are dedicated to the thought, ‘I shall deliver other beings from their suffering, to somewhere other than the three realms!’ and they thus proceed to the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have these three qualities will attain this samādhi. [n640]

“Moreover, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas have faith. [n641] They insatiably seek the Dharma. They listen to many teachings. They have confidence. They long for the Dharma. They are devoted to the Dharma. They are not devoted to obtaining material gain or honors. They are not devoted to attaining success through knowledge. They think first of what will benefit others, and they teach and explain extensively to others the Dharma that they have received. They have no desire for material gain through their reputation. They think, ‘If these beings can hear this Dharma then they will proceed irreversibly to the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.’ [n642] Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have these four qualities will attain this samādhi.

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have these four qualities will attain the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, and they will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.

“Young man, the samādhi has been taught through this Dharma discourse by many buddhas, has been commended by many buddhas,  has been explained by many buddhas, and has been praised [n643] by many buddhas. ^F56b

“Young man, I have entered homelessness in the presence of many buddha bhagavāns. I heard extensively from them this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. I obtained it, asked questions about it, preserved it, recited it to others, promoted it, meditated on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgated it, [n644] and made it widely known to others.” [n645]

Thereupon the Bhagavān taught extensively in verse what he had previously said about the samādhi doorway taught by many buddhas.

“I remember countless, innumerable eons ago<br>There was a jina named Svarāṅgaghoṣa.<br>Tathāgata Svarāṅgaghoṣa<br>Had a lifespan of six thousand years. {1}

“After him there was a buddha,<br>A supreme man named Jñāneśvara.<br>Jñāneśvara, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of twelve thousand years. {2}

“After Jñāneśvara there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Tejeśvara.<br>Tejeśvara, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of sixty-seven thousand years. {3}

“After Tejeśvara there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Matīśvara.<br>Matīśvara, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of ten million years. {4}

“After Matīśvara there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Brahmeśvara.<br>Brahmeśvara, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of fourteen thousand years. [n646] {5}

“After Brahmeśvara there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Agnīśvara. [n647]<br>Agnīśvara, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of seventy-six thousand years. {6}

“After Agnīśvara there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Brahmānana.<br>Brahmānana, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of seven days. {7}

“After Brahmānana there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Gaṇeśvara.<br>Gaṇeśvara, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of a full ten million years. [n648] {8} ^F57a

“After Gaṇeśvara there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Ghoṣeśvara.<br>Ghoṣeśvara, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of ninety million years. {9}

“After Ghoṣeśvara there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Ghoṣānana.<br>Ghoṣānana, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of a hundred million years. {10}

“After Ghoṣānana there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Candrānana.<br>Candrānana, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of one day. [n649] {11}

“After Candrānana there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Sūryānana.<br>Sūryānana, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of eighteen thousand years. {12}

“After Sūryānana there was a buddha,<br>Another jina who was named Brahmānana.<br>Brahmānana, highest of humans, [DP.138]<br>Had a lifespan of twenty thousand years. [n650] {13}

“After Brahmānana there was a buddha,<br>A jina who was named Brahmaśrava.<br>Brahmaśrava, highest of humans,<br>Had a lifespan of eighteen thousand years. {14}

“In one eon these buddhas appeared<br>Among two hundred guides of the world.<br>Listen as I shall proclaim the names<br>Of these invincible tathāgatas: [n651] {15}

“Anantaghoṣa and Vighuṣṭaghoṣa,<br>Vighuṣṭatejas and Vighuṣṭaśabda,<br>Svarāvighuṣṭa and Svarārcita,<br>Svarāṅgaśūra and Svarāṅgaśabda, {16}

“Jñānābala and Jñānaviśeṣaga,<br>Jñānābhibhū and Jñānasamudgata,<br>Jñānārcimat and Jñānābhyudgata,<br>Vighuṣṭajñāna and likewise Jñānaśūra, {17}

“Brahmābala, Brahmavasu, Subrahma,<br>Brahmādeva [n652] and similarly Brahmaghoṣa,<br>Brahmeśvara, Brahma­narendra­netra,<br>Brahmasvarāṅga, Brahmadatta, [n653] {18} ^F57b

“Tejobala, Tejavati, Sutejas,<br>Tejeśvara and Tejasamudrata,<br>Tejovibhu and Tejaviniścita,<br>Tejasvarendra and Suvighuṣṭatejas, {19}

“Bhīṣmabala, Bhīṣmamati, Subhīṣma,<br>Bhīṣmānana and Bhīṣmasamudgata,<br>Bhīṣmārci, Bhīṣmottara, and Bhīṣmaghoṣa—<br>These jinas were guides of the world. {20}

“Gambhīraghoṣa and Śiridhāraṇa,<br>Viśuddha­ghoṣeśvara, Śuddhaghoṣa, [n654]<br>Anantaghoṣa, Suvimuktaghoṣa,<br>Mārabala [n655] and Māravitrāsana, {21}

“Sunetra, Śuddhānana, Netraśuddha,<br>Viśuddhanetra and Anantanetra,<br>Samantanetra and Vighuṣṭanetra,<br>Netrābhibhu, Netrānindita, {22}

“Dāntottara, Dānta, Sudāntacitta,<br>Sudānta, Śāntendriya, Śāntamānasa,<br>Śāntottara, Śāntaśirin, Praśānta,<br>Śāntīya­pāraṃgata and Śāntiśūra, {23}

“Sthitottara, Śānta, Sudāntacitta,<br>Sudānta, Śāntendriya, Śāntamānasa,<br>Śāntottara, Śānta­śriya­jvalanta,<br>Śānta, Praśānteśvara, Śāntiśūra, [n656] {24}

“Gaṇendra, Gaṇamukhya, and Gaṇeśvara,<br>Gaṇābhibhu, Gaṇivara, Śuddhajñānin,<br>Mahāgaṇendra and Gaṇendraśūra,<br>And also Gaṇivara­pramocaka, {25}

“Dharmadhvaja and similarly Dharmaketu,<br>Dharmottara, Dharma­svabhāvodgata,<br>Dharmabala and Sudharmaśūra,<br>And Svabhāva­dharmottara­niścita. {26}

“Also there were eight hundred million with the same name<br>Of Svabhāva­dharmottara­niścita.<br>These are the guides that appeared in two eons.<br>I made offerings to them for the sake of enlightenment. {27}

“Whoever hears the name of those jinas,<br>Svabhāva­dharmottara­niścita,<br>And having heard it remembers that renowned name,<br>They will quickly attain this samādhi.” {28} ^F58a

Then the Bhagavān, through many verses, taught extensively to the youth Candraprabha the samādhi entranceway accomplished by many buddhas in the past. [n657]

“After inconceivable, countless eons<br>Following these buddhas,<br>There was a buddha named Narendraghoṣa,<br>To whom humans and devas made offerings. {29}

“Tathāgata Narendraghoṣa<br>Lived for seventy-six thousand years,<br>And three billion śrāvakas<br>Gathered for his first assembly. {30}

“At that time he had a shining saṅgha<br>Of those who had the six higher cognitions, the three knowledges,<br>Subdued senses, great powers, great miracles,<br>The cessation of outflows, and who were in their last bodies. {31}

“There was a saṅgha of bodhisattvas<br>Who numbered eight thousand quintillion.<br>They had profound understanding, fearlessness, [n658]<br>Great powers, and great miracles. {32}

“They had attained the higher cognitions, eloquence,<br>And they had realized emptiness in everything.<br>They miraculously went to millions of realms<br>And to even more, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges. {33}

“They came into the presence of that jina<br>And addressed questions to that supreme human.<br>They were accomplished in the sūtras and skilled in definitions.<br>They were shining and moved upon the earth. {34}

“They performed bodhisattva conduct for the benefit of beings.<br>They were powerful sons of the Sugata.<br>They performed no bad actions through desire,<br>And toward them even the devas developed aspirations. {35}

“They had no longings and were detached from the realms of existence.<br>They were in meditation, the field of experience of remaining in dhyāna.<br>They had certainty in the true meaning, and were fearless.<br>They maintained celibacy and were free of defilement. {36}

“They had the confident eloquence of unceasing speech.<br>They were skilled in the meaning of the words and the teaching of definitions.<br>They were the sons of the Buddha who taught everywhere,<br>And they perfectly possessed good karma. {37}

“They maintained superior conduct throughout an infinity of eons;<br>They were always praised and extolled by the guides.<br>They taught the words and meaning of liberation.<br>They had perfectly pure conduct free of kleśas. {38} ^F58b

“They were as unstained as a lotus by water.<br>They were liberated from the three realms, and were vigilant.<br>They were unstained by the eight worldly concerns.<br>They had pure bodies and pure actions. {39}

“They had contentment, great power, and few desires.<br>They were free of grasping and were established in buddha qualities.<br>They were a refuge and friend for all classes of beings.<br>They considered practice, not words, as the essence. {40}

“Wherever they dwelt, there they taught others.<br>They were adopted by all the buddhas.<br>They were trustworthy holders of the treasure of the jinas.<br>They were terrified of the entire three realms. [n659] {41}

“Their minds were at peace, they always had the conduct of protectors,<br>And they were blessed by the guides of the world.<br>They taught ten thousand million sūtras,<br>And the buddhas praised their teachings. {42}

“They had forsaken all worldly words. [n660]<br>They aspired to emptiness and taught the ultimate.<br>They were like an ocean of good qualities; there was no end to their being praised.<br>Their learning was vast; they were wise and endowed with knowledge. {43}

“If a young man were to recite their praises<br>Continuously for many millions of eons<br>He would have only uttered a small amount,<br>Like a drop of water from an ocean. {44}

“At that time Narendraghoṣa<br>Taught this samādhi of peace, which is difficult to see.<br>This universe of a thousand million worlds<br>Was filled with devas and nāgas. {45}

“When he taught this samādhi of peace<br>The ground shook in six ways.<br>Devas and humans as numerous as the Ganges sands<br>Became irreversible within the buddha’s wisdom. {46}

“There was a human king, a sovereign<br>Named Śirībala, who was very powerful.<br>He had five hundred sons<br>Who were handsome and attractive to the sight. {47}

“The king had a harem<br>Of eighty thousand million women.<br>The king had daughters<br>Who numbered a full four hundred billion. {48} ^F59a

“He took the eight poṣadha vows<br>On the full moon day of the Kārtika month,<br>And with the eighty thousand million others<br>He came before the Lord of the World. {49}

“The king bowed down to the feet of the supreme human<br>And sat down before the Jina.<br>The supreme human knew the king’s aspiration<br>And he taught this samādhi. {50}

“When the king had heard this samādhi<br>He abandoned his kingdom as if it were spittle.<br>He renounced his beloved family and kinsmen<br>And entered homelessness in that jina’s teaching. {51}

“His five hundred sons entered homelessness,<br>And also his harem and his daughters,<br>And also his other relatives,<br>Numbering seventy-five quintillion. {52}

“Having entered homelessness along with his children and wives,<br>He kept to the station of acquiring alms food [n661]<br>And steadfastly wandered in this way for eight years.<br>While remaining [n662] in wandering his life came to an end. {53}

“His life having ended, that preeminent king, [n663]<br>Being always perfectly focused on a samādhi mind,<br>Was reborn into a king’s family,<br>Appearing miraculously, unstained by a womb. {54}

“Dṛḍhabala was his father’s name.<br>And his mother’s name was Mahāmatī.<br>As soon as he was born, the prince asked,<br>‘Is the Lord of the World present? {55}

“ ‘The Lord of the World, who knows my mind,<br>Taught to me the samādhi of peace.<br>It has no causal factors, is free of causal factors,<br>And is the one teaching for beings in existence. {56}

“ ‘It is the seal of the nature of all phenomena.<br>It is the transmission of a quintillion sūtras.<br>It is the unsurpassable wealth of the bodhisattvas.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {57}

“ ‘It is the purity of the body, the purity of speech,<br>The purity of the mind, and the purity of view.<br>It transcends all objects of the mind.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {58}

“ ‘The result of this Dharma teaching is imperishable.<br>It is the meditation of the supreme eightfold path.<br>It is the sharp wisdom of the congregation of the tathāgatas.<br>It is entering truth and constant knowledge of the Dharma. [n664] {59} ^F59b

“ ‘It is understanding the skandhas, the equality of the dhātus,<br>And the complete elimination of the āyatanas.<br>It is the direct perception of birthlessness.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {60}

“ ‘It is discernment, the wisdom that enters peace. [n665]<br>It is the knowledge of the different categories of all letters.<br>It is transcending focusing upon the material.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {61}

“ ‘It is the comprehension of all sounds, and the attainment of joy.<br>It is the enjoyment of praising the sugatas.<br>It is the kindness and honesty that is the way of the āryas.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {62}

“ ‘It is being pleasant and never frowning.<br>It is being friendly and gentle with a smiling face.<br>It is being first to speak on seeing beings.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {63}

“ ‘It is being without laziness and respecting the gurus.<br>It is being reverential, paying homage, and being pleasant to see.<br>It is being content with whatever arises, and virtuous.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {64}

“ ‘It is having a pure livelihood and dwelling in solitary places. [n666]<br>It is maintaining the disciplines of mendicancy with no loss of mindfulness.<br>It is being adept in the āyatanas and in the dhātus.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {65}

“ ‘It is skill in the āyatanas, and the knowledge of the higher cognitions;<br>It is the elimination of the kleśas, and the level of self-subjugation.<br>It is the termination [n667] of all the multitudes of mantras. [n668]<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {66}

“ ‘It transcends all the states of being in existence.<br>It is remembering previous lives and having no doubt in the Dharma.<br>It is aspiring to the Dharma and seeking to hear it.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? [n669] {67}

“ ‘It is a special attainment, being always engaged in meditation.<br>It is the knowledge of downfalls and remaining in emancipation. [n670]<br>It is the elimination of propensities through remaining in that emancipation.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? [n671] {68}

“ ‘It is the attainment of the perfection of sharp wisdom.<br>It is being as unwavering and unshakable as a mountain.<br>It is the dhāraṇī entranceway that has the characteristic of irreversibility.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {69}

“ ‘It is always longing for good qualities.<br>It is always [n672] avoiding bad qualities.<br>It is never going to the side of the kleśas.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {70} ^F60a

“ ‘The one who is wise in mastering [n673] all training,<br>The one who has mastered remaining in samādhi,<br>The one who inspires beings through knowing their thoughts<br>Teaches the Dharma for the supreme enlightenment of buddhahood. {71}

“ ‘It is unique knowledge, the knowledge of births.<br>It is infinite knowledge, completely perfect knowledge.<br>It is the knowledge of the transition between all existences.<br>Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {72}

“ ‘Abandoning home, aspiring to mendicancy,<br>Finding no joy in the three realms, having no grasping,<br>And rejoicing in controlling the mind:<br>The supreme human teaches that Dharma. {73}

“ ‘Having no attachment for phenomena,<br>Always grasping the supreme Dharma,<br>And having a stable aspiration for the ripening of karma:<br>The supreme human teaches that Dharma. {74}

“ ‘Skill in the vinaya, knowledge of the ripening of karma,<br>The pacification of conflict and quarrels,<br>Freedom from discord, the level that is free of quarrels:<br>The supreme human teaches that Dharma. {75}

“ ‘Having complete patience, never having anger,<br>Always having skill and certainty in the Dharma,<br>Distinguishing between words and having the insight of wisdom:<br>Having developed compassion, he teaches that Dharma. {76}

“ ‘He has taught the knowledge of the past, knowledge of the future,<br>The equality of the three times in the teaching of the sugatas,<br>And the cessation of the three aspects of an action:<br>That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {77}

“ ‘The mind’s perfect stability and one-pointedness,<br>The body’s perfect stability as on the level of the āryas,<br>And at all times guarding the conduct of a mendicant:<br>That is the Dharma that the sage, the preeminent human, teaches. {78}

“ ‘A pleasing sense of modesty and self-respect,<br>Speaking appropriate words, knowledge of the world,<br>The origination of phenomena, and the nature of beings:<br>He teaches that Dharma of the supreme, perfect enlightenment. {79}

“ ‘Benefiting and having a sense of modesty,<br>Abhorring the wickedness of the mind,<br>Never abandoning the mendicant’s discipline, and begging for alms:<br>That is the Dharma that the supreme human teaches. {80} ^F60b

“ ‘Always maintaining a sense of modesty and self-respect,<br>Speaking reverently to the guru and rising to greet him,<br>Having overcome pride from the beginning:<br>That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {81}
