“ ‘That which arises from the mind is the goodness of the mind;<br>There is wisdom’s discrimination, and thus realization,<br>And the region of ignorance is always avoided:<br>He teaches that Dharma of supreme, perfect enlightenment. {82}

“ ‘There is understanding of the mind, the knowledge of words,<br>Being established in definitions, with certainty of meanings,<br>And all that is meaningless [n674] is always avoided:<br>That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {83}

“ ‘Always associating with good persons<br>And always avoiding bad persons,<br>And always being attracted to and delighting in the Jina:<br>That is the supreme Dharma that the Jina teaches. {84}

“ ‘The description of designations and appellations, [n675]<br>The continual avoidance of the suffering of saṃsāra,<br>And indifference to whether there is gain or no gain:<br>That is the supreme Dharma that the Jina teaches. {85}

“ ‘There is no amazement if honors are gained,<br>There is equanimity when there are no honors,<br>And there is never pride when there are praises:<br>This is nature of the teaching that benefits the world. {86}

“ ‘All abuse and disgrace is endured,<br>There is no association with any householder,<br>And there is no mingling with homeless mendicants: [n676]<br>That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {87}

“ ‘Remaining in the Buddha’s scope of conduct,<br>Rejecting all that is not that conduct,<br>And having perfect conduct and a well-controlled mind:<br>That is the way of the Dharma that the Sugata teaches. {88}

“ ‘Always rejecting the dharma of the foolish,<br>Rejecting all that disgraces the family of the Buddha,<br>Always protecting the teaching of the Buddha:<br>That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {89}

“ ‘Speaking little, pleasantly, and articulately,<br>Speaking good and gentle words to others,<br>Subjugating adversaries through the Dharma:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {90}

“ ‘Arriving at the right time, and not the wrong time,<br>Never depending on any ordinary being,<br>Not being saddened on encountering suffering:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {91} ^F61a

“ ‘When seeing the poor, bringing them wealth;<br>When seeing those with bad conduct, feeling compassion;<br>Always teaching those things that are beneficial:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {92}

“ ‘Benefiting beings through the Dharma,<br>Always giving away worldly material things,<br>Never accumulating, never amassing:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {93}

“ ‘Praising correct conduct and condemning bad conduct,<br>Being free of dishonesty and relying on those with correct conduct,<br>Giving away one’s possessions and not relying on wealth:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {94}

“ ‘Providing for the guru with a higher motivation,<br>Doing all that he has told one to do,<br>Never ceasing from serving the dharmabhāṇaka:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {95}

“ ‘Always being respectful and delighted,<br>Remaining continually in a peaceful view,<br>Always being sure of one’s past conduct:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {96}

“ ‘Always following those with correct conduct,<br>With skillful methods shunning [n677] concepts,<br>Repelling identification and the characteristics of things:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {97}

“ ‘Being skilled in the words produced within the sūtras,<br>Having certainty in the words that teach the truth,<br>The manifestation of the wisdom of liberation:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {98}

“ ‘Speaking words that are never contradictory,<br>Skillful in the certainty of what is taught, [n678]<br>And using words that will not be doubted:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. [n679] {i}

“ ‘Always relying on the Dharma of emptiness,<br>Maintaining fearlessly the power of correct conduct,<br>And applying equality through remaining in samādhi:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {99}

“ ‘Not wishing to attain intellectual knowledge,<br>Keeping the mind free from hypocrisy,<br>And rejecting the creation of any view:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {100} ^F61b

“ ‘Supreme confidence in speech and sublime retention,<br>The limitless radiance of wisdom,<br>And correct eloquence with the power of mantra:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {101}

“ ‘Meditation on the path through this doorway of correct conduct, [n680]<br>Excellent practice, instruction, and conduct, [n681]<br>And teaching that follows practicing the teaching: [n682]<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {102}

“ ‘The appropriate patience that is praised by the buddhas,<br>The maintenance of patience that avoids bad actions,<br>And eliminating ignorance by being established in knowledge:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {103}

“ ‘The level of yoga [n683] that is based upon wisdom,<br>The mastery of yoga through entering enlightenment,<br>The continual reliance on good beings:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {104}

“ ‘It is the constant avoidance of unrestrained practitioners, [n684]<br>It is the level of buddhahood taught by tathāgatas,<br>And it is rejoiced in by all who are wise:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {105}

“ ‘It is rejected by the foolish and ignorant.<br>It is not the level [n685] of the numerous śrāvakas, [n686]<br>And it is always obtained by the bodhisattvas:<br>That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {106}

“ ‘It is realized [n687] by the tathāgatas.<br>It is offered to and honored by the devas.<br>It is rejoiced in by a hundred billion Brahmās.<br>Is the Jina teaching this samādhi? {107}

“ ‘Thousands of nāgas always pay homage to it,<br>And so do garuḍas, yakṣas, and kinnaras.<br>It is the supreme enlightenment taught by the Jina.<br>Is the Jina teaching this samādhi? {108}

“ ‘It is always obtained by those who are wise.<br>It is the perfect attainment of the best, supreme wealth.<br>It is the supreme nonmaterial medicine of wisdom.<br>Is the Jina teaching this samādhi? {109}

“ ‘It is wisdom’s treasure of unceasing eloquence.<br>Ten million sūtras are contained within it.<br>It is accurate knowledge, the complete knowledge of the three realms.<br>Is the Jina teaching this samādhi? {110}

“ ‘It is a boat that crosses to the other shore,<br>It is a ship that crosses a great river,<br>And it increases fame and garlands of praises<br>For those to whom this samādhi of peace is taught. {111} ^F62a

“ ‘Those who teach this samādhi of peace<br>Are praised by all the tathāgatas,<br>Extolled by the chiefs among humans,<br>And unceasingly commended by bodhisattvas. {112}

“ ‘It is the teaching of love to end bad actions.<br>It is the level of compassion’s equanimity.<br>It is the comfort of the greatly famed ones [n688]<br>For the ones to whom this samādhi is taught. {113}

“ ‘It is the practice of the teaching of the lion’s roar.<br>It originates from the supreme wisdom of buddhahood.<br>It is the seal of the nature of all phenomena.<br>This is the samādhi taught by the guides. {114}

“ ‘It brings the attainment of omniscient wisdom,<br>It is the conduct of those established in enlightenment,<br>And it also terrifies the army of the māras.<br>This is the samādhi of peace taught by the Jina. {115}

“ ‘This knowledge [n689] is the protection that is based in the Dharma.<br>It is the supreme protection in the midst of enemies.<br>It is the subjugation of adversaries through the Dharma:<br>This is the samādhi of peace taught by the Jina. [n690] {116}

“ ‘This is the teaching of the level of eloquence.<br>It is the strengths, the liberations, and likewise the powers,<br>And it is the eighteen unique qualities of a buddha:<br>That is the practice of this samādhi, this peace. {117}

“ ‘It is seeking the ten strengths,<br>It is the omen of the coming of buddha wisdom,<br>It is the buddhadharma taught by the supreme being,<br>And it is the teaching that compassionately benefits the world. {118}

“ ‘It is possessed by the sons of the buddhas.<br>It is the path taught for those who seek enlightenment.<br>It is rejoiced in by the offspring of the sugatas<br>When they hear this samādhi of peace that is difficult to see. {119}

“ ‘It is the complete wisdom of buddhahood.<br>It is what the wise bodhisattva seeks.<br>One with a pure mind, clear and unblemished, [n691]<br>Practices the peace of this samādhi. {120}

“ ‘One who has a pure body like that of the jinas,<br>Who has the knowledge of liberation, the vision of liberation,<br>And who is never afflicted by the bondage of desire,<br>Practices this excellent samādhi. {121} ^F62b

“ ‘One who is not on the level of anger and is free of ignorance,<br>In whom wisdom has arisen [n692] and who seeks liberation, [n693]<br>In whom knowledge has developed and ignorance is destroyed,<br>Practices the peace of this samādhi. {122}

“ ‘This samādhi of peace is taught to the meditator<br>For whom liberation is central, and is fulfilled by this teaching.<br>The one with the sight of the faultless buddhas<br>Practices the peace of this samādhi. {123}

“ ‘The clairvoyance that reveals many realms,<br>The miraculous powers that reveal infinite buddhas,<br>And dhāraṇī is also not difficult to attain<br>For the one who practices this samādhi. {124}

“ ‘The senses are pacified in this state of enlightenment.<br>There is the revelation of infinite blessings,<br>And subtle, vast, and pure wisdom<br>For the one who practices this samādhi. {125}

“ ‘For the one who has not heard this samādhi of peace,<br>Practice without self-restraint will bring no realization,<br>And as all the words will have been subverted,<br>No understanding will be possible from speech. {126}

“ ‘This is known by wise bodhisattvas<br>Just as taught by the Lord of Dharma.<br>There is faultless realization of peace<br>For the one who practices this samādhi. {127}

“ ‘For the one who practices this samādhi<br>With diligent application, having possession of it,<br>Constantly serving it, and perfectly keeping it,<br>There will be cessation of suffering and the end of rebirth. {128}

“ ‘It has been taught that all phenomena are birthless,<br>As are all the existences of beings.<br>Is the Jina teaching this samādhi<br>Of the greatly famous, supremely wise buddhas?’ {129}

“A full eighty-eight trillion beings<br>Heard these verses recited by the prince,<br>Attained the patience that corresponded to those words,<br>And were established in irreversible progress toward buddha wisdom. {130}

“Dṛḍhabala said to the prince,<br>‘The Lord of the World is still present.<br>I have a question for you, my son:<br>Where did you hear of this samādhi?’ {131}

“The prince said to the king, ‘Listen!<br>During one eon I have seen<br>A quintillion buddhas, honored them all,<br>And asked them for this samādhi of peace. {132} ^F63a

“ ‘And for another ninety-four [n694] eons,<br>And for a thousand quintillion eons,<br>I remember all my births wherever they were,<br>And I was never born from a womb. {133}

“ ‘Then I meditated upon this samādhi.<br>I listened correctly to the teaching of those jinas.<br>Having heard it I had longing for what had been described.<br>Free from uncertainty I embraced enlightenment. {134}

“ ‘I questioned whatever bhikṣus<br>Had understood this samādhi.<br>I venerated them respectfully<br>As if they were benefactors of the world. {135}

“ ‘When I received even one verse from them<br>I practiced that teaching properly<br>And considered them to be teachers,<br>Venerating them with the respect shown to buddhas. {136}

“ ‘Whenever someone questioned me<br>About my understanding of this samādhi,<br>Even in dreams I had no doubts<br>That I would become a jina, a guide of the world. {137}

“ ‘I respectfully attended<br>To senior, middle, and junior bhikṣus.<br>With that respect my renown increased,<br>As did my merit, fame, and qualities. [n695] {138}

“ ‘I had no desire for conflict or quarrels.<br>At that time, I had few desires.<br>Those who do bad actions are reborn in certain existences.<br>Those who do good actions are reborn in other existences. {139}

“ ‘One hears unpleasant words from those<br>Who, without restraint, act inappropriately.<br>At that time I became the lord of my own actions.<br>The karma that is created is never lost. {140}

“ ‘I did not at that time become absorbed in anger.<br>I maintained the power of patience, which is praised by the buddhas.<br>The guides have always praised patience;<br>Attaining enlightenment is not difficult for those who practice patience. {141}

“ ‘I continually had correct conduct<br>And established others in correct conduct.<br>I always spoke the praises of correct conduct,<br>And what I spoke at that time was praiseworthy. {142} ^F63b

“ ‘I was always speaking the praises of solitude.<br>I always maintained correct conduct.<br>I established others in the poṣadha vows<br>And I introduced them to enlightenment. {143}

“ ‘I established them in celibacy,<br>I introduced them to the meaning of the Dharma,<br>And I awoke them to the path to enlightenment,<br>For which they had endless devotion. [n696] {144}

“ ‘I remember an eon in the past<br>When there was the jina Svarāṅgaghoṣa. [n697]<br>I took a vow in his presence<br>To have the power of patience at all times. {145}

“ ‘I remained faithful to that vow<br>For eight hundred and forty million years.<br>Although Māra reviled and abused me,<br>My mind remained unshakable. {146}

“ ‘Māra put me to the test,<br>And discovered my love and patience to be enduring.<br>And with faith [n698] he bowed down to my feet,<br>And I established five hundred beings on the path to supreme enlightenment. {147}

“ ‘At all times I was free of avarice<br>And always praised generosity.<br>I became wealthy, possessing many riches<br>And was a benefactor in times of famine. {148}

“ ‘I pay homage to any monks<br>Who possess this samādhi,<br>Who recite it and teach it.<br>They all become supreme men. {149}

“ ‘Because of that unsurpassable karma<br>I saw many buddhas, many lords of the world.<br>I entered into homelessness in the teachings of those jinas<br>And I always became a wise dharmabhāṇaka. {150}

“ ‘I was always engaged in the discipline of a mendicant.<br>I always remained in the solitude of forests.<br>I never gave the appearance of spirituality in order to obtain food.<br>I was content with whatever I obtained. {151}

“ ‘At all times I was free of envy.<br>I had no attachment to a family.<br>Attachment to family causes envy.<br>Without envy I remained in the pleasant forests. {152}

“ ‘At all times I had loving-kindness.<br>When I was abused I did not become angry.<br>As I was always kind, the garland of fame<br>Of my compassion spread in the four directions. {153} ^F64a

“ ‘I was always content, with few desires.<br>I was dedicated to mendicancy in solitary places.<br>I never abandoned begging for alms.<br>I remained unwaveringly committed to mendicancy. {154}

“ ‘I always had faith and belief.<br>I always had great belief in the Buddha’s teaching.<br>I obtained many benefits from having belief.<br>I became attractive with faultless faculties. {155}

“ ‘I practiced whatever I taught.<br>I always valued practice above all else.<br>As I valued practice above all else,<br>Devas and nāgas believed in me and honored me. {156}

“ ‘There are also numerous other qualities,<br>Other than these that I have described.<br>They should always be trained in by the wise ones<br>Who wish for the enlightenment of buddhahood. {157}

“ ‘I remember the greatest number of hardships<br>That I practiced through numerous eons, [n699]<br>So numerous [n700] I am unable to describe them. [n701]<br>I will now go [n702] into the presence of the Sugata.’ {158}

“That wise bodhisattva with sharp wisdom<br>At that moment attained the five higher cognitions.<br>Through miraculous power he came before the Jina,<br>Accompanied by eight hundred million beings. {159}

“Dṛḍhabala was extremely pleased,<br>And, accompanied by one billion six hundred million beings,<br>He came into the presence of the Buddha,<br>Bowed down to his feet, and sat before him. {160}

“Knowing the aspiration of that king,<br>The Lord of humans taught this samādhi.<br>When the king had heard that samādhi<br>He renounced his kingdom and entered homelessness. {161}

“Homeless, he meditated on this samādhi,<br>And he recited it and taught it.<br>After sixty eons had passed<br>He became a jina named Padmottara. {162}

“The one billion six hundred million beings<br>Who had come with the king into the presence of the Jina<br>Also heard this samādhi,<br>And with the highest joy they entered homelessness. {163} ^F64b

“Homeless, they possessed this samādhi,<br>And recited it and taught it.<br>After six trillion eons had passed<br>They all reached supreme enlightenment in the same eon. {164}

“They all had the name Ananta­jñānanottara.<br>They were buddhas to whom devas and humans made offerings.<br>Each of those supreme humans liberated as many beings<br>As there are grains of sand in the Ganges. {165}

“I was King Śirībala. [n703]<br>The practitioners of this supreme bodhisattva conduct,<br>Those who were my five hundred sons,<br>Are these guardians of the Dharma. {166}

“The one who was my mother<br>Was Māyādevī [n704] in this time.<br>My four hundred billion daughters<br>All entered nirvāṇa.  [n705] {166b}

“The king who was named Dṛḍhabala,<br>The powerful cakravartin with many treasures,<br>Became King Śuddhodana [n706] in this age,<br>And has been my father in various lifetimes. [n707] {166c}

“Thus have I for ten billion eons<br>Exercised diligence that is free of laziness.<br>The pure yearning for this samādhi<br>Brings the accomplishment of supreme enlightenment. {167}

“Therefore, young man, those bodhisattvas<br>Who wish to meditate [n708] on this samādhi<br>Should exercise diligence, regardless of risks to their lives,<br>And always follow, young man, my example.” {168}

The Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, in that way know that there are four beneficial qualities possessed by bodhisattva mahāsattvas who obtain this samādhi, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, and make it widely known to others.

“What are those four beneficial qualities? They will be unsurpassable in merit, they will be undefeatable by opponents, they will have unlimited wisdom, and they will have unending confidence of speech.

Young man, you should know [n709] that bodhisattva mahāsattvas  who obtain this samādhi, study it, keep it, read it out loud, disseminate it, teach it, chant it, and make it widely known to others will possess these four beneficial qualities.” ^F65a

The Bhagavān then recited these verses:

“Throughout time they will be<br>Unsurpassable in merit<br>Through attaining this samādhi of peace.<br>That is the range of activity of all the buddhas. {1}

“Throughout time these heroes<br>Will be protected by merit,<br>Practicing supreme, pure,<br>Unique bodhisattva conduct. {2}

“There will be no adversary<br>Whatsoever who can harm them.<br>They will, throughout time,<br>Be in the care of the buddhas. {3}

“Throughout time their wisdom<br>Will be immeasurable.<br>Their confidence will be eternal<br>Through their possessing this state of peace. {4}

“They will have an eternally unsurpassable accumulation of merit.<br>They will have most excellent bodhisattva conduct.<br>They will not be attacked by adversaries,<br>Having come into possession of this samādhi of supreme peace. {5}

“They will have vast and sharp wisdom<br>And thus will have eternal confidence and pure sight.<br>Those wise ones will always have<br>The power of memory and the power of retention. {6}

“The meaningful words that they teach<br>Will be most beautiful to the minds of the wise.<br>Many beings with wisdom will know<br>This supreme peaceful samādhi that is taught. {7}

“They will obtain perfect, excellent Dharma robes,<br>Bedding, invitations, and hard and soft food.<br>The ones who possess this supreme samādhi of peace<br>Will be very youthful and handsome. {8}

“They will see many buddhas, lords of worlds,<br>And make unequaled offerings to those guides.<br>In seeking this supreme samādhi of peace<br>They will encounter no impediment. {9}

“They will be in the presence of the lords of worlds<br>And made happy by hundreds of beautiful verses.<br>Having gained this supreme samādhi of peace<br>They will never experience decline. {10} ^F65b

“A Lord of the World will be present before them<br>With the beautiful primary and secondary signs of the body.<br>Having gained this supreme samādhi of peace<br>There will be no decline in their wisdom. {11}

“They will never be disheartened.<br>They will always be wealthy and never poor.<br>Having gained this supreme samādhi of peace<br>There will be no attachment in their mind. {12}

“They will never have an unfavorable existence.<br>They will be world rulers, cakravartin kings.<br>Having gained this supreme samādhi of peace<br>Their kingdoms will always be happy. {13}

“They will have vast wisdom free of uncertainty<br>Through unceasing teachings for hundreds of eons.<br>Having heard this samādhi, this level of peace,<br>Constant, they will follow whatever has been taught. {14}

“Though one were to describe the benefits of the ten strengths<br>Throughout countless, endless millions of eons,<br>One would not have spoken of even a fraction of them.<br>It would be like taking a drop of water from the ocean.” {15}

At that time the young man, with great joy,<br>Stood up and paid homage with his palms together.<br>Joyfully standing before the one with the ten strengths<br>He uttered these inspired words: {16}

“Inconceivable great hero,<br>Lord of the World, illuminator,<br>These benefits have been taught to me<br>By you, the Lord of humans. {17}

“Compassionate one who wishes to bring benefit,<br>Great hero, pray tell me,<br>Who, in the future,<br>Will listen to this samādhi?” {18}

The one with a voice like the avadavat’s song,<br>The Teacher who had taught this to him,<br>The Bhagavān, who had unimpeded wisdom,<br>Answered him with these words: {19}

“Listen, young man, and I will explain<br>That which is the highest practice.<br>Those who follow the Dharma<br>Will be the ones who listens to this sūtra. {20}

“They will make offerings to the lords of humans;<br>They will seek the wisdom of buddhahood.<br>Developing a loving mind,<br>They will listen to this sūtra. {21} ^F66a

“Those who have the qualities of mendicancy [n710]<br>And the qualities of austerity, [n711]<br>And who maintain this practice,<br>Will be ones who listen to this sūtra. {22}

“They will not listen to this sūtra<br>When it is in the hands of those whose acts are evil,<br>Nor of those who have lost their correct conduct<br>Regarding the teaching of the lords of worlds. {23}

“They will hear it when in the hands<br>Of the celibates, the heroes,<br>Those who have a mind free of craving<br>And who have been consecrated by the buddhas. {24}

“In future times they will hear<br>This sūtra when it is in the hands<br>Of those who have served the buddhas,<br>The lords of the world, in the past. {25}

“Those who in previous lifetimes<br>Have been tīrthikas<br>Will experience no joy<br>When they hear this sūtra. {26}

“Those who have entered homelessness<br>In my teaching in order to have a livelihood<br>Will be under the power of gain and honor,<br>And they will criticize each other. {27}

“Many bhikṣus with unrestrained senses,<br>Who covet the wives of others,<br>Who wish for gain and have poor conduct,<br>Will have no faith in this sūtra. {28}

“Those who do not intend to attain<br>Merit for buddhahood or to attain dhyāna,<br>And who maintain the conception of a self,<br>Will have no faith in this sūtra. {29}

“In future times there will be those<br>Who are intent on the result of worldly dhyānas.<br>They will eat the alms food of arhats<br>And criticize the enlightenment of buddhahood. {30}

“One who rejects this sūtra<br>Will have greater bad karma<br>Than someone who destroys<br>All the caityas in this Jambudvīpa. {31}

“One who rejects this sūtra<br>Will have greater bad karma<br>Than someone who kills as many arhats<br>As there are grains of sand in the Ganges. {32}

“Who among you has the fortitude<br>To teach this sūtra<br>In the dreadful future time<br>When the Dharma is ruined?” [n712] {33}

The young man stood up, weeping,<br>And at that time spoke to the Jina.<br>This heart-born son of the Buddha<br>Roared thus this lion’s roar: {34} ^F66b

“In the dreadful time in future<br>When the Buddha has passed away,<br>Without concern for my life or body<br>I will spread this sūtra widely. {35}

“I will endure<br>The false talk of fools<br>And, Guide, I will undergo<br>Their abuse and threats. {36}

“I shall cleanse myself of whatever bad actions<br>I have done in the past<br>And any maliciousness<br>Toward other bodhisattvas.” {37}

The Buddha, who was the color of gold,<br>Placed his hand upon Candraprabha’s head.<br>The Tathāgata, who had a gentle voice,<br>The Teacher, then said to him, {38}

“I give you my blessing.<br>Young man, in the future<br>There will be no obstacle to your celibacy<br>Nor will there be to your life.” {39}

Eight hundred dharmabhāṇakas<br>Who were present stood up and said,<br>“In future times we also<br>Will be holders of this sūtra.” {40}

Eight hundred million<br>Devas, nāgas, and yakṣas stood up,<br>And another six trillion,<br>And said to the guide of the world, {41}

“Guide, in future times<br>We will protect<br>These bhikṣus who<br>Stood up today.” {42}

When this sūtra was taught,<br>Through the blessing of the Teacher,<br>Buddha realms shook, in numbers<br>Equal to the Ganges sands. {43}

The Lord of the World sent<br>To all those shaken buddha realms<br>Emanations of the Buddha<br>Who taught the Dharma there. {44}

In each of those realms<br>Countless millions of beings<br>Were established in the wisdom of buddhahood<br>When they had heard that Dharma. {45}

In those buddha realms<br>Nine hundred million devas [n713]<br>Developed the aspiration to enlightenment<br>And scattered flowers on the Buddha. {46}

The Lord of men prophesied that<br>After eight hundred million eons<br>They would all, within the same eon,<br>Become guides of the world. [n714] {47}

Bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs,<br>Upāsakas and upāsikās—<br>Seven hundred and sixty million beings—<br>All heard this sūtra. {48} ^F67a

The Lord of humans [n715] prophesied<br>That they would see as many guides of the world<br>As there are grains of sand in the Ganges<br>While practicing bodhisattva conduct. {49}

“They will make offerings to them all,<br>Seeking the wisdom of enlightenment,<br>And here and there they will hear<br>This unsurpassable sūtra. {50}

“They will make unsurpassable offerings<br>To Buddha Maitreya.<br>They will possess the highest Dharma<br>And they will go to Sukhāvatī. {52} [n716]

“There they will make offerings<br>To the stainless buddha,<br>The Tathāgata Amitāyus,<br>For the sake of supreme enlightenment. {53}

“Having heard this unsurpassable sūtra<br>They will not go in future<br>To the lower existences<br>For seventy-three [n717] countless eons. {54}

“Those who in future times<br>Listen to this unsurpassable sūtra,<br>And keep it and read it, [n718]<br>Will all be honoring [n719] me. {55}

“I make this declaration [n720]<br>To all those who are standing before me.<br>I bestow this enlightenment gained [n721] with difficulty.” {56}

The Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas, having heard the inconceivable and measureless benefits of the qualities that come from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, through wishing not to be fearful, wishing not to be terrified, and not to be gripped by terror, will become learned in the teaching of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. Aspire to the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. Be wise in asking questions about the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. Be wise in seeking the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. Do not be fearful, do not be terrified, and do not be gripped by terror on hearing the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha.” ^F67b

The youth Candraprabha placed his palms together, bowed toward the Bhagavān, and asked him, “Bhagavān, in this way how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas aspire to the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, become wise in asking questions about the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, become wise in seeking the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, and not be fearful, not be terrified, and not be gripped by terror on hearing the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha?”

The Bhagavān replied to the youth Candraprabha, “Those bodhisattva mahāsattvas who listen to and hear this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, and obtain it, understand it, keep it, read it out loud, disseminate it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others, will become wise in the teaching of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. They will aspire to the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, they will become wise in asking questions about the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, and will not be fearful, will not be terrified, and will not be gripped by terror on hearing the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha.” [n722]

“After the youth Candraprabha had been taught by the Bhagavān these words on accomplishing the benefits of the qualities that come from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, he again heard from the Bhagavān countless, innumerable verses [n723] describing the benefits of the qualities that come from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena; and it was at that time that the youth Candraprabha attained this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. [n724]

Innumerable, countless bodhisattva mahāsattvas attained the great, higher cognitions.  Countless beings also developed the motivation that is directed toward great compassion. ^F68a

This universe of a thousand million worlds shook in six ways. It trembled, trembled strongly, and trembled intensely; it quivered, quivered strongly, and quivered intensely; it shook, shook strongly, and shook intensely; it shuddered, shuddered strongly, and shuddered intensely; it quaked, quaked strongly, and quaked intensely; the east sank and the west rose, the west sank and the east rose, the north sank and the south rose, the south sank and the north rose, the perimeter sank and the center rose, and the center sank and the perimeter rose. An immeasurable radiance shone in the universe. There fell a great rain of divine incense. Devas and their sons gathered in order to listen to the Dharma. High in the sky they heard the innumerable verses on the benefits of the qualities that come from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. All the devas and their sons felt pleased, delighted, thrilled, joyous, happy, and glad, and they emitted cries of joy [n725] and laughter. They let fall a great rain of divine flowers of various kinds. They played many thousands of trillions of divine musical instruments. And they proclaimed the following words together as one voice:

“Aho! [n726] We have obtained something that is excellent to obtain. We have heard the innumerable verses on the benefits of the qualities from the Bhagavān. Bhagavān, just as the bodhisattva mahāsattva, the youth Candraprabha, attained this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, we also, Bhagavān, will all together at the same time attain this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena.” ^F68b

At the time when the Bhagavān was teaching the Dharma on Vulture Peak Mountain to the assembly that was like an ocean, the gandharva [n727] Pañcaśikha, in order to honor and serve him, descended from the sky accompanied by the sound of five hundred musical instruments, and remained before the Bhagavān.

The gandharva Pañcaśikha thought, “Just as I [n728] render service and honor in Sudharma before the devas of Trāyastriṃśa and Śakra, the lord of the devas, by singing them songs, in that same way I shall sing in order to make an offering to the god of gods, the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.”

Then the gandharva Pañcaśikha stood up before the Bhagavān holding a lute, the body of which was made of beryl. He was accompanied by the music [n729] of five hundred other gandharvas [n730] holding musical instruments.

The Bhagavān thought, “I shall perform a miracle so that the youth Candraprabha will attain skill in the realization of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, so that he will not waver from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, and so that I may manifest the gandharva Pañcaśikha’s skill in singing and playing the lute.”

Then the Bhagavān performed that miracle, and through the power of the Buddha the five hundred instruments were played excellently. From that excellent playing there came the sound of the inconceivable meaning, which was united [n731] with the true nature. And these verses of the realization of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha were sung: [n732]

“Within the breadth of one hair there are as many buddhas<br>As the number of grains of sand in the Ganges.<br>And those jinas have as many buddha realms, too,<br>Each one separate and with distinct characteristics. {1}

“Within the breadth of one hair there are the five kinds of beings:<br>The beings in hell, those who are animals,<br>Those in the realm of Yama, the devas, and humans,<br>Without overlapping or being squeezed. [n733] {2} ^F69a

“Within that space there are the lakes and oceans,<br>All rivers, and similarly ponds and springs,<br>Without overlapping or being squeezed.<br>In that way the Buddha’s Dharma is inconceivable. {3}

“Within that space there are numerous mountains:<br>Cakravāla, Meru, and Sumeru,<br>Mucilinda and Mahāmucilinda,<br>Vindhya, Gṛdhrakūṭa, and Himavat. {4}

“Within that space there are the terrible hells,<br>The horrible Tāpana and Pratāpana.<br>Those who have fallen into those hells<br>Experience the sensation of suffering. {5}

“Within that space there are divine palaces,<br>Twelve [n734] yojanas in size and beautiful. [n735]<br>Within them there are many thousands of devas [n736]<br>Who experience bliss in divine pleasures. {6}

“Within that space there are the births of buddhas.<br>There is illumination from the teaching of those who know the world.<br>Those [n737] who have not trained in pure conduct<br>And who have no wisdom will not see them. {7}

“Within that space they hear the words,<br>‘The Dharma has ceased, the Guide has passed away.’<br>Within that space there are some who hear,<br>‘The Guide lives and he teaches the Dharma.’ {8}

“Within that space there are some who perceive<br>That they live for countless years.<br>Within that space there are those whose time is ending.<br>They hear the words, ‘You have not long to live.’ {9}

“Within that space there are some who have the perception,<br>Believing what their mind perceives,<br>Of seeing and making offerings to sugatas [n738] and pleasing the buddhas.<br>Yet there is no arising and no making of offerings. {10}

“A man dreams he is in a house<br>Experiencing the bliss of sensory pleasures.<br>When he awakes he does not see those pleasures. [n739]<br>He knows that it was a dream. {11}

“In that way, what is seen, heard, thought, or known, [n740]<br>All of this is unreal, like a dream.<br>The one who has attained the samādhi<br>Will know this nature of phenomena. {12}

“For people such as this there is no pleasure or displeasure.<br>They are always perfectly happy in the world.<br>Those who delight in vast forests<br>Become perfectly happy mendicants. {13} ^F69b

“Those who have no thought of ‘mine,’<br>Those who have abandoned all attachments,<br>Wander in the world like rhinoceroses<br>And roam like the wind through the air. {14}

“Meditation on the path, the development of wisdom,<br>The emptiness and selflessness of all phenomena:<br>He who meditates on these Dharmas<br>Will have unending confidence. {15}

“The people in the world whose minds have no attachment,<br>They are perfectly happy in this world.<br>Their minds are always like the wind,<br>Knowing no attachment to pleasure or displeasure. {16}

“It is suffering to be with that which is unpleasant;<br>It is suffering to be separated from that which is pleasant.<br>Finally abandoning both of these,<br>Those happy people delight in the Dharma. {17}

“The one who has attachment on hearing this Dharma,<br>And animosity on hearing that which is not Dharma,<br>Goes astray through conceit and pride,<br>And overpowered by pride, experiences suffering. {18}

“Those who remain in equanimity<br>Are always free of arrogance and depression.<br>When faced with the pleasant and the unpleasant<br>They always have a liberated mind. {19}

“Those who maintain perfectly pure correct conduct,<br>Who remain always in inconceivable dhyāna<br>And delight in the peace of the forests,<br>Will never know the arising of doubts. {20}

“Those who engage in that which is unreal,<br>The fools who are always enjoying sensory pleasures<br>Like vultures attracted to a corpse,<br>They always fall under the power of Namuci.” [n741] {21}

When these verses had been created through the sound of the lutes, [n742] the youth Candraprabha attained skill in the realization of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha; the gandharva Pañcaśikha attained the patience that was in accord with that sound; countless beings, both devas and humans, developed the aspiration to the highest, complete enlightenment;  and countless beings were benefitted. ^F70a

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this Dharma teaching of entering great compassion and wish to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood quickly should rely upon all roots of merit, training, qualities, and completely pure conduct.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have few involvements, avoid bad companions, rely on kalyāṇamitras, have an inquiring nature, unrelentingly seek the Dharma, have the Dharma as their goal, desire the Dharma, delight in the Dharma, obtain the Dharma, and practice the Dharma in accord with the Dharma will, young man, develop great compassion for beings and will develop the aspiration for the highest, complete enlightenment.

“Moreover, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this Dharma teaching of entering great compassion and wish to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood quickly should be diligent, without regard for life or body, and should continuously seek kalyāṇamitras who teach this Dharma teaching of entering great compassion, and unwaveringly serve them, rely upon them, and honor them.

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who with a higher motivation seek kalyāṇamitras should hear from them the Dharma teaching of entering great compassion, and should obtain it, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation,  promulgate it, and make it widely known to others. They should, with joy and veneration, perceive as the Teacher the person from whom they hear this Dharma teaching on entering great compassion. ^F70b

“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas search for kalyāṇamitras, and respect them and serve them without weariness, at that time, young man, those bodhisattva mahāsattvas easily attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood and they obtain this Dharma teaching on easily entering great compassion.

“Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas should constantly seek for kalyāṇamitras as if their head or clothing were on fire, and unwaveringly attend upon them, serve them, and venerate them.

“Why is that? Young man, for bodhisattva mahāsattvas the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, not even to speak of this Dharma teaching on entering great compassion, depends upon kalyāṇamitras.

“Therefore, young man, you should always practice by thinking, ‘I will not weary of seeking kalyāṇamitras, venerating them, and serving them.’ ”

Thereupon the Bhagavān, in order to make clear this Dharma teaching on entering great compassion, gave the youth Candraprabha the teaching that had been given in the past in detail in the form of the following verses: [n743]

“Many incalculable, innumerable,<br>Inconceivable millions of eons in the past,<br>There was the highest of humans,<br>The Guide named Indra­ketu­dhvaja­rāja. {1}

“He taught this samādhi of peace<br>In which there is no human, soul, or person:<br>‘All phenomena are like the moon on water,<br>Illusions, bubbles, mirages, and lightning. {2}

“ ‘There is no human, no descendant of Manu, to be found<br>Who goes to the next world when his time has come to an end.<br>However, the karma that has been created will not disappear,<br>But will give corresponding black or white results. {3} ^F71a

“ ‘This is the excellent doorway of the way of logic,<br>The subtle, difficult-to-see realm of experience of the jinas.<br>The Bhagavān knows the enlightenment of buddhahood<br>In which there are there no words or letters to be found. {4}

“ ‘Vast retention and the accumulation of wisdom<br>Come from a hundred thousand trillion sūtras.<br>The Bhagavān teaches the samādhi<br>That is the field of experience of a hundred thousand trillion buddhas. {5}

“ ‘This frees the sick from their illness.<br>It is the wealth accomplished by bodhisattvas.<br>It is praised and extolled by all buddhas;<br>A hundred thousand trillion devas make offerings to it. {6}

“ ‘It is condemned by all foolish beings, [n744]<br>And the tīrthikas always reject it.<br>It is the supreme wealth of conduct that is praised by the buddhas.<br>It is as undefiled as lightning in the sky. {7}

“ ‘Those who make offerings to millions of jinas<br>Are wise in the practice of generosity and correct conduct,<br>Have forsaken their previous bad companions,<br>And have an unsurpassable inheritance of wealth.’ [n745] {8}

“There was present a bhikṣu, a dharmabhāṇaka,<br>A celibate who was the heart son of the Sugata.<br>When he had heard this benevolent Dharma,<br>He developed the aspiration to be a guide of the world. [n746] {9}

“The Guide, Indra­ketu­dhvaja­rāja,<br>Said to the dharmabhāṇaka,<br>‘Bhikṣu, develop the supreme, difficult-to-attain<br>Motivation for the highest enlightenment. {10}

“ ‘Maintain the conduct that is like a precious jewel,<br>Always depend on favorable friends,<br>Never depend on friends whose actions are evil<br>And before long you will attain buddha wisdom.’ {11}

“The one who developed the aspiration to enlightenment<br>In the presence of Indra­ketu­dhvaja­rāja<br>Became a supreme dharmabhāṇaka,<br>A celibate who was the heart son of the Sugata.” [n747] {12}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas should entertain no misgivings about all the teachings on the root of merits, the training, and the qualities. [n748] They should have few involvements, avoid bad companions, rely on kalyāṇamitras, have an inquiring nature, unrelentingly seek the Dharma, have the Dharma as their goal, desire the Dharma, delight in the Dharma, obtain the Dharma, and practice the Dharma in accord with the Dharma. They should perceive every buddha and bodhisattva as the teacher. They should with joy and veneration perceive as the teacher the person from whom they hear this Dharma teaching.

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who adopt and follow this Dharma teaching of entertaining no misgivings about all the teachings on the root of merits, the training, and the qualities will quickly display unending confidence of speech. They will accomplish [n749] the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. They will realize the profound Dharma of the Buddha. They will be like a light that dispels the darkness of perplexity, uncertainty, and doubt of the people of the world and the devas.”

Then at that time, in order to relate this Dharma teaching of entertaining no misgivings about all the teachings on the root of merits, the training, and the qualities, he spoke to the youth Candraprabha these verses that told of the past. [n750]

“In the past, in this world named Jambudvīpa, [n751]<br>There were two excellent sons [n752] who were not heedless.<br>They entered homelessness in the teaching of a sugata,<br>And dwelt like rhinoceroses in a grove of trees. {1}

“They had miraculous powers and had attained the four dhyānas,<br>They were very learned and skilled in composing poetry and texts,<br>They had mastered levitating up into the air,<br>And they could travel freely through the sky. {2} ^F72a

“They were engaged in conversation<br>In that cool grove of trees<br>That was filled with a variety of beautiful flowers<br>And attended by flocks of varieties of birds. {3}

“A king who was pursuing a deer<br>Heard their voices and entered that grove.<br>The monarch saw the two dharmabhāṇakas<br>And with the greatest joy he approached them. {4}

“They addressed each other agreeably<br>And the king sat down before them.<br>The king’s multitudinous army<br>Of sixty quintillion soldiers approached. {5}

“Then both of those dharmabhāṇakas<br>Said to the king, ‘Listen, Kṣatriya! [n753]<br>It is very difficult to reach supreme buddhahood.<br>Monarch, always be careful! {6}

“ ‘Life is always passing and never stays.<br>It passes as quickly as a mountain stream.<br>From the torment of illness, misery, and aging<br>You have no other refuge than good actions. [n754] {7}

“ ‘Supreme king, [n755] be a protector of the Dharma.<br>Guard the teaching of the one with ten strengths<br>In this utterly terrible time of degeneration.<br>Remain on the side of Dharma, supreme king!’ {8}

“Thus the wise ones at that time<br>Gave much advice to that sovereign,<br>Following which the monarch, with the other six quintillions, [n756]<br>Developed the aspiration to enlightenment. {9}

“When the supreme king had heard the Dharma,<br>He was joyful, very happy, and enraptured<br>With those who had spoken it so gently and pleasantly,<br>And bowed down to their feet before departing. {10}

“Under that king there were many other bhikṣus<br>Who desired gain and who entered homes.<br>When he saw how dissimilar was their conduct<br>The king did not show them respect. {11}

“The teacher of the teaching had passed away<br>And this was the time of the latter years.<br>There were very few worthy recipients in Jambudvīpa,<br>And there were present many who were without self-control. {12}

“The many bhikṣus, who were desirous and greedy,<br>Yearned for acquisitions, held the view of objective reality,<br>And had fallen away from the Sugata’s teaching,<br>At that time repeatedly urged the king to action. {13} ^F72b

“ ‘You must kill those two dharmabhāṇakas.<br>They are tīrthikas who are teaching nihilism.<br>Among those who have adopted that practice for a long time<br>There are none who have attained nirvāṇa. {14}

“ ‘They deny karma, they deny ripening;<br>Those imposters teach that there are no skandhas.<br>Your Majesty, banish them from the land<br>And then the Dharma will remain for a long time.’ {15}

“When he had listened to what they had to say,<br>The elephant-like king became distrustful.<br>‘I shall kill these two dharmabhāṇakas.<br>I must not leave them alone, for that would be harmful.’ [n757] {16}

“The king was attended by a goddess [n758]<br>Who had practiced with him in a previous lifetime.<br>She was wise and had benefited him for a long time,<br>And at this time she said to the sovereign king, {17}

“ ‘Kṣatriya, [n759] do not think in this way<br>Because of what bad associates have said.<br>Do not kill [n760] those two wise dharmabhāṇakas<br>Because of what bad associates have said. {18}

“ ‘Lord of men, do you not remember even a little<br>Of what they said to you in the forest grove?<br>In this perfectly terrible time of degeneration,<br>Remain on the side of Dharma, elephant-like king!’  [n761] {19}

“The king, inspired by those true words,<br>Did not abandon the teachings of the jinas. [n762]<br>But the king had a cruel brother<br>Who was persuaded by those around him. [n763] {19b–20a} [n764]

“They told him, ‘The king, your brother, is wicked;<br>He has no joy in being alive. [n765]<br>Those two bhikṣus possess dreadful spells.<br>With those spells they can fly through the sky. [n766] {20}

“ ‘Having heard this we have come to you,<br>To tell you all that has occurred.<br>Quickly kill those dreadful magicians,<br>Or afterward you will be filled with regret.’ {21}

“Then the king’s brother [n767] put on his armor,<br>Under the influence of those bad associates.<br>The king’s brother, encircled by his entire army,<br>Came to the forest where the two bhikṣus dwelt. {22}

“The nāgas and yakṣas that lived in that forest<br>Knew the intention of the king’s dreadful, cruel brother<br>And hurled upon them a rain of bricks and stones<br>That killed the king’s brother and his army. {23} ^F73a

“See how the life of the king’s cruel brother came to an end<br>Because he listened to what bad associates said.<br>Those who were angry at the dharmabhāṇakas<br>Took rebirth sixty times in the Avīci hell. {24}

“Those numerous bhikṣus who believed in reality<br>And drove the kṣatriya king to action<br>Experienced the sufferings of hell<br>For countless billons of rebirths. {25}

“The goddess who influenced the king<br>And protected the dharmabhāṇakas<br>Saw buddhas as numerous as sand grains in ten million Ganges,<br>Made offerings to them, and engaged in practice. {26}

“The multitudinous six quintillion men,<br>Who with the king had heard the Dharma<br>And developed the aspiration to enlightenment,<br>Became buddhas in numerous different realms. {27}

“Their lifespans were many millions of eons.<br>They had inconceivable, unequaled wisdom.<br>They all taught this excellent samādhi,<br>And then those supreme humans passed into nirvāṇa. {28}

“Having heard this unsurpassable teaching<br>On the accumulation of correct conduct, purity, qualities, and wisdom,<br>You must practice intently, without distraction,<br>And quickly attain the wisdom of buddhahood. [n768] {29}

“Look upon us, you tathāgatas in the ten directions,<br>Who have peaceful minds and compassionate, loving eyes.<br>You are the refuge and protection for all beings.<br>Send down your rain of Dharma upon the world. [n769] {30}

“Do not think that those two young men,<br>Those perfect sons, [n770] were anyone else:<br>Dīpaṃkara was at that time one of them,<br>And I was the second dharmabhāṇaka. {30a}

“At that time Maitreya was the king [n771]<br>Who listened favorably to the Dharma.<br>And you, young man, at that time,<br>Were the wise goddess who wished to help. {30b}

“At that time, Devadatta<br>Was the king’s brother,<br>Influenced by the acquisitive bhikṣus<br>Who said, ‘Kill those two dharmabhāṇakas.’ ” {30c} ^F73b

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should have no attachment to their life or body. Why is that? Because, young man, beings accomplish bad actions due to attachment to their lives and bodies. [n772]

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have no attachment to their life and body will not even find it difficult to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, not to mention this samādhi. Therefore, young man, have no attachment to your life and body. That is how you should practice.”

It was said concerning this:

“Foolish beings always unceasingly<br>Have strong attachment to the putrid body.<br>Grasping at life, and for the sake of happiness,<br>The unwise always commit bad actions. {i}

Those who do not know attachment<br>To body and life, which have no essence,<br>Will defeat the armies of Māra<br>And realize enlightenment at the foot of the Bodhi tree. {ii}

Those who have attachment to these two things—<br>The body that is empty and selfless,<br>And life, which is like a dream or a fleeting dewdrop—<br>Those people will go to hell when they die. {iii}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should not know the Tathāgata to be the rūpakāya. [n773] Why is that? It is because the Buddha Bhagavān manifests because of the dharmakāya and does not manifest because of the rūpakāya. ^F74a

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas whose wish is to aspire to the body of the tathāgata, who wish to know the body of the tathāgata, should obtain this samādhi, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with dedication to the practice of meditation, and make it widely known to others.

“Young man, the body of the tathāgata [n774] is taught to be one meaning, [n775] with the understanding that it arises from a hundred merits. It arises from the Dharma. [n776] It is without attributes. It is devoid of all attributes. It is profound. [n777] It is immeasurable. It is an immeasurable phenomenon. [n778] It has the nature of the absence of attributes. [n779] It is free of all attributes. [n780] It is unwavering. [n781] It has no location. It completely has the nature of space. It is invisible. It transcends the scope of the eye’s vision. That should be known as the dharmakāya. [n782]

“It is inconceivable. It is beyond the level of thought. It is unaffected by bliss or suffering. It transcends all conceptual elaboration. [n783] It has no location, [n784] because it transcends the scope of the words of those who aspire to the wisdom of buddhahood. It is the quintessence [n785] because it transcends desire. It is indivisible because it transcends anger. [n786] It is stable because it transcends the scope of ignorance. It is taught through the teaching of emptiness. It is unborn because it transcends birth. [n787] It is ‘permanent’ in terms of words, and terminology is empty. [n788] It is undifferentiated because it is nirvāṇa. [n789] It is ‘nirvāṇa’ [n790] because of a word. It is ‘peace’ because of speaking. [n791] There is equality in terms of conventional appellations. [n792] There are appellations in terms of ultimate truth. There is ultimate truth through correct speech. [n793]

“It is calmness, the absence of anguish. [n794] It is groundless, [n795] and cannot be comprehended. [n796] There is no end to its description. [n797]

“Young man, it arises from training in the great, higher cognitions, and it is known as the tathāgatakāya.”

Thereupon, the Bhagavān spoke these verses: ^F74b

“Someone who wishes to know<br>This body of the Lord of the World [n798]<br>Should meditate on this samādhi,<br>And then they will know the Buddha’s body. [n799] {1}

“A buddha’s body is born from merit. [n800]<br>It [n801] is pure and it is brilliant.<br>It is the same as space;<br>There is no difference between them. {2}

“The characteristics of a buddha<br>Are the same as those of enlightenment.<br>The characteristics of the body<br>Are the same as those characteristics. {3}

“The body has enlightenment’s characteristics<br>And a buddha realm has the same.<br>The strengths, liberations, and dhyānas<br>Are all also a single characteristic. {4}

“That is the nature of the emergence<br>Of the buddhas, of the lords of worlds.<br>There is no being who with physical eyes<br>Is able to see their bodies. {5}

“There are many who declare,<br>‘I have seen the guide of the world.<br>He is the color of gold and his body<br>Illuminates the entire world.’ {6}

“This body that is seen,<br>Beautified by characteristics,<br>Is a manifestation through the power<br>Of the blessing of the buddhas. {7}

“The Buddha’s body is displayed<br>As having a height and a width,<br>But that body cannot be measured,<br>And therefore it is inconceivable. {8}

“If the Buddha’s body could be measured<br>And found to be of a certain size,<br>Then the Teacher would be the same<br>As a deva or a human. {9}

“That characteristic is the ripening<br>Of a mind in meditation.<br>There will be pure, radiant names-and-form<br>That have that characteristic. {10}

“There is no being whatsoever<br>Who has meditated on this samādhi of peace<br>It is in that way that the Lord of the World<br>Has practiced for millions of eons. {11}

“I have developed this samādhi<br>Through a multitude of good qualities.<br>Because of the vastness of that samādhi<br>My body cannot be seen. {12}

“As is someone’s mind,<br>So are their names-and-form;<br>The mind that has no nature of its own<br>Has names-and-form with that characteristic. {13}

“Those who have a gross perception<br>Of names-and-form,<br>Their inharmonious perception<br>Gives rise to a mind that is gross. {14} ^F75a

“Those who have a subtle perception<br>Within their names-and-form<br>Will have a mind that is radiant<br>And without attachment to names-and-form. {15}

“I remember that in my previous lives<br>During seven countless eons,<br>The three bad perceptions [n802]<br>Never arose in me at any time. {16}

“My mind has been undefiled<br>For countless millions of eons.<br>I bring benefit to beings<br>And my body is not visible. {17}

“The one whose mind<br>Is liberated from existents<br>Will never again be<br>Connected with existents. {18}

“My consciousness is liberated<br>Completely from all things.<br>I know the nature of the mind,<br>So that henceforth wisdom will arise. {19}

“My emanations proceed<br>To thousands of millions of realms.<br>There they benefit beings<br>Though there is no body to be found. {20}

“Without characteristics, without attributes,<br>It is the same as space.<br>My body is indescribable.<br>It is taught to be difficult to understand. {21}

“The dharmakāya, the great hero,<br>Is a body born from the Dharma.<br>The Jina cannot be made known<br>By means of the rūpakāya. {22}

“Māra will find no opportunity<br>To cause harm to the one<br>Who has felt joy on hearing<br>These words that have been taught. {23}

“Those who have heard the profound Dharma<br>And have not been frightened by it,<br>Will not even for the sake of their lives<br>Forsake the enlightenment of buddhahood. {24}

“They will know the truth that is taught<br>In thousands of millions of sūtras.<br>They will be a light for the world<br>Wherever it is that they will go. [n803] {25}

“Young man, the body of the Tathāgata is not easily known through attributes or actions. It is blue, or is colored blue, or is like blue, or shines with blue light; or it is yellow, or is colored yellow, or is like yellow, or shines with yellow light; or it is red, or is colored red, or is like red,  or shines with red light; or it is white, or is colored white, or is like white, or shines with white light; or it is madder, or is colored madder, or is like madder, or shines with madder light; or it is crystal, or is crystal-colored, or is like crystal, or shines with crystal light; or it is fire, or is fire-colored, or is like fire, or shines with fire light; or it is distilled ghee, or is ghee-colored, or is like ghee, or shines with ghee-colored light; or it is gold, or is gold-colored, or is like gold, or shines with golden light; or it is beryl, or is beryl-colored, or is like beryl, or shines with beryl light; or it is lightning, or is lightning-colored, or is like lightning, or shines with lightning’s light; or it is Brahmā, or is Brahmā-colored, or is like Brahmā, or shines with Brahmā’s light; or it is a deva, or is deva-colored, or is like a deva, or shines with a deva’s light. It is not easy to know it. ^F75b

“Young man, in that way the body of the tathāgata is pure. It cannot be conceived of through attributes, and so it is taught to be inconceivable. It cannot be conceived of [n804] through any attribute, and so it is taught to be inconceivable. It cannot be conceived of through external appearances. It is immeasurable. The beings and devas of this world cannot easily grasp its extent even through the perfect rūpakāya.” [n805]

The Bhagavān then spoke these verses:

“All the particles in the world<br>And all that can be conceived of as dust,<br>And all the water that is in springs,<br>Lakes, ponds, and the ocean— {26}

“One may ask how many particles there are,<br>But one can never find the end.<br>Even if, with the tip of a hair, one could measure out<br>How much water there is in an ocean, [n806] {26–27}

“Even that could not be taught<br>As an analogy for the Lord of the World.<br>There are countless drops of water<br>And it is the same for atoms, {27} ^F76a

“But I see that even a single sentient being<br>Has far more numerous<br>Aspirations and motivations<br>That are developed at numerous times. [n807] {28}

“Yet even the aspirations of all beings<br>Are not adequate as an analogy<br>For those qualities of the body<br>That I have indicated. {29}

“One cannot [n808] through [n809] attributes and actions<br>Know the appearance of these kinds<br>Of qualities [n810] of a buddha,<br>And that is my distinctive characteristic. {30}

“The buddhas are devoid of attributes.<br>They are the manifestation of the dharmakāya.<br>They are profound and immeasurable,<br>And therefore the buddhas are inconceivable. {31}

“The inconceivable buddha body<br>Of a buddha is also inconceivable.<br>Those bodies are inconceivable.<br>They are the manifestation of the dharmakāya. {32}

“The mind is incapable of conceiving<br>The bodies of the buddhas.<br>One cannot, therefore, obtain<br>The measure of such a body. {33}

“Those immeasurable qualities<br>I have practiced for ten million eons.<br>Therefore have I accomplished<br>A body that is inconceivable and radiant, too. {34}

“There is no being that can grasp it<br>Or that can obtain its measure.<br>In that way the body of a buddha<br>Is inconceivable and immeasurable. {35}

“Because the qualities are immeasurable<br>There is no measure that can be conceived for them. [n811]<br>Because the qualities are not conceived<br>The buddha also is inconceivable. {36}

“The measured is taught to be a conception;<br>The measureless is nonconceptual.<br>That which is not conceived is without conception;<br>Therefore the buddha is inconceivable. {37}

“Just as space is limitless<br>And no one is able to measure it,<br>Likewise a buddha’s body<br>Is just the same as space. {38}

“Those who thus know the body<br>Of the buddhas are the progeny of the jinas.<br>They will also become buddhas,<br>Inconceivable lords of worlds.” {39}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha,  “Young man, aspiring bodhisattva mahāsattvas think, ‘How can I make manifest the four discernments? What are these four? They are the discernment of meaning, the discernment of phenomena, the discernment of definitions, and the discernment of eloquence. I shall manifest these four!’ On having this thought, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas should obtain this samādhi, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, and make it widely known to others. ^F76b

“Young man, what is the discernment of phenomena?

“Young man, however many words there can be for forms, the tathāgata has that many appellations for them. [n812] It is the same for sensation, identification, mentation; and, young man, for consciousnesses. Young man, in that way there are infinite, endless, inconceivably numerous [n813] words for forms, and the tathāgata, too has inconceivably numerous appellations for them. It is the same for sensation, identification, mentation, and, young man, for consciousnesses: there are infinite, endless, inconceivably numerous words for them, and the tathāgata, too has inconceivably numerous appellations for them. [n814]

“Young man, there are countless faults in those composite phenomena; there are also countless benefits in nirvāṇa, and the tathāgata, too, has that many countless appellations. Young man, as numerous as are the names for nirvāṇa, the tathāgata has that many appellations.  Thus, young man, there are countless names of nirvāṇa, and the tathāgata, too, has that many appellations. ^F77a

“Young man, the tathāgata has spoken of four kinds of appellations that are inconceivably numerous because it is not easy to state that there is an end to them. What are these four? They are the inconceivably numerous appellations in regard to the composite, the inconceivably numerous appellations for sounds, the inconceivably numerous appellations for kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous appellations for purification. Young man, those are the tathāgata’s four kinds of inconceivably numerous appellations. Young man, those four, the tathāgata’s inconceivably numerous appellations, are taught to be inconceivably numerous as it is not easy to state that there is an end to them. To understand what those four are, they should be taught in detail.

“Young man, there are the four ways of the bodhisattvas. What are the four ways? They are the inconceivably numerous ways of the composite, the inconceivably numerous ways of teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous ways of the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous ways of purification. Those are the four.

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of reasoning. [n815] What are the four kinds of reasoning? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of reasoning concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of reasoning concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of reasoning concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of reasoning concerning purification. Those are the four.

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of doorways. What are the four kinds of doorways? They are the inconceivably numerous doorways concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous doorways concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous doorways concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous doorways concerning purification. Those are the four.

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of elucidation. What are the four kinds of elucidation?  They are the inconceivably numerous elucidations concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous elucidations concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous elucidations concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous elucidations concerning purification. Those are the four. ^F77b

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of speaking. What are the four kinds of speaking? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of speaking concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of speaking concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of speaking concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of speaking concerning purification. Those are the four.

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of words. What are the four kinds of words? They are the inconceivably numerous words concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous words concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous words concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous words concerning purification. Those are the four.

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of recitation. What are the four kinds of recitation? They are the inconceivably numerous recitations concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous recitations concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous recitations concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous recitations concerning purification. Those are the four.

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of pertinent speech. What are the four kinds of pertinent speech? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of pertinent speech concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of pertinent speech concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of pertinent speech concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of pertinent speech concerning purification. Those are the four.

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of comprehension of the devas. What are the four kinds of comprehension of the devas? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of comprehension of the devas concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of comprehension of the devas concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of comprehension of the devas concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of comprehension of the devas concerning purification.  Those are the four. ^F78a

Those are the four. ^F82b

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of the individual. What are the four kinds of knowledge of the individual? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the individual concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the individual concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the individual concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the individual concerning purification. Those are the four.

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of apprehensions. What are the four kinds of knowledge of apprehensions? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions concerning purification. Those are the four.

“Young man, those are the four inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions that are taught to be inconceivably numerous. It is not easy to state an end to them.

“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of retention. What are the four kinds of retention? The first retention is of what is known concerning the teaching of all infinite composites. The second retention is of what is known concerning the teaching of all infinite sounds. The third retention is of what is known concerning the teaching of all infinite kleśas. The fourth retention is of what is known concerning the teaching of all infinite purifications. Those are the four retentions. The four retentions are those.

“So it is in these ways that there is the discernment of phenomena through knowing phenomena.

“The discernment of meaning is the meaning in the knowledge of phenomena. ^F83a

“The discernment of definitions is delight [n827] in the knowledge of phenomena.

“Young man, the discernment of eloquence is teaching terminology, explaining, expounding, [n828] clarifying, [n829] disseminating, [n830] analyzing, differentiating, proclaiming, [n831] having unimpeded speech, having unalloyed [n832] speech, not being mute, [n833] not stammering, [n834] and speaking without loss of confidence in relation to the knowledge of phenomena.”

Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:

“As numerous as are the knowledges of the Buddha,<br>There are that many designations for forms.<br>As numerous as are the designations for forms,<br>There are that many appellations of forms. [n835] {1}

“As numerous as are the appellations of forms,<br>There are that many names for conduct.<br>As numerous as are the names for conduct,<br>There are that many names of buddhas. {2}

“As numerous as are the names of buddhas,<br>There are that many names of beings.<br>I know [n836] whatever number of names<br>Even one single being has. {3}

“The names for conduct, names of buddhas,<br>And names of beings are equal<br>To the infinity of names and appellations<br>That I have previously taught. {4}

“As numerous as are the faults in the composite,<br>There are that many qualities [n837] in nirvāṇa.<br>I have taught as many analogies<br>As there are qualities of the buddhas. {5}

“As numerous as are the motivations<br>That I have taught beings to have,<br>There are that many light rays<br>From a single hair of a Lord of the World. {6}

“As numerous as are the names<br>And aspirations of all beings,<br>A lord of humans has even more<br>Qualities of the aspects of his speech. {7}

“The names of all beings that have been taught<br>To be those of one being<br>Are the names of one being<br>That have been taught to be those of all beings. {8}

“The Buddha has taught<br>This engagement with discernment. [n838]<br>Infinite names have been taught<br>For the sake of the bodhisattvas. {9}

“Those who wish to teach in some way<br>The endless millions of sūtras<br>Should recite this sūtra<br>And teach it with full confidence. {10} ^F83b

“They should teach in the middle of an assembly<br>Millions of sūtras without impediment.<br>They should teach the Dharma in the way<br>That space is without any limit. {11}

“In that way the bodhisattvas,<br>The pure beings, the protectors,<br>Having taken up this sūtra<br>Will become endowed with wisdom. {12}

“Through the way this path is taught<br>By those who have faith,<br>That is how wisdom grows,<br>Like a tree on a snow mountain.” {13}

“Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas who practice that discernment of phenomena, who view phenomena as phenomena, attain the highest, complete enlightenment?

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who practice that discernment of phenomena, who view phenomena as phenomena, do not perceive enlightenment as other than form. They do not approach enlightenment as other than form. They do not seek enlightenment as other than form. They do not attain enlightenment as other than form. They do not inspire beings to an enlightenment that is other than form. They do not see a tathāgata as other than form. They see a tathāgata in this way: ‘The Tathāgata is the fearlessness that is the nature of form.’ They do not see the tathāgata as other than form, as other than the nature of form. They do not see the nature of form as other than the tathāgata. The nature of that which is called form and that of the tathāgata are nondual. The bodhisattva mahāsattvas who see in that way are engaging in the discernment of phenomena.

“In that same way they do not perceive enlightenment as other than sensation, other than identification, other than mentation, or other than consciousness. They do not approach enlightenment as being other than consciousness. They do not seek enlightenment as other than consciousness. They do not attain enlightenment as other than consciousness. They do not inspire beings to an enlightenment that is other than consciousness. They do not see a tathāgata as other than consciousness. They see a tathāgata in this way: ‘The Tathāgata is the fearlessness that is the nature of consciousness.’ They do not see the tathāgata as other than consciousness, as other than the nature of consciousness. They do not see the nature of consciousness as other than the tathāgata. The nature of that which is called consciousness and that of the tathāgata are nondual. The bodhisattva mahāsattvas who see in that way are engaging in the discernment of phenomena.” [n839] ^F84a

Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:

“Enlightenment is taught through form;<br>Form is taught through enlightenment.<br>Through these dissimilar words<br>The highest of Dharma is taught. {1}

“The highest form is taught through words;<br>Its nature is profound.<br>Form and enlightenment are the same:<br>There is no difference that can be found. {2}

“Nirvāṇa is profound<br>And it is taught through words, [n840]<br>Yet nirvāṇa is not to be found<br>And words are not to be found. {3}

“Both words and nirvāṇa,<br>Neither of them are to be found.<br>Thus nirvāṇa has been taught<br>In terms of empty phenomena. {4}

“Nirvāṇa is not to be found<br>In saying ‘passed into nirvāṇa.’<br>There is no development of phenomena.<br>It is afterward just as it was before. {5}

“All phenomena are by nature<br>Exactly the same as nirvāṇa.<br>That is known by those dedicated to renunciation,<br>By those engaged in the Buddha’s teachings. {6} ^F84b

“Some say, ‘I have seen the Guide,<br>For I saw the Buddha’s body.’<br>But it is not possible for anyone<br>To see me because of my rūpakāya. {7}

“The known nature of form,<br>That is the characteristic of form.<br>When the nature of form is known,<br>Then my body is revealed. [n841] {8}

“In that way I know the characteristics<br>Of phenomena, of the five skandhas.<br>Knowing that nature of phenomena,<br>I remain in the dharmakāya. {9}

“I teach the Dharma to beings<br>Without departing from the dharmakāya. [n842]<br>But the qualities of the buddhas<br>Cannot be expressed in words. {10}

“Those who do not know this way<br>Listen to the Buddha’s words<br>And then merely say with words,<br>‘I have seen the Guide of humans.’ {11}

“Whoever casts off all conceptual identification<br>Brings to an end the identification of existence.<br>Whoever has a conceptual identification of words<br>Will never be able to see the Teacher. {12}

“Whoever knows emptiness<br>As the characteristic of form<br>Will not say that emptiness<br>Is other than the nature of form.<br>Whoever knows form,<br>Knows emptiness. [n843] {13}

“Whoever knows emptiness<br>As the characteristic of form<br>Will overcome and defeat<br>Tens of millions of māras. [n844] {14}

“Whoever knows form,<br>Knows emptiness.<br>Whoever knows emptiness,<br>Knows nirvāṇa. [n845] {15}

“Those who do not know this way,<br>Those who conceptualize, are lost. [n846]<br>They conceive of the unreal as being real<br>And the real as being unreal. [n847] {16}

“They are deceived by acquisitions through reputation [n848]<br>And wander far [n849] from my teaching.<br>They maintain the conception of a result<br>And lose all their wealth of mendicancy. {17}

“Those who are lazy and lacking in diligence,<br>Who do not maintain the aspect of conduct,<br>They will stand up and state,<br>‘That is not the teaching of the Buddha!’ {18} ^F85a

“Some of them will declare,<br>‘We are enlightened!’<br>But they will be uncontrolled, untrained,<br>And disrespectful to each other. {19}

“They will delight in words<br>And have no stability in the Dharma.<br>They will have that kind of aspiration,<br>Desiring what is gained through reputation. {20}

“They will be motivated to have a following.<br>They will delight in acquisition.<br>They will be overpowered by arrogance and carelessness.<br>Their goal will be gain and honors. {21}

“Based upon gains and honors<br>They will desire the intellect’s accomplishments.<br>They will build temples and stūpas.<br>Their interest will be in the women of families. {22}

“They will depend upon their perception.<br>They will dwell in craving and desire.<br>They will be within the realm of Māra<br>And they will do the work of laypeople. {23}

“Their desire will be like the flames of a fire.<br>They will give teachings to laypeople.<br>They will enter into their homes<br>And they will corrupt those families. {24}

“The laypeople will come to think of them<br>As their teachers.<br>They will take up residence with them<br>And they will corrupt their sons and daughters. {25}
