“The numerous inconceivable Dharmas<br>Are taught by using words.<br>Someone who is attached to words<br>Will not know the meaning of the teaching. {3} ^F104b

“How can someone teach the meaning<br>Who does not know the meaning behind the words?<br>Someone who has not learned what the true nature is<br>Teaches that which is not the Dharma as the Dharma. {4}

“The one meaning of the differing words<br>Of the sūtras that have been taught by me<br>Within thousands of worlds<br>Is something that cannot be stated. {5}

“Through contemplating a single word<br>All of them will be meditated on—<br>All of the many kinds of Dharma that have been taught<br>By however many buddhas there have been. {6}

“For people who have mastered the meaning<br>That all phenomena are selfless, [n1047]<br>When they have learned this word<br>The Dharmas of the Buddha will not be hard to attain. [n1048] {7}

“All phenomena are the Buddha’s Dharma. [n1049]<br>They who have learned the nature of phenomena,<br>They know the nature of phenomena<br>And do not contradict the nature of phenomena. {8}

“All words are the Buddha’s words,<br>As all words have no substance.<br>Although one seeks them in the ten directions<br>The words of the Buddha will not be found. {9}

“These words are the Buddha’s words.<br>Though one seeks them in the ten directions,<br>These unsurpassable words are not to be found.<br>They have never been found and never will be found. [n1050] {10}

“The Buddha’s words are unsurpassable.<br>There is nothing higher than the Buddha’s words.<br>There is not an atom of them that is to be found,<br>And that is why they are called unsurpassable. {11}

“An atom, a phenomenon, is not produced.<br>Although explanations use the term ‘atom,’<br>Something the size of an atom cannot be found;<br>It is a term used in teaching on the worldly level. {12}

“The unfindability of phenomena is found,<br>But that finding also cannot be found.<br>Thus they who know phenomena<br>Realize the highest enlightenment, {13}

“And having realized the highest enlightenment<br>They will turn the wheel of the Dharma.<br>Through turning the wheel of the Dharma<br>They teach the Buddha’s Dharma. {14}

“The bodhisattvas who realize<br>The highest wisdom of buddhahood,<br>Because of that are called buddhas,<br>As they have realized buddhahood’s wisdom. {15}

“The absence of existents, the absence of aspiration,<br>The absence of attributes, and emptiness—<br>It is these doorways to liberation<br>That the Buddha taught as doorways. {16}

“The eyes, the ears, and the nose,<br>The tongue, the body, and likewise the mind,<br>The buddhas have explained<br>That they are by nature empty. {17}

“They who know in that way<br>The nature of phenomena,<br>Knowing the characteristics of phenomena,<br>They will not be in disagreement with it. {18} ^F105a

“This is the realm of experience of the heroes,<br>Of the bodhisattvas, the protectors.<br>They know the emptiness of phenomena<br>And they never have any doubt. {19}

“Those who know the nature of phenomena,<br>Those ones are called a buddha.<br>They guide countless, innumerable<br>Beings to enlightenment. {20}

“That which is accomplished by the word buddha<br>Is also accomplished by the words correct conduct.<br>The words buddha and correct conduct<br>Have the same characteristic. {21}

“However many [n1051] words are spoken<br>Whether superior, middling, or lesser,<br>They are all taught in the one word meditation,<br>And in the one word buddha. {22}

“The Buddha’s Dharma [n1052] is stated<br>To have no location and no direction.<br>It has no birth and no cessation.<br>Neither is it single nor multiple. {23}

“It is not new and it is not old.<br>There is nothing to be proud of.<br>It is not blue and it is not yellow;<br>Neither is it white, nor red. {24}

“That which is taught through verses<br>Is inexpressible and ungraspable.<br>This miraculous activity of the Sage<br>Is beyond the level of verses. {25}

{26} [n1053]

“The buddha who has passed into nirvāṇa<br>Is seen in the form of a buddha.<br>The one who imagines that he is present<br>Will also see the buddha’s miracles. {27}

“When someone has reached nirvāṇa<br>There is no being that is to be found.<br>That is how the Dharma is taught<br>And many beings are liberated. {28}

“Just as the sun and moon<br>Appear in a bronze bowl<br>Without their own form going there,<br>Such is the nature of phenomena. {29}

“Those who know the nature<br>Of phenomena to be like reflections, [n1054]<br>They do not see the Buddha’s body<br>As being a body of form. [n1055] {30}

“This phenomenon has no body; [n1056]<br>There is no body in it at all.<br>A phenomenon has no body,<br>And that is the body of the Buddha. {31}

“Those who see the dharmakāya,<br>They are the ones who see the Guide.<br>The dharmakāyas [n1057] are the buddhas.<br>That is seeing the buddhas. {32} ^F105b

“That which is specified through dependence<br>Is specified to not be specific.<br>Those who wish to be renunciants<br>Should understand this approach. {33}

{34} [n1058]

“Whoever thinks, ‘I have attained,’<br>Is for that reason said to be without attainment.<br>The one who is said to be a renunciant<br>Is the one who thinks, ‘I have not attained renuncation.’ {35}

“Those who have not learned this profundity,<br>How can they teach the Dharma?<br>They cannot describe it<br>Through using profound words. {36}

“The five skandhas are insubstantial.<br>Being nonexistent they arise.<br>For the one to whom the skandhas arise,<br>There is nothing that arises. {37}

“Those characteristics of the skandhas<br>Are the characteristics of all phenomena.<br>Those characteristics are taught<br>But there are no characteristics that exist. {38}

“The characteristic of phenomena<br>Is the same as that of space and sky,<br>As seen in the past, the future,<br>And as in the present. {39}

“Space is taught to be ungraspable;<br>There is nothing there to be grasped.<br>That is the nature of phenomena:<br>It is ungraspable like space. {40}

“That is how phenomena are taught,<br>That there is nothing to be seen.<br>For the one who does not see phenomena,<br>Phenomena are beyond conception. {41}

“These phenomena have no nature;<br>They have no nature to be found.<br>For those dedicated to buddhahood’s enlightenment<br>This is the domain of the yogin. {42}

“The ones who know phenomena in that way<br>Will not have attachment to phenomena.<br>Not being attached to phenomena,<br>They understand the conceptualization of phenomena. {43}

“The bodhisattvas, the protectors,<br>Have annihilated all phenomena.<br>Having annihilated the conceptualization of phenomena<br>They do not become proud in the Buddha’s Dharma. {44}

“Having no pride in that preeminence,<br>They examine and teach that preeminence.<br>The ones who know that preeminence<br>Will have no pride throughout ten million eons. {45}

“The foolish examine that preeminence<br>And subsequently continue in saṃsāra.<br>It has no location that can be found<br>Even though one searches throughout the ten directions. {46}

“The bodhisattva, [n1059] knowing emptiness,<br>Has no attachment to saṃsāra. [n1060]<br>They [n1061] practice to attain enlightenment<br>But their practice cannot be found. {47} ^F106a

“Their passage cannot be found,<br>Like that of a bird through the sky.<br>The bodhisattvas realize<br>That nature of enlightenment. {48}

“Just as a well-trained conjurer<br>Is able to display illusions,<br>Although there are many kinds of forms<br>There is no form that can be grasped. {49}

“There is no pride in acquisition or nonacquisition,<br>As there is no acquisition in acquisition.<br>That wisdom is like an illusion,<br>And that illusion has no location. {50}

“Thus the understanding of fools<br>Is a conceptualization of empty phenomena.<br>Engaging in conceptualization,<br>They are doomed to the six existences. {51}

“Beings undergo rebirth and aging;<br>There is no end to their being reborn.<br>There is no end to the suffering<br>Of skandhas that are born and die. {52}

“The suffering of birth and saṃsāra<br>Is the conceptualization of foolish understanding.<br>This does not cease throughout eons;<br>Beings continue in saṃsāra for millions of eons. {53}

“They continue in the performance of activities,<br>Whether that of engagement or disengagement.<br>They delight in the actions they perform,<br>But those activities will not liberate them. {54}

“They are carried along on a river of actions,<br>And their actions will have no end.<br>They will die over and over,<br>Always dwelling in the realm of the māras. {55}

“Overpowered by the māras, with poor understanding,<br>They act through being afflicted by the kleśas.<br>They experience births and deaths<br>That take place in various worlds. {56}

“Those various beings who are blind fools,<br>They proceed toward death.<br>They are killed and destroyed,<br>And their existences are terrible. {57}

“Those with foolish understanding<br>Kill each other with weapons.<br>By continuing with that kind of activity<br>Their sufferings only increase. {58}

“Those with foolish understanding think,<br>‘My sons’ and ‘my wealth.’<br>They conceive of that which has no existence<br>And thereby continue to extend saṃsāra. {59}

“They who extend saṃsāra,<br>Those individuals continue in saṃsāra.<br>They each go their individual ways<br>And therefore they are called individual beings. {60}

“They reject the Buddha’s teaching<br>And teach numerous other doctrines.<br>They are under the power of Māra<br>And they will not attain liberation. {61} ^F106b

“These fools, because of their desires,<br>Have intercourse with putrid women.<br>They will be reborn as putrid beings,<br>Falling into the lower realms as a result. {62}

“The buddhas praise neither desire,<br>Nor having intercourse with women.<br>That is a terrifying noose,<br>The dreadful noose of women. {63}

“Those who are wise avoid it<br>Like a vicious poisonous snake.<br>They do not put their trust in women.<br>That is not the path to enlightenment. {64}

“They meditate on the path to enlightenment<br>That has been taught [n1062] by all the buddhas.<br>Having meditated on that path<br>They become unsurpassable buddhas. {65}

“Those who have become unsurpassable<br>Become shrines in the world.<br>With unsurpassable wisdom<br>They become unsurpassable buddhas. {66}

“They follow the poṣadha vows<br>And follow the path of correct conduct.<br>They lead toward enlightenment<br>Countless millions of beings. {67}

“They accomplish the benefit of<br>Innumerable, countless beings.<br>They are heroes with great wisdom<br>Who beat the drum of deathlessness. {68}

“They make the realm of Māra shudder;<br>They make the māras shake.<br>They lead to enlightenment<br>Countless millions of māras. {69}

“They overcome their opponents.<br>They defeat the tīrthikas.<br>They shake the entire earth<br>With its mountains and oceans. {70}

“The great leaders [n1063] through many transformations<br>Manifest miraculous manifestations of the body.<br>The great wise ones display<br>Inconceivable miracles. {71}

“They shake millions of realms<br>As numerous as the Ganges sands.<br>They defeat the māras<br>And are greatly famed buddhas. [n1064] {72}

“They manifest trees [n1065]<br>Adorned with jewels,<br>Aromatic and beautiful,<br>Bearing flowers and fruits. {73}

“Those heroes emanate<br>Delightful [n1066] mansions, [n1067]<br>Palaces and pinnacled halls,<br>And beautiful lotus ponds [n1068] {74} ^F107a

“Filled with water that has the eight qualities,<br>That is clear, cool, and unstained.<br>Those who drink that water<br>Cease yearning for the three existences. {75}

“They become irreversible,<br>Those who drink that supreme water.<br>Through supreme wisdom<br>They become supreme buddhas. {76}

“Know that they enter<br>The supreme way of peace.<br>Those who do not know that way,<br>Those focused on perceptions, [n1069] will perish. {77}

“The beings who follow that way,<br>And those who depend upon them,<br>Will fall into the great terror<br>Of unendurable Avīci. {78}

“The terrible sufferings there<br>Are beyond description,<br>But I and the bodhisattvas,<br>The protectors, know them. {79}

“They doubt the Dharma,<br>Which is profound and difficult to see.<br>It is not on the level of fools,<br>Those who remain focused on perceptions. {80}

“The manifestations of displays,<br>Of appearances of many forms,<br>They are all of them seen in<br>The supreme buddha realms. {81}

“All the appearances of manifested forms<br>That are in every buddha realm<br>Are all revealed here by bodhisattvas<br>With great miraculous powers. {82}

“Those great heroes with great strength<br>Wear the armor of the great Dharma.<br>They strike with the blows<br>Of the great vajra of the meaning of emptiness. {83}

“Many thousands of millions of light rays<br>As numerous as the sands in the Ganges<br>Are radiated from their bodies<br>And they illuminate the world. {84}

“They find no pleasure in women<br>And have no desire for them.<br>Those conceptions have been destroyed<br>Naturally with their conceptions of women. {85}

“Wherever those heroes are present,<br>Those buddha realms are not empty.<br>How could the māras and evil ones<br>Create an obstacle for them? {86}

“Those who remain in fabricated views<br>Displease a multitude of buddhas.<br>Those who are based upon maliciousness<br>Maintain their desires and attachments. {87}

“All of those who maintain those views<br>Should be known to be māras.<br>But those māras and evil ones<br>Cannot cause them an obstacle. [n1070] {i} ^F107b

“When all conceptualization has ceased<br>They do not relapse into conceptualization.<br>That is how one should know wisdom to be,<br>The inconceivable wisdom of buddhahood. {88}

“They see the past, the future,<br>And also the present.<br>Phenomena are revealed in that way,<br>But there is nothing to be revealed. {89}

“They do not know through knowledge.<br>They are not despondent because of no knowledge.<br>When knowledge and no knowledge have been examined<br>That is what is said to be ‘the knowledge of buddhahood.’ [n1071] {90}

“The bodhisattvas know<br>Communication, words, and terms,<br>And they accomplish immeasurable,<br>Inconceivable benefits for beings. {91}

“In order for a concept to be known,<br>It is taught through grasping.<br>The non-grasping of a concept<br>Is taught for the sake of detachment. {92}

“That which is detachment is taught<br>To be detachment from conceptions. [n1072]<br>As the nature of conceptions is known, [n1073]<br>There will be no [n1074] conceptions. [n1075] {93}

“When someone has the conception<br>‘I must eliminate this conception,’<br>They cause conceptions to increase,<br>And they will not be free from conceptions. {94}

“For whom has this conception arisen?<br>Who has made this conception arise?<br>Who perceives this conception?<br>Who ends this conception? {95}

“When a conception arises for anyone,<br>Even a buddha could not find any such phenomenon.<br>Contemplate the meaning of this<br>And there will be no conception. {96}

“When does a conception arise?<br>For whom does the conception appear?<br>How does liberation arise<br>In the process of the mind? {97}

“When liberation is experienced,<br>All thoughts become nonthought.<br>When thoughts become nonthought,<br>At that time there is nonthought. {98}

“When one is on the level of thoughts,<br>Having thus contemplated,<br>All thoughts are eliminated<br>And there is nonthought. {99}

“This is the ripening of good qualities,<br>Which is seen without mentation,<br>And the thoughts of all beings<br>Are known in a single instant. {100} ^F108a

“As beings are, so are their thoughts;<br>As are their thoughts, so are the jinas.<br>The inconceivable Buddha<br>Has taught these thoughts. {101}

“When will thoughts cease for those<br>Who think of being alone in solitude?<br>When they do not think that thought<br>Then all thoughts will cease to be. {102}

“When it comes to the time of death<br>And their thoughts are continuing,<br>Their consciousness will follow the thoughts<br>And they will not be free from thought. {103}

“If a man retains the concept of a woman,<br>His desire will continue to arise.<br>If this concept has ceased<br>He will not be stained by desire. {104}

“This thought is a great thought;<br>It is the unsurpassable thought of the Dharma.<br>Through this thought of the Dharma<br>There will be a continuity of correct thoughts. {105}

“Through incorrect thought<br>There will be numerous, countless thoughts,<br>And though one thinks for a very long time<br>There will still be no cessation to thinking. {106}

“When someone has the thought of a name,<br>In that cessation there is no wisdom. [n1076]<br>There is no cessation in the knowledge of a word— [n1077]<br>That is the nature of cessation. {107}

“Through words, speech, and communication,<br>Phenomena are taught using the term cessation.<br>Between phenomena there is no distinction,<br>And through knowing that there is cessation; {108}

“Even if it is explained for ten million eons<br>That they are unproduced and unceasing,<br>Without attributes and without characteristics,<br>They are taught to be without attributes. {109}

“When all existents have ceased to exist<br>And they remain in nonexistence,<br>Existence is not taught to be other than nonexistence,<br>And nonexistence is not taught to be other than existence. {110}

“The teaching of nonexistence<br>Is given through the word nonexistence,<br>But not even all the buddhas<br>Can see nonexistence. {111}

“That which exists is taught<br>As this nonexistence of all that exists.<br>Knowing existents in this way,<br>They are taught to be nonexistent. {112}

“There is no one whosoever<br>Who can connect with this nonexistence.<br>The connection with this nonexistence<br>Results in a teaching that is one of conventions. [n1078] {113}

“The ones who have in their minds the thought<br>‘I shall become a buddha in this world’<br>Will not be afflicted by craving for existence,<br>And those wise ones will attain enlightenment. {114} ^F108b

“The bodhisattvas in meditation<br>Do not long for any phenomenon.<br>When nothing is apprehended, [n1079]<br>That is called enlightenment. {115}

“There are many who say,<br>‘I am in a state of enlightenment,’<br>But not knowing this approach<br>They are far from buddhahood’s enlightenment. {116}

“The Dharma that is taught through words<br>Is entirely composite and empty.<br>The nature of these words<br>Is profound, subtle, and difficult to see. {117}

“It is through great higher cognition<br>That the teaching of this sūtra is given.<br>It is taught by all the buddhas<br>For the sake of the bodhisattvas. {118}

“Remedies defeat<br>However many kleśas they have.<br>Remaining in higher cognition,<br>They cultivate miraculous powers. {119}

“They maintain the knowledge of contemplation<br>And then that knowledge also ceases.<br>There is an insatiable acquisition<br>Of inconceivable, immeasurable wisdom. {120}

“Their samādhi and miraculous actions<br>Are devoid of mentation.<br>Such is the ripening of these heroes<br>Who are always in a state of meditation. {121}

“With these ripened miraculous powers<br>They go to millions of realms<br>And they see those who are the illumination of the worlds,<br>Who are as numerous as the sands of the Ganges. {122}

“Their births and their deaths<br>Are the processes of their minds.<br>They have attained power over their minds<br>And their bodies are bright. {123}

“The Buddha’s śrāvakas who maintain<br>The miraculous powers they have cultivated<br>Do not even approach a sixteenth fraction<br>Of the miraculous activities free of mentation. {124}

“All the devas are unable<br>To know their thoughts.<br>Only the lords of the worlds,<br>And those who are equal to them, can do so. {125}

“They do not become bald<br>And their hair does not become white.<br>They do not have evident aging<br>And thus have no suffering or death. {126}

“They do not have doubt or mistrust<br>And they have no uncertainty.<br>Day and night they seek for<br>Thousands of millions of sūtras. {127} ^F109a

“All their propensities<br>For the kleśas are eliminated.<br>They always have an equal mind<br>Toward all beings. {128}

“They teach quintillions of samādhis<br>Throughout the ten directions.<br>Without respite they answer<br>Thousand of millions of questions. {129}

“The concept of male, the concept of female,<br>And all other concepts have ceased.<br>They remain in the recognition of nonexistence<br>And they teach that which is certain and true. {130}

“With completely pure wisdom<br>They teach the Dharma correctly.<br>They are dedicated to proclaiming the Dharma,<br>And are in the domain of samādhi and wisdom. {131}

“Though they practice dhyāna,<br>They do not remain in existence.<br>Their words are not meaningless;<br>Their teaching of the Dharma is fruitful. {132}

“Those who delight in this sūtra<br>Will easily become human,<br>Avoid all disadvantageous existences,<br>And repay the kindness of all the buddhas. {133}

“Those who possess one verse<br>Of this precious sūtra<br>Will abandon saṃsāra<br>For countless eons. {134}

“Those who delight in this sūtra<br>Are seen by all the buddhas.<br>They will serve the buddhas<br>And quickly attain enlightenment. {135}

“Those who delight in this sūtra,<br>They will have no doubt or uncertainty<br>Concerning the entire Dharma,<br>And they are near to nirvāṇa. {136}

“They will see a great hero,<br>A tathāgata on Gṛdhrakūṭa.<br>All the buddhas will give them prophecies<br>And they will appear to be compassionate jinas. {137}

“Those who follow this sūtra<br>In this time of destruction<br>Will see Buddha Maitreya<br>And attain excellent patience. {138}

“They will remain at the summit of existence,<br>The inconceivable summit of existence,<br>And at that inconceivable summit<br>They will know no doubt. {139}

“They will not have any doubt at all,<br>Not even an atom of doubt.<br>As they have eliminated every atom of doubt, [n1080]<br>Enlightenment will not be difficult to attain. {140} ^F109b

“In the terrifying age of destruction<br>They will undergo hardship,<br>Train in this precious sūtra,<br>And have an unceasing eloquence. [n1081] {141}

“They will promulgate this sūtra<br>And will guard the treasure of the buddhas.<br>This is an offering to all the buddhas,<br>An inconceivable offering of the Dharma. {142}

“Those who maintain this sūtra<br>During the cruel age of destruction<br>Will without difficulty attain wisdom,<br>The inconceivable wisdom of buddhahood. {143}

“Those who received this sūtra<br>From the buddhas of the past<br>Will come into possession of it<br>And promulgate it in the age of destruction. {144}

“Their voices will proclaim<br>The conduct of the Śākya lion<br>In the presence of lords of the world<br>In millions of buddha realms. {145}

“And in the presence of the buddhas [n1082]<br>They will always roar the lion’s roar<br>With an endless confidence of speech,<br>Teaching the enlightenment of buddhahood. {146}

“Those who have been prophesied by the Buddha<br>Will be born into the Ikṣvāku family.<br>They will protect this enlightenment<br>During the terrifying age of destruction. {147}

“Their bodies will be perfect,<br>Adorned by the primary signs of a great being.<br>They will send emanations<br>To make homage to millions of buddhas. {148}

“There will be the manifestation<br>Of golden, illusory flowers,<br>And flowers made of beryl,<br>Of crystal, and of silver, {149}

“And every kind of jewel<br>Appearing from their hands,<br>Which they will scatter toward the buddhas<br>In seeking the path to enlightenment. {150}

“Various kinds of offerings,<br>And perfectly created music,<br>As numerous as the Ganges sands,<br>Will be emitted from the pores of their bodies. {151}

“The countless millions of beings<br>Who hear that music<br>Will progress irreversibly toward<br>Buddhahood’s highest wisdom. {152}

“Those millions of buddhas<br>Recite countless praises<br>And their sound is heard<br>Within countless realms. {153}

“For those who hear that sound<br>All their conceptualization ceases.<br>When their conceptualization has ceased<br>They will see endless [n1083] buddhas. {154} ^F110a

“With that kind of wisdom<br>They will practice bodhisattva conduct.<br>They will benefit all beings<br>And become jinas who benefit others. {155}

“Those who possess this samādhi<br>Are wise ones who will obtain<br>These benefits and qualities,<br>And also countless others. {156}

“Even a female who hears<br>This sūtra and retains a single verse<br>Will change from having a female existence<br>And will become a dharmabhāṇaka. {157}

“She will never again afterward<br>Have a female existence,<br>And will always be handsome<br>And adorned by the primary signs of a great being. {158}

“They will all come to possess<br>These supreme qualities<br>Described in this supreme sūtra,<br>And they will quickly attain enlightenment. {159}

“Having obtained this sūtra,<br>Which is the domain of all the buddhas, [n1084]<br>Throughout all their lifetimes<br>They will always be without fear. {160}

“Teaching this samādhi, this peace<br>Is the creation of bodhisattvas.<br>Whoever wishes to attain enlightenment<br>Should give the teaching of this sūtra. {161}

“They will be close to the lords of sages<br>And will be close to buddhahood’s enlightenment.<br>They will before long attain<br>This level of peace and meditation. {162}

“The bodhisattvas, the heroes,<br>Always remain in this enlightenment.<br>They see millions of buddhas<br>As numerous as the Ganges sands. {163}

“They will become cakravartin kings who rule the world,<br>See stainless buddhas who have minds of perfect peace,<br>Praise those lords of the worlds with hundreds of verses,<br>And obtain the peace of this stainless samādhi. {164}

“They will make unequaled offerings to those guides [n1085]<br>Who have perfect, great fame and are supreme among humans and devas,<br>And they will cast aside the kingdom like spittle,<br>And pure, perfectly pure, will practice celibacy. {165}

“They will enter homelessness in the Sage’s teaching<br>And obtain the peace of this stainless samādhi.<br>They will have friendly speech with gentle words,<br>And become empowered and wise in teaching [n1086] a million sūtras. {166} ^F110b

“Having attained this samādhi they will teach it to many beings:<br>Empty and without attributes, the perfect attainment of peace,<br>The perfect and unimpeded practice of the Dharma of complete peace,<br>The empty nature that is constant, stainless peacefulness. {167}

“They have profound realization, continuous endless realization,<br>A vast realization, a realization that is incalculably beneficial.<br>Having attained profound peace, this samādhi,<br>They will become an illumination for all worlds. {168}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>They will be continually pure in celibacy,<br>Unsullied, always free of the kleśas,<br>And lead millions of other beings to be the same. {169}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>They will have exceedingly sharp wisdom, supreme wisdom;<br>They will gain an ocean of learning and always have infinite understanding,<br>Virtuous speech, excellent understanding, and knowledge of the instructions. {170}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>They will gain skill in works and skill in the arts,<br>Skill in healing and likewise skill in herbs.<br>In everything they will be constant and perfect. {171}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>They will be perfect and completely skilled<br>In poetry, treatises, comedy, music, song, and dance,<br>Always becoming masters of these in this world. {172}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>Such people will be those who always have a retinue.<br>They will not cause division, but will always keep harmonious unity<br>And practice the supreme, highest, peaceful bodhisattva conduct. {173}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>Those wise people will never have<br>Sorrow, pain, or mental anguish,<br>And will at all times be free of illness. {174}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>In this human world they will not have any illness,<br>No physical pain, nor likewise mental pain,<br>No toothache, and similarly no headache. {175} ^F111a

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>They will never have any illness occur:<br>None of the various sicknesses of the mortal world,<br>Whether physical illness or likewise mental illness. {176}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>They will never have the many different kinds of afflictions,<br>Whether they are the various kinds of mental afflictions<br>Or the various kinds of physical illnesses. {177}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>Just as space, the air, is undefiled,<br>Has a pure nature, and is vast [n1087] and bright,<br>In the same way their minds will be completely pure. {178}

“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,<br>Just as moonlight, and likewise sunlight, too,<br>Are pure, ungraspable, and radiant,<br>In the same way their minds will be bright. {179}

“Just as it is not easy, using pigments,<br>To paint various forms in the air,<br>In the same way it is not easy to create pictures in the minds [n1088]<br>Of those who remain in this stainless samādhi of peace. {180}

“Just as the wind blows in the four [n1089] directions,<br>Going in every direction without impediment,<br>Their continuum of mind is like the wind,<br>Moving unimpeded, without attachment, [n1090] throughout the world. {181}

“One may be able to catch the wind with a net,<br>One may be able to bind the wind with a noose,<br>But it is not so easy to know the mind of someone<br>Who has meditated on this stainless samādhi of peace. {182}

“One may be able to catch a reflection on water,<br>And obtain from it a bowl of sesame oil,<br>But it is not so easy to know the mind of someone<br>Who has meditated on this stainless samādhi of peace. {183}

“Someone may be able to catch in their hands<br>The lightning that flashes from the thundering clouds,<br>But it is not so easy to know the extent of the mind of someone<br>Who has meditated on this stainless samādhi of peace. [n1091] {184} ^F111b

“One may be able to know the languages of all beings,<br>The beings in the buddha realms in the ten directions,<br>But it is not so easy to know the heights of the mind<br>Of bodhisattvas who have attained this samādhi. {185}

“When they have attained this stainless samādhi of peace<br>They will have no kleśas and be undefiled.<br>Those who have attained this samādhi of peace<br>Will never again have attachment [n1092] to the three existences. [n1093] {186}

“Having attained this stainless samādhi of peace,<br>They have no longing for objects of desire, no longing for forms; [n1094]<br>They have no longing for women and have unconfused minds.<br>They are peaceful, completely peaceful, and undefiled. {187}

“Having attained this stainless samādhi of peace,<br>They have no longing for sons, no longing for daughters;<br>They have no longing for a wife, and no longing for attendants.<br>Their conduct is peaceful and they are undefiled. {188}

“They have no longing for gold and no longing for wealth.<br>They have no longing for higher rebirth and no attachment to money and jewels.<br>They have completely pure minds and are free of thought.<br>That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {189}

“They do not practice celibacy for a higher rebirth. [n1095]<br>The wise are not generous out of yearning for a higher rebirth;<br>Bodhisattvas are generous because they desire enlightenment.<br>That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {190}

“Those who accomplish this stainless samādhi<br>Do not practice asceticism in order to have a kingdom,<br>Nor in order to become sovereign over the three existences.<br>They benefit many beings because they long for enlightenment. {191}

“They have no longing for songs and no longing for dance,<br>They have no longing for incense [n1096] and no longing for drink,<br>And they have no longing for food and no longing for clothes.<br>That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {i} [n1097]

“They have no longing for eyes and no longing for ears,<br>They have no longing for a nose and no longing for a tongue,<br>And they have no longing for a body and no longing for a mind.<br>That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {ii}

“They have no longing for home and no longing for the forest,<br>They have no longing for a monastery and no longing for a village,<br>And they have no longing for a region and no longing for a town.<br>That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {iii} ^F112a

“They have no longing for generosity and no longing for conduct,<br>They have no longing for patience and no longing for diligence,<br>And they have no longing for meditation and no longing for wisdom.<br>That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {iv}

“They have no longing for being and no longing for life,<br>They have no longing for the Buddha and no longing for the Dharma,<br>And they have no longing for the Saṅgha and no longing for enlightenment.<br>That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {v}

“They have no longing for existence and no longing for nonexistence,<br>They have no longing for the middle way and no longing for the extremes,<br>And they have no longing for everything and no longing for nothing.<br>That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {vi}

“When they have attained this stainless samādhi of peace,<br>Desire can never cause them harm.<br>Those who yearn for women have confused minds<br>And they know that this is the nature of desire. {192}

“When they have attained this stainless samādhi of peace,<br>Anger can never cause them harm.<br>The wise ones destroy malice;<br>Through love they completely overcome anger. [n1098] {193}

“Ignorance can never cause them harm;<br>Wisdom eliminates ignorance and stupidity.<br>They attain measureless wisdom free of darkness.<br>These qualities from attaining samādhi are measureless. {194}

“Desire is always overcome by repulsiveness. [n1099]<br>Anger is constantly defeated by love.<br>Wisdom cuts through ignorance, the net of the kleśas.<br>Those who have attained samādhi are majestic to the whole world. {195}

“Sleep can never cause them harm.<br>They eliminate the various subsidiary kleśas.<br>They are undefiled and liberated.<br>These qualities from attaining samādhi are measureless. {196}

“Desire can never cause harm<br>To the bodhisattvas who possess this samādhi.<br>They delight always in generosity:<br>They give away their possessions and give happiness. {197} ^F112b

“The bodhisattvas who possess this samādhi<br>Possess power that is beyond compare.<br>At all times they are in the possession of strength.<br>There is no one who is their equal in the world. {198}

“They become cakravartins in this world.<br>They come to Jambudvīpa as the sovereign of humans<br>And many beings make offerings to them,<br>And in particular they attain the unique wisdom free of darkness. {199}

“Such bodhisattvas become the leaders in a special, jewellike family. [n1100]<br>They have great wealth and are lords over many people. [n1101]<br>They have horses, elephants, and perfect chariots to ride upon.<br>They have abundant gold and precious jewels. [n1102] {200}

“Those who have faith in the supreme wisdom of the Buddha,<br>They are called the jewellike families in Jambudvīpa.<br>They are born there into special, jewellike families<br>And they benefit a multitude of their kin. {201}

“They carefully engender faith in those<br>Who are of families in Jambudvīpa who have no faith.<br>They bring a multitude of beings to aspire to enlightenment,<br>And they become self-arisen buddhas, supreme jinas. {202}

“They attain unequaled, highest enlightenment<br>And turn the unequaled Dharma wheel in buddha realms. [n1103]<br>Those who then know that Dharma wheel<br>Will all remain in the birthlessness of phenomena. {203}

“The bodhisattvas will perform many activities.<br>Beings will constantly make offerings to them.<br>They will constantly accomplish unequaled benefit.<br>They will remove the darkness from the eyes of beings. {204}

{205} [n1104]

“The bodhisattvas, joyous, with loving minds<br>And unstained, will become buddhas.<br>Wherever those bodhisattvas are present<br>They will create an immeasurable benefit for beings. {206}

“They will protect correct conduct and have matchless celibacy.<br>They will meditate on samādhi for many endless eons.<br>They will constantly have certainty in dhyāna and liberation.<br>Those bodhisattvas will be the sons of the buddhas. {207} ^F113a

“They always practice the bases of miraculous powers,<br>And they go to various infinite realms.<br>They listen to the Dharma taught by the sugatas<br>And, having the power of retention, they remember everything. {208}

“Those bodhisattvas who have the power of retention<br>Teach endless, countless sūtras.<br>Those bodhisattvas who have the power of retention<br>Accomplish countless benefits for beings. {209}

“They know the deaths and rebirths<br>And the coming and going of beings,<br>What kind of actions they do,<br>And the ripening of their karma. {210}

“In that transference of karma<br>There are not even atoms to be found.<br>Those greatly famous bodhisattvas<br>Know, too, that this is so. {211}

“Emptiness is the supreme<br>Dwelling of the great beings.<br>They establish countless millions<br>Of beings in the great yāna. {212}

“When they are teaching<br>They have no concept of beings.<br>The bodhisattvas teach<br>Without engaging in phenomena. {213}

“When they teach the Dharma<br>There is no apprehending of an object.<br>They reside in emptiness,<br>Established in enduring wisdom. {214}

“When someone has been taught this samādhi,<br>In which all the teachers reside,<br>No conceptions arise in him,<br>He naturally has no conceptions about women. {215}

“When conceptions of women have ceased,<br>He sits at the Bodhimaṇḍa.<br>Once he has sat at the Bodhimaṇḍa<br>The conceptions of Māra cease. {216}

“The wise one does not see<br>Māra [n1105] and Māra’s army, [n1106]<br>And neither does he see<br>The three daughters of Māra. {217}

“Once he is seated upon the Bodhimaṇḍa,<br>All his conceptions are eliminated.<br>Once all his conceptions are eliminated<br>This entire world is shaken. {218}

“So, too, are all the worlds in the ten directions<br>With their Sumerus and their oceans,<br>And this is known<br>By all the beings in the ten directions. [n1107] {219} ^F113b

“This shaking of the world<br>Is the miracle of the bodhisattva;<br>It is shaken six times<br>When he attains supreme enlightenment. {220}

“All the composite phenomena there are,<br>And all the noncomposite phenomena—<br>All phenomena are understood<br>That are taught by the word phenomena. [n1108] {221}

“There is nothing there to be understood,<br>And that lion’s roar arises.<br>Knowing this process of arising,<br>He becomes an illuminating buddha. {222}

“Phenomena appear dependently.<br>Phenomena are produced dependently.<br>The wise ones know the entirety<br>Of the dependence of phenomena. {223}

“They know the development of all phenomena.<br>They have complete understanding through emptiness.<br>They have wisdom concerning states of existence.<br>They have complete understanding of all phenomena. {224}

On seeking for these states of existence,<br>The bodhisattva does not find them.<br>That is the same as the inconceivable knowledge<br>Of all the buddhas concerning states of existence. {225}

“The one who has that complete knowledge<br>Knows all states of existence. [n1109]<br>Knowing the characteristic of the true Dharma,<br>He brings to an end all illusions. [n1110] {226}

“Knowing the characteristic of the true Dharma,<br>He gazes upon all the realms.<br>Having gazed upon all the realms,<br>He seats himself at the Bodhimaṇḍa. [n1111] {i}

“Having sat at the Bodhimaṇḍa,<br>There is the sound of the lion’s roar,<br>Which thus resounds throughout<br>Countless, innumerable millions of realms. {227}

“All those greatly renowned buddha heroes<br>Also cause those realms to shake.<br>The leader of beings guides beings<br>In the way that they are to be guided. {228}

“Having reached the highest enlightenment,<br>He rises from the Bodhimaṇḍa.<br>He guides the countless, innumerable beings<br>Who are to be guided. {229}

“Then the Buddha emanates<br>Infinite buddha emanations.<br>These buddha emanations [n1112] go<br>To thousands of millions of realms. [n1113] {230}

“They lead countless millions<br>Of beings to the highest enlightenment.<br>He teaches the supreme Dharma<br>For the benefit of all beings. {231} ^F114a

“That kind of great wisdom<br>Is the inconceivable wisdom of a buddha.<br>Therefore develop the aspiration,<br>The supreme aspiration to enlightenment. [n1114] {232}

“Develop veneration for those with the highest qualities:<br>The Buddha, the Dharma, and the Saṅgha,<br>And the heroes, the bodhisattvas,<br>Who seek for the highest enlightenment. {233}

“Without becoming disheartened,<br>Venerate them unflaggingly,<br>And become before long<br>An illuminating buddha. {234}

“Those bodhisattvas who come here<br>From thousands of realms<br>See the lamp of the world<br>Teaching the supreme Dharma. {235}

“Those great heroes throw down<br>Great jewels for the Guide,<br>And in order to attain enlightenment<br>They cast down coral tree flowers. {236}

“They adorn this realm,<br>The highest buddha realm.<br>All of the ten directions [n1115]<br>Are covered with networks of jewels. {237}

“They string up flags<br>And erect millions of banners,<br>And they adorn this realm<br>With endless adornments. {238}

“They create countless, beautiful<br>Pinnacled halls with balconies, [n1116]<br>Upper chambers, [n1117] and towers [n1118]<br>Adorned with every jewel. {239}

“They create palaces with crescents,<br>Round windows and aviaries,<br>Incense, banners, and vases, [n1119]<br>And adorned with many jewels. {240}

“The aroma [n1120] of incense<br>Spreads through this buddha realm. [n1121]<br>That delightful incense<br>Pervades a billion [n1122] realms. {241}

“When it has spread through them<br>A rain of incense falls.<br>Those who smell that incense<br>Become buddhas, guides. {242}

“They cast away the pain [n1123] of desire.<br>They do not have anger and craving. [n1124]<br>The net of ignorance [n1125] is destroyed<br>And all darkness comes to an end. {243}

“There they attain the miraculous powers,<br>And the strengths, powers, and aspects of enlightenment.<br>They attain the dhyānas and the liberations<br>And become worthy of offerings. {244} ^F114b

“Fifty million [n1126] beautiful<br>Seats are arranged,<br>Draped with millions [n1127] of cloths<br>And nets of jewels. [n1128] {245}

“The bodhisattvas, the famous heroes,<br>Are gathered there upon those seats. [n1129]<br>They shine with the primary signs<br>And also with the secondary signs. {246}

“This entire buddha realm<br>Is adorned by trees made of jewels.<br>There are emanated ponds that are filled<br>With water that has the eight qualities. {247}

“Those on the banks of those pools<br>Who drink from their waters<br>Are freed from all craving<br>And become worthy of veneration by the world. {248}

“In other realms, too,<br>Bodhisattvas gather.<br>They praise the Buddha,<br>The lion of the Śākyas, the protector. {249}

“Those who hear that praise<br>Become guides of the worlds.<br>Here I have described<br>This sūtra’s inconceivable benefits. {250}

“Countless millions of lotuses<br>Are emanated, which have<br>Petals made of gold,<br>And pericarps of uragasāra. [n1130] {251}

“They have stems [n1131] of beryl,<br>They have leaves [n1132] of crystal,<br>They have stamens of emerald, [n1133]<br>And have beautifully appeared. {252}

“They have an inconceivable aroma<br>That they continuously emit.<br>The inconceivable aroma of the lotuses<br>Fills millions of realms. [n1134] {i}

“Those who smell that aroma<br>That they delightfully emanate<br>Will have delight in their minds<br>And all their illnesses will cease. {253}

“Desire, anger, and ignorance<br>Will cease without trace.<br>When those three faults have ceased in them<br>They will be buddhas who bestow happiness. {254}

“From them are emitted sounds,<br>Countless numbers of the word buddha.<br>And from them also the words<br>dharma and saṅgha emanate everywhere, {255}

“And also the words emptiness,<br>Absence of attributes, and absence of aspiration.<br>The progress of the numerous millions of beings<br>Who hear them becomes irreversible. {256} ^F115a

“These words that are emanated<br>Also reach millions of realms.<br>They establish countless millions<br>Of beings in this buddha wisdom. {257}

“The birds that are peacocks, [n1135]<br>Avadavats, and partridges<br>Also sing out a word,<br>The unsurpassable word buddha. {258}

“The birds that are snipes,<br>Mynas, cranes, and cuckoos<br>Also sing out a word,<br>The inconceivable [n1136] word dharma. [n1137] {i}

“The birds that are parrots, geese,<br>Ducks, shelducks, and swans<br>Also sing out a word,<br>The unsurpassable word saṅgha. {ii}

“All the birds that there are<br>In the deva or the human worlds<br>Are continuously singing<br>Praises of the Three Jewels. {iii}

“Trees made of jewels<br>Are manifested in this realm.<br>Those delightful jewel trees<br>Are uniquely beautiful. {259}

“On all those trees are hung<br>Every kind of ornament.<br>They have manifested in this realm<br>Through the power of the Buddha. [n1138] {260}

“This display does not exist<br>Anywhere in any realm.<br>This unique, superior sight<br>Is not to be seen in this realm. [n1139] {261}

“This is what has been taught<br>By the Śākya lion, the protector.<br>The greatly famed bodhisattvas<br>Have no doubt in that wisdom. {262}

“They comprehend that highest point.<br>Their way is inconceivable.<br>Their wisdom increases<br>Like an ocean into which rivers flow. {263}

“They have no final end.<br>It is like drinking an ocean.<br>This is the inconceivable way<br>Of the bodhisattvas that has been taught. {264}

“The greatly famed bodhisattvas,<br>The heroes, are at the highest point.<br>They give forth aspects of speech<br>That are as numerous as the Ganges sands. {265}

“There is such inconceivable speech<br>But the bodhisattvas have no pride. [n1140]<br>They have eliminated pride<br>And are near to enlightenment, {266}

“They will not ruin their correct conduct<br>Even for the sake of their life.<br>The bodhisattvas are resolute<br>And behave immaculately. {267} ^F115b

“They do not become ruined<br>By any concept of desire.<br>They have eliminated all conceptions<br>And they have countless samādhis. {268}

“They practice them while in meditation<br>Yet have no attachment to those samādhis.<br>They have no clinging, they are attentive,<br>And they have no attachment to the world. {269}

“When they leave this world<br>They go to Sukhāvatī.<br>When they have arrived there<br>They see Buddha Amitābha. {270}

“Those bodhisattva heroes<br>Are adorned by the primary signs.<br>They have reached the domain of the five higher cognitions,<br>Great wisdom, [n1141] and the retentions. {271}

“They go to millions of realms<br>And bow down to the feet of the buddhas.<br>Shining, they travel<br>To countless buddha realms. {272}

“They have eliminated all faults<br>And are purified of all kleśas.<br>With the kleśas completely eradicated<br>They are one lifetime from becoming a jina. {273}

“They will not go to the lower realms.<br>From that realm of humans<br>All rebirth into the lower realms<br>Has been eradicated in that realm. {274}

“Do not doubt what has been revealed<br>Concerning that protector,<br>The Lord of the World, Amitābha,<br>And you will go to Sukhāvatī. [n1142] {275}

“A woman who has faith on hearing<br>The praise of this precious sūtra [n1143]<br>Will soon become a superior wise man<br>Who miraculously goes to billions of realms. {276}

“Many offerings of innumerable kinds,<br>Offered continuously to supreme beings<br>Within the appearance of a quintillion realms,<br>Cannot equal a fraction of a loving mind. {277}

“Those who always practice correct conduct and samādhi,<br>And also countless dhyānas and liberations,<br>Who always practice emptiness devoid of attributes—<br>They will soon become sugatas in the world. {278}

“The bodhisattvas who maintain the aggregate of correct conduct<br>Make the greatest, most special offering to me.<br>Those who maintain the aspiration to enlightenment in the time of degeneration<br>Are continuously making an offering to all the buddhas. [n1144] {279} ^F116a

“The bodhisattvas in the dreadful time of degeneration<br>Who protect this supreme Dharma [n1145] taught by the sugatas,<br>Are my offspring and protectors of the Dharma in the later times. [n1146]<br>They have been entrusted by ten billion buddhas.” {280}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, [n1147] “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should abide in the absence of attributes and be dedicated to making vast offerings to a present tathāgata or to the stūpa of a tathāgata who has passed into nirvāṇa.

“Young man, those bodhisattva mahāsattvas should develop an aspiration focused upon all beings as they wish for this samādhi. And, wishing to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, they should abide in the absence of attributes, without aspiration for the ripening of karma, and use even their own body and life to perform vast actions of making offerings to a present tathāgata or to the stūpa of a tathāgata who has passed into nirvāṇa.

“With their mind and attention focused on compassion; with a loud, clear voice, elevated and pleasant; and with especially noble vocabulary and a continuity of words they should teach extensively to others, propagate, and explain the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. Why is that? Because, young man, this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, is the basis and root of the entire Dharma.

“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have great compassion and diligently rely on methods are dedicated to making vast offerings to a present tathāgata or to the stūpa of a tathāgata who has passed into nirvāṇa, they should teach extensively to others this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. ^F116b

“At that time, young man, those bodhisattva mahāsattvas should abide in the doorways to liberation that are emptiness, the absence of attributes, and the absence of aspiration, and should not apprehend any phenomenon whatsoever. The bodhisattva mahāsattvas who abide in the practice of the samādhi that is free of apprehending will abide in all aspirations. Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who abide in all aspirations will fulfill all the aspirations of all beings, will quickly attain this samādhi, and will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. [n1148]

“Young man, you should understand this through the following teaching.

“Young man, in the past, uncountable, vast, immeasurable, inconceivable, innumerable countless eons ago, [n1149] at that time and in those days, there appeared in the world the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, who was perfect in wisdom and conduct, a sugata, a knower of the world, an unsurpassable guide who tamed beings, a teacher of devas and humans, a buddha, and a bhagavān.

“Young man, the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta established countless, innumerable beings in the cessation of defilements, in arhatship, and having established them in that state, he passed into nirvāṇa. He also established countless, innumerable beings in irreversible progress toward the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood and then passed into nirvāṇa. ^F117a

“Young man, at that time and in those days, [n1150] in Jambudvīpa there was a king named Śrīghoṣa. In order to make offerings to the Tathāgata who had passed into nirvāṇa he built eighty-four quintillion stūpas that contained the relics of the Tathāgata and he presented eighty-four quintillion lights to each of those stūpas. In the same way he offered eighty-four quintillion musical instruments, percussion instruments, flowers, incense offerings, perfumes, garlands, ointments, powders, robes, parasols, banners, and flags to each of those stūpas.

“Young man, in that way King Śrīghoṣa made offerings to the stūpas that contained the relics of the Tathāgata. Then he gathered eighty quintillion bodhisattvas and dedicated himself to making offerings of all the most pleasing necessities to those bodhisattvas.

“Every one of all those bodhisattva mahāsattvas was a dharmabhāṇaka. They had uninterrupted eloquence, the attainment of samādhi, and the attainment of unimpeded retention. They were teachers of the pure Dharma, and had attained the perfection of the supreme powers of a bodhisattva.

“Young man, at that time, within that assembly there was a bodhisattva mahāsattva [n1151] named Kṣemadatta. He was a young boy with black hair, in the first stage of youth. He had become a youth who did not indulge in desires, but was a young celibate, who had been keeping the vow for a year.

“Young man, at that time, King Śrīghoṣa made a request to that great assembly of bodhisattvas. He made a request to those bodhisattva mahāsattvas that he might, combining the six perfections, accomplish the great retention of the bodhisattva piṭaka, skill in methods, and unimpeded power and guidance.  That evening he lit a quintillion lights before the stūpas that contained the relics of the Tathāgata. He also swept clean the circumambulation walkway, moistened and washed it, scattered flowers upon it, and arranged various seats. King Śrīghoṣa then came there accompanied by his harem and the people of the villages, towns, and regions. Holding musical instruments, percussion instruments, cymbals, flowers, incense, perfumes, garlands, ointments, powders, robes, parasols, banners, and flags, they made offerings to the stūpa, which contained the relics of the Tathāgata. Afterwards, in order to hear the Dharma, accompanied by his harem of queens, he ascended to the roof of the palace. Gatherings of devas and humans also assembled in order to hear the Dharma. ^F117b

“The bodhisattva Kṣemadatta saw them and the lights from the numerous quintillions of offered lamps that shone as one pervading radiance. Knowing that many devas and humans had assembled in order to hear the Dharma, he thought, ‘I have entered the Mahāyāna, and because I now long for this samādhi I shall make an offering to the Tathāgata. It will be such an offering to the Tathāgata that it will amaze the worlds of devas, humans, and asuras, and bring them joy, delight, pleasure, and happiness, and they will obtain the light of the Dharma. I shall make an offering that will surpass all the offerings made to the Tathāgata by King Śrīghoṣa and amaze King Śrīghoṣa, his harem of queens, and his attendants, and bring them joy, delight, pleasure, and happiness.’ ^F118a

“The bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta was joyful and happy, and knowing that the great assembly of people had gathered to hear the Dharma, that evening he sat in front of the Tathāgata’s stūpa, bound his right hand in cotton, and immersed it in sesame oil. Having immersed it in sesame oil he set it alight.

“At this point the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta developed the supreme intention. He developed the supreme intention for the highest, complete enlightenment and, seeking complete enlightenment, although his right hand was burning brightly, his mind and the expression of his face remained unchanged.

“Young man, as the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta’s right hand burned brightly, and was transformed into a single flame, at that time this great earth shook. The light from his burning right hand made that of the many quintillions of offering lamps seem dark, and its great illumination spread in all directions, its radiance illuminating and pervading every direction.

“He became joyful and happy, and with a gentle and pleasing voice, a uniquely superior vocabulary, and a continuity of words and letters, he taught [n1152] the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena so that the entire assembly understood it in detail.

“The one thousand two hundred Trāyastriṃśa devas assembled there to listen to the Dharma were made joyous and happy and made various divine offerings. The apsarases engaged in singing divine songs. [n1153]

“King Śrīghoṣa, who was keeping the eight poṣadha vows, was in the middle of his harem of queens, with his court before him, seated on the roof of his palace. He saw that the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta’s hand was burning and outshining all other lights,  creating a brightness that transcended the lights of devas and the lights of humans. ^F118b

“He thought, ‘This bodhisattva mahāsattva has attained great higher cognition,’ and felt intense joy, faith, veneration, and reverence for the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta. Supported by his great accumulation of merit and roots of merit he leapt from the roof of the palace, together with his harem of eighty queens. He leapt because of his joy on having seen the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta.

“Because of the roots of merit that were produced by his veneration, he and his retinue were caught by devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kinnaras, and mahoragas. After they had been caught by devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kinnaras, and mahoragas, King Śrīghoṣa and his retinue, even though they had jumped from a building that was a hundred thousand cubits high, were physically unharmed, mentally unharmed, and were not unnerved.

“King Śrīghoṣa extended both his hands, and together with the great assembly of people saw the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta’s hand on fire and burning brightly. All of them cried out loudly and wailed. Then the king, together with the great assembly of people, weeping and shedding tears, came before the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta.

“Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta saw King Śrīghoṣa, and having seen him asked, ‘Great king, why are you and this great assembly of people here before me crying out loudly, wailing, sorrowful, and weeping?’ ^F119a

“King Śrīghoṣa spoke these verses to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta:

“ ‘These beings have cried out [n1154]<br>Because they have seen that Kṣemadatta,<br>The one with great wisdom, the learned one,<br>The dharmabhāṇaka, has lost a limb. {1}

“ ‘Seeing that this body<br>That emits this brilliant light<br>Has had a hand destroyed,<br>I also feel great suffering. {2}

“ ‘The light from your burning hand<br>Has shone into the ten directions.<br>The divine light you have emitted<br>Has obscured the light of these lamps. {3}

“ ‘This earth has been shaken<br>And you are not disheartened.<br>There arose in me the thought,<br>“That is no ordinary wise man.” {4}

“ ‘I leapt a hundred thousand cubits<br>From the roof of my palace,<br>Together with my harem of queens,<br>But my body was not harmed. {5}

“ ‘How excellent your wonderful wisdom!<br>How excellent your unsurpassable mind!<br>How excellent your dedicated diligence!<br>How excellent your great aspiration! {6}

“ ‘Your hand [n1155] is burning<br>But you are not disturbed.<br>You are happy and joyous<br>And again teach the Dharma. {7}

“ ‘Worthy friend, you are as beautiful<br>As the moon that is full,<br>Or the sun high in the sky,<br>Or Sumeru, the king of mountains. {8}

“ ‘Wise one, may I also<br>Fulfill such a prayer!<br>Rejecting my care for the body<br>I will accomplish benefit for beings. {9}

“ ‘I delight in joy for the Dharma;<br>My happiness in that is inconceivable.<br>That you have lost a limb<br>Causes me the highest suffering.’ {10}

“Kṣemadatta, through devas and nāgas,<br>Made offerings to the king<br>And he spoke these verses<br>With infinite confidence: {11}

“ ‘Someone who has no hand<br>Is not the one who lacks a limb;<br>Someone who has no correct conduct<br>Is the one who is lacking a limb. {12}

“ ‘This putrid [n1156] body of mine<br>I have offered to the tathāgatas,<br>The inconceivable recipients of offerings,<br>The ones to whom offerings should be made by all the world. {13} . ^F119b

“ ‘Seeking the wisdom of buddhahood<br>I offer to the lords of the worlds<br>Infinite billion-world universes<br>Entirely filled with jewels. {14}

“ ‘There are these material offerings<br>But there are other inconceivable offerings.<br>Those who know that phenomena are empty<br>Give away their bodies and their lives. {15}

“ ‘I shall speak words of truth.<br>Great king, listen to me!<br>All the people gathered here,<br>Understand the meaning of these verses! {16}

“ ‘If it is true that I will become a buddha,<br>One who is revered by the world,<br>May that truth cause this earth<br>To shake in six ways!’ {17}

“He spoke those words<br>And the earth shook.<br>Millions of devas were overjoyed,<br>Amazed, and astonished. {18}

“The joyous devas and humans<br>Developed the aspiration for enlightenment.<br>Immeasurable, incalculable numbers<br>Were established in the supreme yāna. {19}

“The benefit accomplished<br>By the bhikṣu Kṣemadatta<br>Is the unending and inconceivable engagement<br>With the wisdom of the buddhas. {20}

“ ‘If it is true that this phenomenon<br>That is called “hand” does not exist,<br>Then may that truth cause my hand<br>To be instantly restored as it was before! {21}

“ ‘If it is true that this phenomenon<br>Called “Kṣemadatta” does not exist,<br>Though one seeks for it in the ten directions,<br>It will be not be found, because it is empty. {22}

“ ‘Whatever sound arises,<br>Know it to be empty.<br>Sound is like an echo:<br>Know phenomena to be like that. {23}

“ ‘When there is fearlessness,<br>Emptiness is fully comprehended.<br>Through those words of truth<br>May the entire world not be burned! {24}

“ ‘May all the beings in the three existences,<br>The devas and the humans,<br>All rest in a state of meditation<br>Because of the brilliance of omniscience. {25}

“ ‘All the misfortunes<br>That devas and humans have,<br>May they all come to cessation<br>Through the brilliance of irreversibility!’ {26}

“After Kṣemadatta spoke those verses<br>His hand grew back,<br>And Kṣemadatta’s body became<br>Adorned by the primary signs. {27} ^F120a

“Ten thousand million devas<br>Who were residing in the sky<br>Threw down at that moment<br>Coral tree flowers upon the bhikṣu. {28}

“Those divine flowers<br>Filled up this world.<br>A quintillion apsarases<br>Engaged in performing songs. {29}

“When Kṣemadatta<br>Emitted these words,<br>Ten thousand million buddhas<br>Witnessed this miracle. {30}

“In each of their realms<br>They made his great fame known<br>To their bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs,<br>Upāsakas and upāsikās: [n1157] {31}

“ ‘This bhikṣu Kṣemadatta<br>Is wise and has great might.<br>He burned his hand in order to gain<br>The wisdom of buddhahood.’ {32}

“Thousands of realms,<br>As numerous as the Ganges sands,<br>Were illuminated by that lamp,<br>Which was like the fire at an eon’s end. {33}

“All the realms became filled<br>With flowers and sandalwood [n1158] powder,<br>Up to kneeheight<br>From the ground. [n1159] {34}

“Jewels and flowers of every kind<br>Filled the buddha realm.<br>Nāgas brought down a rain of pearls<br>As an offering to Kṣemadatta. {35}

“This realm became adorned<br>By a display of every kind of jewel.<br>Jewels and pearls were spread out<br>As an offering to Kṣemadatta. {36}

“Devas, nāgas, and yakṣas,<br>kinnaras  [n1160] and mahoragas,<br>As numerous as the Ganges sands,<br>Were established in the highest enlightenment.” {37}

The Śākya lion, the Buddha,<br>Was on Vulture Peak Mountain.<br>In front of his assembly of bhikṣus<br>The Jina roared this lion’s roar: {38}

“It is I who was Kṣemadatta<br>And Ajita was Śrīghoṣa.<br>For ten thousand million eons<br>I practiced the bodhisattva conduct. {39}

“Countless women,<br>The moment they saw<br>Bhikṣu Kṣemadatta,<br>Ceased being women. [n1161] {40}

“The Lord of humans prophesied<br>That they would not return<br>But that they all would become<br>Self-arisen guides of the world. [n1162] {41} ^F120b

“The wise who have heard this sūtra,<br>The teaching on the disciplines of mendicancy,  [n1163]<br>Should have no cherishing for the body<br>And should study well this Dharma.” {42}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should plant roots of merit and apply themselves to practicing generosity through the Dharma or generosity through material things.

“Those bodhisattva mahāsattvas should dedicate that generosity through four prayers of dedication.

“What are the four dedication prayers? The first dedication prayer is: ‘I plant [n1164] the roots of merit of this generosity so that I may attain skills in methods, those skills in methods by which the buddha bhagavāns attained the highest, complete enlightenment of buddhahood.’

“The second dedication prayer is: ‘I plant the roots of merit of this generosity so that I may listen to those skills in methods from kalyāṇamitras, remember them, understand them, possess them, and recite them, and so that I will always be in the company of those kalyāṇamitras who will attain the highest, complete enlightenment of buddhahood.’

“The third dedication prayer is: ‘I plant the roots of merit of this generosity so that all may obtain the requisites that sustain life in the world, and so that these requisites may come together for me.’ [n1165]

“The fourth dedication prayer is: ‘I plant the roots of merit of this generosity so that I may attain an existence in which I take care of beings, taking care of them in two ways: taking care of them through the Dharma and taking care of them through material things.’

“Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas dedicate those roots of merit through those four prayers of dedication. ^F121a

“Moreover, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who yearn for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, whether they are homeless renunciants or householders, should sincerely [n1166] serve, provide for, [n1167] and attend upon a bodhisattva mahāsattva who has correct conduct, good qualities, and wisdom. [n1168] If that bodhisattva mahāsattva bhikṣu who possesses this samādhi were to become ill, afflicted by a powerful illness, then they should eagerly cure him of the illness with their own flesh and blood. Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who with the perfect higher motivation yearn for this samādhi and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood should fearlessly and confidently [n1169] give even their own flesh and blood so that the dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu will be healed from his illness.

“Young man, this is how that teaching is to be understood.

“Young man, in a past countless eon—numerous, incalculable, countless eons ago—at that time and in those days, there was a tathāgata, an arhat, a perfectly enlightened buddha perfect in wisdom and conduct, a sugata, a knower of the world, an unsurpassable guide who tamed beings, a teacher of devas and humans, the Bhagavān Buddha Acintya­praṇidhāna­viśeṣa­samudgata­rāja who had appeared in the world.

“Young man, before the end of the day on which he attained the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, he manifested incalculable, innumerable buddha emanations and guided countless beings, establishing them in the arhathood in which all outflows have ceased,  and he established countless beings in irreversible progress toward the highest, complete enlightenment. And then, before that day had ended, he passed into nirvāṇa. ^F121b

“The Dharma of that Bhagavān who had passed into nirvāṇa remained for a hundred thousand quintillion years.

“Young man, in the last five hundred years before the Dharma of Bhagavān Acintya­praṇidhāna­viśeṣa­samudgata­rāja finally came to an end, there were many bhikṣus who held the view of objective existence. They had no yearning, no aspiration for a sūtra like this and opposed it and attacked it. They harmed and even killed the bhikṣus who possessed this sūtra. They had attachment to gain and honor and therefore they killed thousands of bhikṣus who possessed a sūtra like this.

“Young man, at that time and in those days, King Jñānabala ruled over Jambudvīpa. He possessed the Dharma and had appeared because of his perfect prayers in previous lifetimes.

“Young man, at that time and in those days, in this Jambudvīpa there was a bhikṣu named Bhūtamati who possessed this sūtra. That dharmabhāṇaka went to the king’s palace and became a kalyāṇamitra who was altruistic, was compassionate, and wished to benefit others. The king never tired of gazing upon him and always longed to see him. He came to him for teaching and for discussions on the Dharma. He honored him, asked him questions, obtained answers, and was able to understand what was spoken.

“That dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu was wise in the behavior, [n1170] conduct, aspirations, natures, and propensities of beings. He knew the extent of the powers, strengths, and diligence of beings. He was wise in natures and propensities. [n1171] He was wise in implying the truth. He was also wise in giving answers without implied meaning. He had profound eloquence and was wise in the ways of guiding all beings. He spoke sincerely. [n1172] His face was free of frowns.  He remained in a state of greatness of mind. He was dedicated to great compassion. He could not be defeated by any opponent. ^F122a

“Young man, at that time and in those days, King Jñānabala’s daughter was sixteen years old and she was beautiful, attractive, and charming. She had a lovely complexion, and was magnificent. Her name was Jñānāvatī. The bhikṣu Bhūtamati was her ācārya. He taught her the virtuous qualities, extolled them, delighted in them, and made her develop them.

“Young man, at that time and in those days, the dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu developed widespread, black erysipelas on both his thighs, which did not respond to treatment and had no known cure, so that the physicians gave up trying to heal him. King Jñānabala with his harem, sons, daughters, and attendants, on learning that the bhikṣu was ill, wept and shed tears.

“Eighty thousand women, the inhabitants of the cities and towns, the people of the kingdom, the people of the market towns and the regions, the astrologers, ministers, and prime ministers, and the doorkeepers and attendants, hearing that the bhikṣu was ill, wept and shed tears and cried, ‘May this bhikṣu not die!’

“Young man, at that time and in those days, the goddess of King Jñānabala’s family since ancient times, who was always by his side, instructed the king in a dream, saying, ‘Great king, if fresh, unspoiled human blood [n1173] is applied to this bhikṣu’s erysipelas, and if fresh, untarnished human flesh is prepared with various flavors and given to him to eat, then this bhikṣu will be cured of his illness.’

When that night had passed and King Jñānabala awoke from his sleep he entered his harem and he described the dream to his harem, saying, ‘This is the kind of dream that I have had.’ ^F122b

“Young man, none of the women in the harem, the king’s wives, had the fortitude to provide that remedy for the bhikṣu.

“Princess Jñānāvatī also dreamed that kind of dream. When she awoke, she went into the harem and described the dream to her circle of mothers, but none of the women had the fortitude to provide that remedy for the bhikṣu.

“Then Princess Jñānāvatī became happy, delighted, thrilled, joyful, pleased, and glad, and made this resolution: ‘In that case I shall cut from myself the remedy, and as instructed will give him the fresh blood and fresh flesh. I am the youngest and least within the royal household, and my body, speech, and mind are untarnished. I seek untarnished wisdom, and therefore I shall offer my flesh and blood to the untarnished dharmabhāṇaka, so that I may heal this bhikṣu of his illness!’

“Then Princess Jñānāvatī returned to her own dwelling and, taking up a sharp knife and with her mind focused on the Dharma, she cut flesh from her own thigh. She prepared it, adding various excellent flavors. Bringing the blood, too, she went to her ācārya [n1174] and, seated before King Jñānabala, she applied the blood onto the black erysipelas and nourished the bhikṣu with the well-prepared meal.

“Then the bhikṣu, not knowing, unaware, and unsuspecting, ate that food. As soon as he had eaten it, the bhikṣu’s illness completely vanished and he was entirely cured of his illness. Freed from pain and happy, he taught the Dharma so that twelve hundred beings from among the harem and the assembled people from the land, towns, and countryside developed the aspiration to highest, complete enlightenment.

“King Jñānabala then recited these verses to his daughter: ^F123a

“ ‘Daughter, from where did you obtain this blood?<br>And from where did you obtain this human flesh?<br>Daughter, by your preparing this food<br>The dharmabhāṇaka has become healthy. {1}

“ ‘Was it from someone slain or who had died that you obtained<br>This flesh prepared with various flavors?<br>Daughter, where did you obtain this blood<br>That has freed him from this evil sickness?’ {2}

“The daughter listened to her father’s words<br>And Jñānāvatī then addressed him.<br>With no despondency, she spoke these words:<br>‘Listen, father, to what I have to say. {3}

“ ‘I too, father, had the dream<br>That was sent by the goddess.<br>Lord of the World, listen to me,<br>And understand its true meaning. {4}

“ ‘That goddess said to me<br>That whoever gives to the bhikṣu<br>The flesh and blood of a human<br>Will cure him of his evil illness. {5}

“ ‘I arose from my bed<br>And I entered the harem.<br>I then related my dream<br>To my superiors, my mothers. {6}

“ ‘I asked the servants who among them<br>Would be able to do this,<br>To make perfectly delicious<br>Human blood and flesh? {7}

“ ‘If that food is given to him<br>And if the blood is applied,<br>The bhikṣu will be freed<br>From this black erysipelas. {8}

“ ‘If we do not use this method,<br>If we do not apply this remedy,<br>This bhikṣu will soon die<br>Because of this illness that he has. {9}

“ ‘What being in the three existences<br>Would not give their flesh and blood? [n1175]<br>What wise ones on seeing this<br>Would hold fast to their body? {10}

“ ‘Though I told the harem of this,<br>Not even one woman said she would give.<br>The bhikṣu is beloved and he is beloved by me,<br>So I gave him my flesh and blood for the sake of enlightenment. {11}

“ ‘Those who seek enlightenment, peace, and freedom from misery<br>Have no devotion to their body or dependence on it;<br>Of themselves they cherish not even an atom,<br>And are not saddened to give themselves away. {12}

“ ‘When the harem heard those words,<br>They were all perplexed.<br>None of them had the fortitude<br>To take on such an act. {13} ^F123b

“ ‘Then I developed the intention<br>That I would provide the food for the bhikṣu,<br>Cutting off pieces of my own flesh<br>And using for lotion my own blood. {14}

“ ‘I cut into my own thighs<br>And obtained the flesh and blood.<br>I myself cooked the pieces of flesh<br>And added various flavorings. {15}

“ ‘In the presence of my father<br>I gave to the sick bhikṣu<br>The meal of human flesh<br>And the lotion of blood. {16}

“ ‘Lord of men, listen to my words!<br>Sovereign, there not being any human flesh,<br>I cut the flesh from my own thighs,<br>And having cooked it gave it to the dharmabhāṇaka. {17}

“ ‘It was for the sake of the highest enlightenment<br>That I accomplished this great purpose with my body.<br>The bhikṣu is cured and returned to health<br>And I have created immeasurable merit.’ {18}

“The king inquired of his daughter,<br>‘How did you cut the flesh from your body?<br>Daughter, when you engaged in creating this remedy,<br>Did you not suffer from physical pain?’ {19}

“The wise and fearless princess replied to him,<br>‘King, lord of the earth, listen!<br>Having listened, understand correctly<br>The inconceivable ripening of karma. {20}

“ ‘Father, through having done bad actions,<br>Beings fall into dreadful hell.<br>They lose their flesh, and again have flesh.<br>See the inconceivable result of actions! {21}

“ ‘Through bad karma they have no flesh or blood,<br>And in an instant they again have flesh and blood.<br>Therefore, needless to say that, because of good karma,<br>Through aspiration flesh and blood will be created. {22}

“ ‘I had no pain when I cut my flesh.<br>When the blood flowed I did not become dizzy.<br>Even if I were to cut off all of my flesh,<br>The body of the Dharma would have no wound or cut. {23}

“ ‘Feeling perfect joy in the Dharma,<br>I cut the flesh to be given from my thighs.<br>I had no suffering because of the wounds,<br>And my body became as it was before. {24} ^F124a

“ ‘Father, just like a fig-tree flower is only seen<br>A few times in many millions of eons,<br>This dharmabhāṇaka is just like that,<br>Seen rarely in this Jambudvīpa. {25}

“ ‘Just as humans never tire of gazing<br>Upon shining Jambu River gold,<br>Devas and humans never tire of gazing<br>In that way upon this dharmabhāṇaka. {26}

“ ‘Just as a thirsty man is freed from thirst<br>When he drinks clear water,<br>In the same way wise dharmabhāṇakas<br>Free beings of thirst with the nectar of Dharma. {27}

“ ‘This my flesh and blood that I bestowed<br>Upon the bhikṣu who was afflicted by illness<br>Eliminated the dharmabhāṇaka’s erysipelas,<br>And I thus respectfully rendered homage to the Buddha. {28}

“ ‘I gave of my own flesh<br>To the learned one with correct conduct,<br>Who is a holder of this supreme samādhi.<br>May I obtain from him this Dharma! {29}

“ ‘Just as the fragrant aroma of the incense<br>Of yellow sandalwood and red sandalwood [n1176]<br>Spreads throughout the ten directions,<br>So, too, does the aroma of the dharmabhāṇaka. {30}

“ ‘Just as Meru is seen from every direction,<br>And seeing its beauty brings joy<br>And it illuminates, shining in all directions,<br>In that way the dharmabhāṇaka is like Meru. {31}

“ ‘Just as when a wise man rebuilds<br>A stūpa that has fallen into ruin,<br>His having faith in that stūpa<br>Is the cause for it to be rebuilt, {32}

“ ‘Likewise, this stūpa of the Dharma was ill<br>And I cured it by applying blood.<br>With veneration for the Dharma, with my own flesh<br>I have lit the lamp for Jambudvīpa. {33}

“ ‘If this bhikṣu had passed away,<br>The words of this samādhi would have been<br>Forever silenced for the beings in this world.<br>By healing him, this samādhi will be obtained. {34}

“ ‘This bhikṣu is a protector of the whole world,<br>And gives sight to the blind world.<br>With the king of medicines he even heals<br>Desire, anger, and ignorance. {35} ^F124b

“ ‘He always has a mind that is vast,<br>The extent of his conduct is immeasurable,<br>He is learned in words and their definite meaning,<br>And he cannot be defeated by opponents. {36}
