“They constantly train in wisdom<br>And beat loudly the drum of the Dharma.<br>They cut through the creepers of doubt in all beings<br>And are constantly engaged in wisdom.<br>They are stainless, well-learned holders of the Dharma.<br>They are wise and have understanding.<br>They sit upon a seat within the assembly<br>And they teach millions of sūtras. {54} ^F144b

“They are greatly learned and hold what they have learned;<br>They are holders of the Dharma of the buddhas.<br>They are holders of the treasure that is the Dharma<br>And they rejoice in the treasury of the Sage.<br>They have become possessors of immense wisdom<br>And they are constantly giving rise to vast joy.<br>They teach the peace of the supreme Dharma,<br>Which is subtle, liberating, [n1314] and difficult to see. {55}

“They know what is Dharma and what is not.<br>They are gentle, wise, and remain within the Dharma.<br>They are unequaled teachers of the kingdom of the Dharma<br>And constantly practice the supreme, unequaled Dharma.<br>They are devoted to the excellent Dharma<br>And maintain veneration of the guru.<br>They dwell in the supreme city of the Dharma.<br>They who are wise raise up the banner of the Dharma. {56}

“When they see beings who are proud,<br>Arrogant, [n1315] and constantly heedless,<br>Who are on a destructive, wrong path,<br>Who are following the path of saṃsāra,<br>They have vast love and compassion for them<br>While remaining in joy and equanimity.<br>They teach them the supreme eightfold path<br>Of peace that is difficult to see. {57}

“They build the strong ship of the Dharma<br>To save and carry the many beings<br>Who have fallen into the great ocean<br>And into the rivers of saṃsāra.<br>Armored in the strengths, powers, and aspects of enlightenment,<br>They set out upon the ship of the Dharma,<br>And they always easily and without fear<br>Bring beings to the far shore. [n1316] {58}

“They practice the discipline of the supreme medicine.<br>They are physicians who possess the supreme medicine.<br>They have perfectly attained liberation through knowledge and wisdom,<br>And they dispense the medicine of the good Dharma.<br>When they see sick beings<br>Afflicted by many illnesses,<br>They give them the medicine of the Dharma<br>And they heal them through the Dharma. {59}

“They are lords of the world, sovereigns of speech,<br>And they defeat their adversaries in debate.<br>They shine with the light of omniscience.<br>They have understanding and are on the level of the highest wisdom.<br>They are heroes with the strength of wisdom that defeats other strengths.<br>They are praised by those who have wisdom.<br>With their wisdom they bring happiness to many<br>Trillions of beings, establishing them in the Dharma. {60} ^F145a

“They are the masters, the leaders of merchant caravans, [n1317]<br>Who are dedicated to protecting beings from misfortune. [n1318]<br>When they see beings bewildered on a path of jewels<br>Who are constantly caught in the trap of Māra,<br>They explain to them the supreme path<br>Of constant peace, happiness, and emancipation.<br>Through that path of wisdom<br>The wise ones guide many billions of beings. {61}

“They are a sanctuary, they are a shelter,<br>They are a refuge; they are eyes and a lamp.<br>They give freedom from fear to those who are afraid.<br>They constantly bring relief to those who are fearful.<br>When they know of beings in great suffering,<br>Of beings who have been completely blind from birth, [n1319]<br>With the precious teachings on correct training<br>They shine the light of the Dharma. {62}

“They are the best artisans in the world,<br>Who benefit beings with their craft.<br>They always make beings happy<br>Through being well trained in their craft.<br>They have attained perfection in the supreme training<br>And are completely skilled, with wondrous attainment in the world.<br>They who are established in enlightenment<br>Have realization and give sight to the world. {63}

“They never cease longing to listen<br>To the supreme, unequaled Dharma of the buddhas.<br>They have perfected conduct, patience, and samādhi,<br>And have heard the profound Dharma.<br>They never cease wishing to teach<br>The precious Dharma of peace.<br>They send down a rain of methods for liberation,<br>Satisfying beings with the rain of the Dharma. {64}

“However many beings, wise ones,<br>Come to them for the sake of the Dharma,<br>Thinking, ‘We will listen to the true, honest path<br>Of the supreme jewel of the excellent Dharma,’<br>The realized ones cut through their doubts<br>And bring them happiness through the Dharma.<br>They have perfect conduct, patience, and samādhi,<br>And they know the aspirations of beings. {65}

“They have wisdom, the perfection of the highest wisdom,<br>And they are wise concerning the aspirations of beings.<br>They know the motivations and conduct of other beings<br>And they know what should be said to them.<br>Through their speaking words of wisdom<br>Millions of beings attain the sight of the supreme Dharma.<br>They have attained the perfection of the highest wisdom<br>And they give the teachings of the path. {66} ^F145b

“Even billions of māras cannot know<br>The minds of those wise ones,<br>Just as no one can know the path<br>That a bird has flown through the air.<br>They are peaceful, tamed, tranquil, have the power of wisdom,<br>And are established in superior wisdom.<br>They are heroes, leaders who have destroyed Māra<br>And realized the peace of enlightenment. {67}

“They have attained perfect miraculous powers<br>And are always traveling to hundreds of realms.<br>They see many quintillions of buddhas,<br>As numerous as the sands of the Ganges.<br>Their sight is free of impediment<br>And they see many forms in the ten directions.<br>They are guides for all the beings<br>Who are present throughout the ten directions. {68}

“If one were to describe the entirety of their benefits,<br>Even if one spoke with eloquence<br>For many billions of eons,<br>One could not finish praising their past conduct.<br>Any human who possesses<br>This unequaled, stainless samādhi<br>Has the inexhaustible wealth of the buddhas<br>And an extremely vast ocean of wisdom.” [n1320] {69}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for these and countless other wonderful [n1321] and marvelous bodhisattva qualities, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should hear this revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena samādhi and obtain it, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, [n1322] and make it widely known to others. ^F146a

“They should meditate on the strength of patience, rely on patience, and promulgate patience. They should be dedicated to the Dharma, long for the Dharma, possess the Dharma, engage in the Dharma in a way that accords with the Dharma, and apply themselves to making offerings to the buddhas.

“They should apply themselves to three points. What are the three points? They are ending the kleśas, mastering merit, [n1323] and generating the roots of goodness out of longing for the wisdom of the buddhas and not out of desire for reaching worldly happiness. Apply yourself to those three points.” [n1324]

Thereupon the Bhagavān, to explain what this meant, related an account of the past by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha: [n1325]

“Young man, listen to me as I tell you<br>How I practiced for thousands of eons.<br>Seeking this sublime, excellent samādhi,<br>I made offerings to hundreds of thousands of buddhas. {1}

“In that way, after countless eons had passed,<br>As numerous as the grains of sand in a hundred worlds,<br>When such a number had passed by<br>There appeared a jina named Gaṇeśvara. {2}

“There were no fewer than six hundred billion<br>In the saṅgha of that jina.<br>All were without ouflows, their kleśas had come to an end,<br>They had dhyāna, and were established in the eight liberations. {3}

“At that time the entire surface of this earth<br>Was pleasant and had good harvests, and no disorder.<br>All the people were joyful and happy,<br>And the happiness of humanity was widespread. {4}

“Everyone possessed the strength of merit.<br>They were attractive and beloved.<br>All were rich and possessed much wealth,<br>And physically they experienced divine pleasures. {5}

“They were gentle, with good discipline and few kleśas.<br>They enjoyed [n1326] the strength of patience and had good features.<br>They were like devas within the paradises.<br>They possessed the qualities of correct conduct and understanding. {6}

“At that time there was a sovereign,<br>A king named Varapuṣpasa.<br>He had no fewer than five hundred sons,<br>All endowed with mindfulness and realization. {7} ^F146b

“That king and his sons offered to the Jina,<br>To that compassionate one,<br>Six hundred thousand parks,<br>All beautified by flowers and fruits, [n1327] {8}

“And a hundred thousand various parks<br>With thousands of walkways, seats, and beds,<br>And with a trillion Dharma robes<br>Spread on the ground where they walked and sat. {9}

“Thus the king with great faith<br>Presented to that Sugata<br>In many thousands of ways<br>Whatever renunciants would enjoy. {10}

“That king, who followed the path<br>Of the ten good actions,<br>Came to see the Guide, accompanied by<br>A hundred thousand trillion beings. {11}

“Holding flowers, perfumes, and incense,<br>Parasols, banners, and musical instruments,<br>He made offerings to that Jina,<br>And with his hands in homage sat before him. {12}

“The thousands of bhikṣus were pleased,<br>As were the devas, humans, asuras, and yakṣas, wondering,<br>‘The Jina to whom these offerings were made, will he give a prophecy?<br>Will this lord of humans teach the Dharma?’ {13}

“The self-arisen one knew their thoughts<br>And knew the king’s supreme motivation,<br>That his aspiration was to the further shore,<br>And therefore taught him the samādhi of peace. {14}

“When the Sugata’s voice came forth<br>The earth and its forests shook.<br>A rain of flowers fell from the sky<br>And hundreds of lotuses appeared out of the ground. {15}

“The Teacher had trained in the words and their meaning,<br>And the Guide, knowing the king’s thoughts, gave a prophecy.<br>That lord of men taught the samādhi of peace.<br>Listen to these words and their meaning. {16}

“ ‘All existences are nonexistent: they are concepts,<br>They are insubstantial, they are like mirages and illusions.<br>They are like lightning and clouds, unstable and empty. [n1328]<br>All are without a self, without a being, without a soul. [n1329] {17}

“ ‘Primordially empty, phenomena do not come.<br>They have not come, they are not present, and they have no location.<br>They are always without essence; they have the nature of an illusion.<br>They are all pure—completely pure like space. {18} ^F147a

“ ‘They are neither blue, nor yellow, nor white.<br>Those are just names, vacuous, with a nature that is just sound.<br>They are devoid of mind; their nature is not mind.<br>They are momentary and are devoid of sound. {19}

“ ‘Words do not go anywhere if spoken.<br>Words are not diminished if not spoken.<br>Words do not go in any direction.<br>Words do not come from anywhere. [n1330] {20}

“ ‘Words do not perish, cease, or end,<br>Whether they are spoken or unspoken.<br>Words are said to be always unceasing.<br>Those who know that will be unceasing. {21}

“ ‘In the past, hundreds of thousands of buddhas<br>Have taught the Dharma hundreds of thousands of times.<br>But the Dharma does not cease; words do not cease,<br>And as there is no arising, there is no cessation. {22}

“ ‘Those who know the unceasing Dharma<br>Will always know the unceasing Dharma.<br>Having taught a hundred thousand sūtras,<br>They know that the Dharma is devoid of words. [n1331] {23}

“ ‘The Dharma that the jinas have taught<br>Is unceasing and therefore is not seen.<br>The Dharma is primordially without a self, without a being.<br>Although [n1332] it is taught, it does not cease. {24}

“ ‘The wise teach using all words,<br>But their minds are not captivated by the words.<br>All words are like echoes on a mountain,<br>So therefore never have attachment to words. {25}

“ ‘The Dharma is taught through illusory words<br>And all those words cease in that instant.<br>That which is the characteristic of those words<br>Is the characteristic that all phenomena have. {26}

“ ‘All phenomena have no characteristics, are devoid of characteristics;<br>They all have no characteristics, and are pure of characteristics.<br>They are always empty, and they are as pure as space.<br>In brief, they cannot be enumerated. {27}

“ ‘They are devoid of “composite” or “noncomposite,”<br>And the sages have no concepts concerning them;<br>They have arrived at the noncomposite in all the existences of beings<br>And are always devoid of contrived views. {28}

“ ‘The one whose mind is at rest in that nature<br>Is always without desire, anger, and ignorance.<br>The one who knows phenomena in that way<br>Becomes strong with the strength of samādhi. {29} ^F147b

“ ‘Just as echoes are created through conditions<br>In caves, mountains, and canyons,<br>All that is composite is known to be the same:<br>The entire world is like an illusion, a mirage. {30}

“ ‘This samādhi of peace is taught by one<br>Who has the strength of wisdom, the qualities of the Dharma,<br>Who with the strength of knowledge has the higher cognitions of the sages,<br>And who has skill in methods of speech and knows the definitions of words. {31}

“ ‘The appellations that are spoken are merely appellations;<br>Within saṃsāra there is no end to be found.<br>That which was in the past is devoid of characteristics,<br>And one should be certain that the future is the same. {32}

“ ‘Through engaging in creating karma<br>There will be the best and the worst.<br>Knowing that all things are always empty,<br>Empty by nature, and that all things are without a self, {33}

“ ‘The Jina thus teaches the relative Dharma:<br>Regard the composite and noncomposite in that way.<br>There truly is no self and no human.<br>That is the characteristic of all beings. {34}

“ ‘Good and bad karma are indestructible.<br>Whatever I have created I will have to experience;<br>The result of one’s actions cannot be transferred to others.<br>Nothing is experienced without a cause. [n1333] {35}

“ ‘All existences are illusory and powerless,<br>As insubstantial and insignificant as foam.<br>They are always empty, like illusions and mirages. [n1334]<br>They are taught through words, but are devoid of them. {36}

“ ‘Understand in that way without having pride.<br>Have correct conduct but without attachment,<br>With the power of patience have no conceptualization,<br>And, practicing in that way, rest in equanimity.’ {37}

“The king understood the Dharma<br>That was taught by the Jina.<br>When the king had heard this Dharma from the Jina,<br>Together with his entourage he took up the training. {38}

“The king, having heard this samādhi,<br>Joyous and happy, said these words:<br>‘This samādhi you have taught is excellent<br>And I bow down to your feet.’ {39}

“Eighty thousand beings who were there<br>Had heard this excellent nature of phenomena,<br>This teaching on the ultimate truth,<br>And attained the acceptance of birthlessness. {40} ^F148a

“A person has no origination or cessation,<br>And likewise these phenomena have always been empty.<br>When that is known there is no loss,<br>And the king attained the acceptance of birthlessness. {41}

“The king [n1335] renounced his kingdom<br>And entered homelessness in that Jina’s teaching.<br>And all five hundred princes, no less,<br>Followed him into the homeless state. {42}

“When the king and his princes had entered homelessness,<br>Many thousands of other beings also at that time<br>Entered homelessness in the presence of the Sugata,<br>Seeking to receive the Dharma of that Jina. {43}

“For a full two thousand years<br>The Jina taught the Dharma.<br>And the king, his sons, and the people<br>Practiced the Dharma for those two thousand years. {44}

“And then at a later time<br>The Jina passed into nirvāṇa.<br>The Jina’s śrāvakas also passed away<br>And his Dharma became diminished. {45}

“At that time there was a prince, [n1336]<br>Puṇyamatin, who had faith and trust.<br>There was a bhikṣu connected with his family<br>Who taught to him this samādhi of peace. {46}

“The bhikṣu was gentle and mild,<br>Honored by a hundred thousand beings,<br>Was followed by a billion devas,<br>And was praised when he came to the city. {47}

“He had recollection and realization.<br>He was disciplined and compassionate, and he delighted in correct conduct.<br>His lovely voice was not harsh but gentle,<br>And he had attained the power of knowledge of the sensory constituents. {48}

“That bhikṣu was named Yaśaḥprabha.<br>He received a billion Dharma robes.<br>Unable to endure the strength of his merit<br>A thousand monks became jealous of him. {49}

“He had the strength of merit and the strength of body,<br>The strength of wisdom and the strength of miracles,<br>The strength of correct conduct, the strength of samādhi,<br>And the strength of the Dharma, and therefore was a superior bhikṣu. {50}

“He delighted and was beloved by people.<br>Bhikṣus, upāsakas, and bhikṣuṇīs,<br>Those beings who had faith in the Jina’s teaching,<br>Made offerings to him and honored him. {51} ^F148b

“The one who was the king’s son was there,<br>Puṇyamatin, who had constant faith and trust.<br>When he knew that many bhikṣus had wickedness in mind,<br>He became a protector for his teacher. {52}

“Five hundred thousand people,<br>Armored and holding swords and clubs,<br>Constantly surrounded the bhikṣu<br>Who taught the conduct that is endlessly correct. {53}

“He taught to his followers the Dharma<br>That phenomena are empty, with no self and no soul.<br>Those who were fixated on objects and were attached to a self<br>Did not approve of the bhikṣu’s teaching. {54}

“Those bhikṣus rose up and took up weapons,<br>As they did not approve of emptiness and peace.<br>They said, ‘What this bhikṣu is teaching is not the Dharma,<br>It will be meritorious if we kill him.’ {55}

“The bhikṣu was not afraid when he saw their weapons.<br>He was aware of the emptiness of phenomena,<br>That there was no being or man there to be killed,<br>That these phenomena were as insubstantial as plaster. {56}

“The bhikṣu placed his hands together upon his head<br>And spoke these words of homage to the jinas:<br>‘Through the truth of the emptiness of phenomena<br>May these weapons become coral tree flowers!’ {57}

“He possessed the conduct and discipline of the Sage<br>And as soon as he spoke those words and no others,<br>The earth and its forests shook<br>And the weapons became coral tree flowers. {58}

“At that time, the bhikṣus who believed in objective reality<br>And who were holding weapons became ill-shaped in body.<br>They could not approach any nearer<br>And became frightened and greatly amazed. {59}

“Those who had faith and trust in the Lord of sages,<br>Those who delighted in emptiness and peace,<br>They cried out ‘A la la!’ [n1337] a thousand times,<br>And presented the bhikṣu with hundreds of lengths of cloth. {60}

“The bhikṣu had love for them<br>And said to all the people before him,<br>‘I will practice bodhisattva conduct<br>For the sake of those beings who are angry with me.’ {61}

“Then for no fewer than eighty years<br>He taught emptiness, the treasure of the jinas.<br>And the son of the king protected him<br>From the thousands of bhikṣus who were his adversaries. {62}

“During that time he was despised,<br>And his bhikṣus became few in number.<br>Evil things were heard said about him,<br>But the power of his patience never declined. [n1338] {63} ^F149a

“Then at another time he accomplished<br>A great benefit for hundreds of beings.<br>He recollected countless Dharma teachings [n1339]<br>And at that time Puṇyamatin felt great joy. [n1340] {64}

“He [n1341] respectfully honored the bhikṣu<br>And then Puṇyamatin said to him,<br>‘No one at all should do anything<br>That is displeasing to my teacher.’ {65}

“He [n1342] replied, ‘Young prince, listen to me.<br>It is through the power of patience that buddhas appear.<br>When someone speaks unpleasantly to me,<br>Toward him I feel a great love.’ {66}

“I was that bhikṣu Yaśaḥprabha,<br>Who meditated on patience in previous lives<br>Throughout a hundred thousand eons.”<br>Those were the words Bhagavān Śākyamuni spoke. {67}

“The prince Puṇyamatin, who was<br>The protector of Bhikṣu Yaśaḥprabha,<br>Has been my companion in thousands of lifetimes,<br>And I prophesy that he will be Buddha Maitreya. [n1343] {68}

“The one who made offerings to the teacher Gaṇeśvara,<br>The one who had built a perfect monastery,<br>The one who was previously known as Varapuṣpasa [n1344]<br>Became the Lord of humans Padmottara. [n1345] {69}

“In that way, for many endless eons<br>I held the Dharma of the jinas.<br>In the past, I accomplished the power of patience.<br>Young man, having heard this, follow my example. {70}

“After I have passed into nirvāṇa, in future times<br>When the Dharma is being destroyed<br>Bhikṣus will follow the thoughts of tīrthikas<br>And will forsake my Dharma of peace. {71}

“They will be arrogant, conceited, wicked, and reckless.<br>They will associate with sinners and be greedy for food.<br>They will be attached to their robes and alms bowls, greedy for cloth,<br>And be devoted to acquisition and forsake the Dharma. {72}

“They will be aggressive, fierce, and ungrateful.<br>They will come from vile families, poor families,<br>Enter homelessness within my teaching<br>And will reject the Dharma of peace. {73}

“They will have Māra’s thoughts and will be beings in darkness.<br>They will be under the power of desire and have strong attachment.<br>They will be under the power of ignorance and be ignorant fools,<br>And they will not delight in the Dharma of emptiness and peace. {74} ^F149b

“The bhikṣus, bhikṣuṇīs, and laypeople,<br>With wicked minds, will be avaricious and stupid.<br>They will always become overpowered in that way,<br>And in the later times they will reject enlightenment. {75}

“Listen, young man, to these my words.<br>A bhikṣu should always dwell in solitude.<br>Those who long for peace and emptiness<br>Should possess this Dharma of the jinas. {76}

“The one who possesses this samādhi<br>Has practiced homelessness in my teaching,<br>Is ordained as a bhikṣu and practices poṣadha,<br>And eats free of craving, without attachment to food. {77}

“Forsaking all concern for life and body,<br>Meditate on emptiness, upon perfect peace.<br>Meditating with dedication, complete dedication.<br>Like a deer, live always in the forests. {78}

“Always make offerings to the jinas [n1346]<br>With parasols, banners, [n1347] and with dwellings. [n1348]<br>Make offerings to stūpas of the sugatas<br>And quickly attain this samādhi. {79}

“Develop the aspiration for the state of enlightenment.<br>Beautify the stūpas of the sugatas,<br>Adorning them with gold and covering them with silver,<br>And have beautiful images from precious materials made. {80}

“Make a commitment to attain enlightenment<br>And make all the good offerings that there are in the world,<br>Of all that is pleasing to devas and humans,<br>And honor the buddhas with desirable offerings. {81}

“See as the true nature, too, all the lords of humans;<br>For within the worlds in all ten directions,<br>The jinas who are present and those who have passed away<br>Have come to be buddhas through the true nature. {82}

“Have the aspiration to be generous to all.<br>Have pure conduct and a stable mind.<br>Delight in patience and always delight in kindness,<br>And know that all phenomena are empty. {83}

“Develop diligence confidently and fearlessly.<br>Delight in dhyāna and delight in solitude.<br>Develop wisdom, completely pure wisdom,<br>And quickly become compassionate. {84} ^F150a

“Always pacify desire through contemplating ugliness,<br>Overcome anger with the power of patience,<br>Overcome ignorance with the power of wisdom,<br>And attain the enlightenment praised by the jinas. {85}

“The body has no essence; it is like foam.<br>It creates suffering, and is putrid and foul smelling.<br>Know all aggregates to be insubstantial<br>And quickly attain the highest wisdom. {86}

“Never hold views that give rise to bad actions:<br>That there is a self, an individual, and a soul.<br>Know that all phenomena are empty<br>And quickly reach the highest enlightenment. {87}

“Never have yearning for possessions.<br>Do not be distressed if you do not obtain alms,<br>Be unmoved by praise or blame,<br>And be as unshakable as Mount Meru. {88}

“With veneration seek the Dharma;<br>Having heard it then become that.<br>Maintain the conduct of the jinas<br>And quickly go to the realm of Sukhāvatī. {89}

“Be even-minded toward all beings.<br>Do not have likes or dislikes in your mind.<br>Do not long for gain and fame,<br>And quickly become a buddha, a lord of sages. {90}

“Always describe the qualities of the buddhas<br>Correctly through their definitions,<br>So that the beings who hear about the qualities will have faith<br>And you cause them to aspire to the qualities of a buddha. {91}

“Always venerate your teacher,<br>Your parents, and similarly all beings.<br>Do not fall under the power of pride,<br>And attain the thirty-two signs of a great being. {92}

“Avoid all crowds without exception,<br>And always delight in solitude.<br>Always be pleasant, disciplined, and peaceful.<br>Be beneficial for yourself and beneficial to other beings. {93}

“Cultivate kindness and compassion,<br>And always aspire to rejoicing and equanimity.<br>Always follow the teaching of the jinas<br>And quickly become one who benefits the world. {94}

“Never gain wicked friends;<br>Have friends who are noble. [n1349]<br>Those who long for emptiness and peace<br>Are established in the path to supreme enlightenment. {95} ^F150b

“Do not train on the level of the śrāvakas,<br>And do not delight in their practice.<br>Do not turn your mind away from the buddha qualities<br>And quickly become a buddha, a lord of jinas. {96}

“Always speak pure, true words.<br>Do not speak harshly or tell lies.<br>Always speak gently and pleasantly<br>And obtain the speech of the world’s teacher. {97}

“Do not be concerned with your life and body.<br>Do not criticize others and praise yourself.<br>Accomplish your own good qualities<br>And have equanimity toward the conduct of others. {98}

“Always delight in the liberations and emptiness.<br>Do not make prayers for rebirth in the realms of beings.<br>Abandon all concepts without exception<br>And always abide in a state without concepts. {99}

“Reject the extremes at all times.<br>Do not follow nihilism or eternalism.<br>Always know that everything is dependent,<br>And in that way become such a teacher. {100}

“Reject delighting in the pleasures of desires,<br>Reject the stains of rigid anger,<br>Reject all the darkness of ignorance,<br>And become a lion among men, delighting in peace. {101}

“Always see that the permanent is impermanent.<br>Be liberated from the happiness and suffering of all existences.<br>See that self and purity are nonself and impure.<br>Meditate and become a lord of men. {102}

“The jinas, the lamps for the world,<br>Taught whatever Dharma would be beneficial.<br>They defeated the armies of the māras<br>And attained the supreme, highest enlightenment. {103}

“I have taught the good qualities that there are<br>And described hundreds of faults.<br>Reject the faults and practice the qualities.<br>Then, young man, in this life you will become a buddha.” {104}

Then the Bhagavān  said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, you should train by thinking, ‘I shall have self-control through physical restraint.’ ^F151a

“Young man, what is meant by physical restraint? That which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas are free of attachment to all phenomena.

“Young man, that which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the thirty-two primary signs of a great being.

“That which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the eighty secondary signs of a great being.

“Young man, that which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the ten strengths, the four fearlessnesses, and the eighteen distinct qualities of a buddha.

“Young man, that which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the three doorways to liberation. What are these three? They are emptiness, the absence of attributes, and the absence of aspiration. They attain those three doorways to liberation.

“Young man, that which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the four great brahmavihāras. What are the four great brahmavihāras? They are great love, great compassion, great joy, and great equanimity. They attain those four great brahmavihāras.

“Young man, that which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the four discernments. What are the four discernments? They are the discernment of meaning, the discernment of phenomena, the discernment of definitions, and the discernment of eloquence.  They attain those four discernments. ^F151b

“Young man, that which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the thirty-seven aspects of enlightenment. What are the thirty-seven aspects of enlightenment? They are the four kinds of mindfulness, the four correct exertions, the four bases for miraculous powers, the five powers, the five strengths, the seven aspects of enlightenment, and the noble eightfold path. They attain those thirty-seven aspects of enlightenment.

“Young man, that which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the state of great compassion, attain the state of great equanimity, and attain easeful examination and analysis of phenomena.

“Moreover, young man, that which is called ‘physical restraint’ is the physical restraint through which bodhisattva mahāsattvas desist from killing, taking what is not given, not maintaining celibacy, lying, slandering, harsh speech, idle talk, avarice, malice, and wrong views; desist from fraud in weights, fraud in measures, and fraud in wealth; [n1350] desist from capturing, [n1351] binding, restraining, [n1352] beating, [n1353] threatening, [n1354] severing, [n1355] impaling, and terrorizing; desist from desire and greed; desist from wild hand movements, wild leg movements, and unrestrained movements of the legs and arms; and desist from wicked habits of body, speech, or mind so that, like palm trees that have had their tops cut off, they will not arise again in the future.

“Therefore, young man, understand this teaching in the following way.  Young man, in the past, innumerable, vast, immeasurable, inconceivable, unfathomable countless eons ago, at that time and in those days, there appeared in the world the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Jñānaprabhāsa, who was perfect in wisdom and conduct, a sugata, a knower of the world, an unsurpassable guide who tamed beings, a teacher of devas and humans, a buddha, and a bhagavān. ^F152a

“At that time and in those days, the lifespan of the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Jñānaprabhāsa was six hundred million years. He had a śrāvaka saṅgha of six hundred million arhats. There were countless bodhisattva mahāsattvas who held the supreme Dharma.

“Young man, at that time and in those days, there was a king named Viveśacintin. King Viveśacintin came with eight hundred million people into the presence of the Tathāgata. When he arrived he bowed his head down to the feet of the Tathāgata, circumambulated the Bhagavān three times, and sat down in one place. Once King Viveśacintin had sat down in one place, he honored the Tathāgata.

“Then the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Jñānaprabhāsa, knowing the superior aspiration of King Viveśacintin and his followers, taught them from this Dharma teaching by chanting the following verses on entering through the doorway of the samādhi of physical restraint:

“ ‘Just as space and the sky are pure,<br>Ultimately pure, and with a clear nature,<br>The restraint of the body, too, is pure,<br>And cannot be taught in verse. {1}

“ ‘This physical restraint is devoid and empty,<br>And those are also the two characteristics of the body.<br>Just like space it is without characteristics.<br>That is taught to be the characteristic of the body’s restraint. {2} ^F152b

“ ‘Those who know that characteristic of the body’s restraint<br>Will never be ones without restraint.<br>How can those without activity have a field of conduct?<br>Those who are immaculate have no birth. {3}

“ ‘One cannot have this restraint while pursuing desires<br>Through yearning for forms and enjoyments.<br>Not knowing the wickedness of existence,<br>One cannot know this restraint of the body. {4}

“ ‘There will never be birth<br>For those who have immaculate restraint.<br>They have qualities like those of the arhats,<br>Which cannot easily be known by tīrthikas. {5}

“ ‘Those who are terrified of the three realms<br>Will not develop desire for sensual gratification.<br>They who do not wish for the pleasures of a king<br>Will know this kind of restraint of the body. {6}

“ ‘The restraint of the body is said to have this meaning.<br>It is a meaning that cannot be taught through words.<br>The one who knows this way of the Dharma<br>Is firmly established in this restraint. {7}

“ ‘I teach the meaning to those who are engaged with the meaning,<br>To those wise ones intent upon the way of the meaning.<br>Those engaged in the meaning shun that which is not the meaning<br>And are always firmly established in that restraint. {8}

“ ‘How can one know the meaning<br>That is spoken of in the teaching of the jinas?<br>Those who know the nature of that way of meaning<br>Are said to be established in the restraint of the body. {9}

“ ‘Those who know insubstantiality, emptiness,<br>The absence of a self, and the absence of attributes<br>Will never be without that restraint,<br>And in that way they will train in correct certainty. {10}

“ ‘They know that existents are nonexistent<br>And do not give rise to attachment to existents.<br>They will never give rise to attachment to any existent<br>And will reach the samādhi of the absence of attributes. {11}

“ ‘Those who know that phenomena have no self,<br>Have an empty nature and the characteristic of clarity,<br>Will never be without that restraint,<br>And thus will have definite correct understanding. [n1356] {12}

“ ‘Those who know the five skandhas to be empty<br>Know their empty nature that is devoid of a self.<br>They will never be without that restraint<br>In any physical activity that they perform. {13}

“ ‘Those who focus on attributes, who are without restraint,<br>Who are constantly fixed in the conception of a self—<br>Those beings who are attached to forms<br>Are overcome by unrestrained desires. {14} ^F153a

“ ‘Those who are trained in the true, highest point,<br>The gentle ones who have realized emptiness,<br>Are never overcome by the arising of desires<br>That cause the unrestrained to go to the lower realms. {15}

“ ‘Just as all the ants together cannot shake<br>And cannot move great Mount Sumeru,<br>Even divine forms cannot unsettle<br>A wise one who is correctly trained. {16}

“ ‘Someone may be able to paint a picture on space,<br>Someone may be able to grasp space in his hand,<br>But desire, anger, or millions of māras<br>Will not be able to unsettle such a wise one. {17}

“ ‘Someone may be able to catch an echo,<br>A stone may be able to float on the water,<br>But no one can see the thoughts of someone<br>Who is trained in this restraint of the body. {18}

“ ‘Someone may be able to catch all the sounds<br>In the entire world and put them in a box,<br>But they cannot know whether someone who maintains<br>The restraint of the body is or is not maintaining it. {19}

“ ‘Someone may be able to catch the light from the disk of the sun,<br>Or the thunder and lightning that burst from the clouds,<br>But they cannot know the nature of the body<br>Of someone who has trained in the restraint of the body. {20}

“ ‘Someone may be able to catch in a trap or a net<br>The circle of wind that moves through the four directions,<br>But they cannot come to know the body<br>Of someone who is established in the restraint of the body. {21}

“ ‘This is not the domain of activity of beings.<br>It is the domain of a wise one who has a controlled mind.<br>It is the domain of activity of someone with restraint of the body<br>Who, like space, is unstained by worldly qualities. {22}

“ ‘Someone may be able to see the tracks of all the creatures<br>That move through the sky in all four directions,<br>But they would not be able to know the extent<br>Of the fields of activity of such a person’s mind or body. {23}

“ ‘Those who are established in this restraint of the body<br>Do not have any of the various kinds of kleśas.<br>They have eliminated even the minor kleśas, [n1357]<br>And thus are trained in the restraint of the body. {24}

“ ‘They cannot be harmed by weapons or by fire,<br>And in that way their bodies are ungraspable.<br>They remain in the peace, perfect peace, of samādhi,<br>And in that way they are trained in the restraint of the body. {25} ^F153b

“ ‘Thus established, they have no fear, they have no terror,<br>Their minds are undisturbed, and they feel no envy.<br>They who are thus trained in the restraint of the body<br>Have become liberated from all misfortune. {26}

“ ‘They are not afraid of poison or weapons;<br>They are not afraid in the middle of fire or water.<br>They who are thus trained in the restraint of the body<br>Have become liberated from all misfortune. {27}

“ ‘They are without fear among thieves,<br>Swindlers, criminals, and poisonous snakes.<br>In this way they have no conception of a self<br>And, liberated from that concept, they have no fear. {28}

“ ‘Those who are freed from fear do not become frightened.<br>As there is no fear, there is no instability.<br>How can those who are unshakable feel fear?<br>Even millions of māras cannot disturb them. {29}

“ ‘The one who benefits bodhisattvas<br>Explains and teaches the practice of restraint.<br>Even millions of māras cannot disturb<br>The one who has trained in this restraint of the body. {30}

“ ‘Unimpeded knowledge of the entire Dharma,<br>The complete eighty secondary signs,<br>And the thirty-two primary signs of a pure mind<br>Are not difficult to obtain for one established in restraint. {31}

“ ‘Whoever wishes to realize the qualities of a buddha,<br>Which are inconceivable and beyond measure,<br>Should train in this kind of restraint of the body<br>And become a shrine for the entire world. {32}

“ ‘Whoever wishes for these qualities of a great sage,<br>For the ten inconceivable strengths of a buddha,<br>Should train in this restraint of the body.<br>The strengths are not difficult to attain for one thus trained. {33}

“ ‘The eighteen distinct qualities of a buddha,<br>In which the jinas are established,<br>Are not difficult to attain for someone<br>Who has trained in this restraint of the body. {34}

“ ‘The seven limbs of enlightenment of the great sages,<br>And their discernments and bases of miraculous powers,<br>Are not difficult to attain for someone<br>Who has trained in this restraint of the body. {35} ^F154a

“ ‘The four brahmavihāras and the dhyānas,<br>The doorways to liberation that have been taught,<br>And easeful examination and analysis<br>Are not difficult to attain for one established in restraint. {36}

“ ‘One who is established in this supreme restraint<br>Dwells in compassion and also in equanimity,<br>And likewise practices the conduct of supreme love,<br>And has the motivation to benefit all beings. [n1358] {37}

“ ‘Maintaining mindfulness and correct exertion,<br>The five strengths and five powers of the great sages,<br>And the eight branches of the supreme path of the noble ones<br>Are not difficult to attain for one trained in restraint of the body. {38}

“ ‘Also, the other sublime qualities of a buddha,<br>Which are inconceivable and beyond measure,<br>Are all not difficult to attain for someone<br>Who has trained in this restraint of the body.’ {39}

“When he had listened to this restraint of the body,<br>The eminent king [n1359] gained exceptional accomplishment. [n1360]<br>He felt the highest joy and unequaled happiness<br>And entered homelessness in that Jina’s teaching. {40}

“For a hundred million years he entered homelessness<br>And practiced a pure and perfect celibacy.<br>He also meditated on the four brahmavihāras<br>In order to benefit the world and its devas. {41}

“Having meditated well on the brahmavihāras,<br>He saw eight hundred million buddhas,<br>And even more, as numerous as the Ganges sands,<br>And he practiced this supreme celibacy. {42}

“He entered homelessness in all of their teachings<br>And practiced a pure and perfect celibacy.<br>He became an excellent bhikṣu dharmabhāṇaka<br>Who was very learned and had eloquent speech. {43}

“Knowing well this restraint of the body,<br>He had unimpaired conduct, faultless conduct,<br>Pure conduct, and unalloyed conduct,<br>And maintained noble conduct that was immaculate. {44}

“If you think, young man, that Viśeṣacintin,<br>The eminent king of that time, was someone else,<br>Do not see him as being anyone else:<br>That was me while I was practicing bodhisattva conduct. {45} ^F154b

“Therefore, young man, follow my teaching,<br>And maintain this restraint of the body.<br>Teach it, too, to millions of other beings,<br>And before long you will become the same as me.” {46}

Then the Bhagavān said to Candraprabha, “Young man, you should train by thinking, ‘I will practice completely pure physical conduct in that way.’ Why is that? Because, young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure physical conduct have no fear of the hells, of rebirth as an animal, of the realm of Yama, or of any other lower existences. They have no fear of water, and no fear of fire, of poison, of weapons, of lions, of tigers, of bears, [n1361] of elephants, of bulls, or of humans and nonhumans.

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure physical conduct can place the great billion-world universe on the palm of their hand and throw it up to the height of one palm tree, two palm trees, three palm trees, four palm trees, five palm trees, six palm trees, seven palm trees, or as high as they wish to throw it.

“Moreover, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure physical conduct attain the perfection of supreme miraculous powers. They have ripened the bases of miraculous powers, possess pure merit, and have detachment. They can go anywhere, have attained this samādhi, have completely perfected immaculate merit, and have unimpeded vision of all worlds, and therefore have gained miraculous powers. What is this attainment of miraculous powers? Through miraculous powers there is the perfection of the accomplishment of aspirations [n1362] and success. [n1363]

“What kind of attainment of miraculous powers are these miraculous powers that are spoken of?  Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who possess miraculous powers experience a range of different kinds of miracles: they transform from one to many, from many to one, and from visible to invisible; they pass without impediment through house walls, through city walls, and through mountains; they travel through the air just like a bird; they dive into the ground and emerge from it, just as they would in water; they stand on water just like they would on the ground; they give off smoke and flames, just like a great blaze of fire; their bodies emit many thousands of trillions of great torrents of water, just like a great cloud that can extinguish the great fire of a thousand-billion world universe being on fire; [n1364] they grasp in their hands and polish the moon and the sun, which are so miraculous, powerful, and majestic; and just as they wish, their bodies have power over beings, as far up as those in Brahmā’s realm.” ^F155a

Thereupon the Bhagavān recited these verses: [n1365]

“They dive into the earth and reemerge,<br>They walk unimpeded on water,<br>They travel through the air like a bird,<br>And they miraculously emit smoke and flames. [n1366] {47}

“Just as the wind is unimpeded by space,<br>And a multitude of clouds move through it,<br>In that way the yogins fly through the air,<br>Unimpeded like the wind and the clouds. {48}

“The skilled bodhisattvas, on seeing<br>Realms burning in a blazing inferno,<br>Emit water from their bodies,<br>Extinguishing the fire of millions of realms. {i} [n1367]

“The skilled bodhisattvas, while seated,<br>Grasp the sun and moon in their hands.<br>Seated, they know the realm of Brahmā<br>And teach the Dharma to millions of Brahmās. [n1368] {49} ^F155b

“When they wish to teach the Dharma,<br>The entire billion-world universe hears them.<br>As they wish, they teach the Dharma<br>In millions of realms to millions of beings.” {50}

Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, you should train by thinking, ‘I will practice completely pure physical conduct in that way.’ Why is that? Because, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure physical conduct have a divine sense of hearing so that they can hear from afar the voices of devas, humans, beings in the hells, those reborn as animals, and those in the realm of Yama.

“Moreover, young man, you should train by thinking, ‘I will practice completely pure physical conduct in that way.’ Why is that? Because, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure physical conduct, while they are seated, with their divine sense of smell can smell from afar all the divine pleasant aromas of the Dharma that there are in all the worlds in the billion-world universe.” [n1369]

Then again the Bhagavān said to Candraprabha, “Young man, you should train by thinking, ‘I will practice completely pure physical conduct in that way.’ Why is that? Because, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure physical conduct know accurately the motivation, conduct, and thoughts of other beings and individuals. They accurately know a mind that has desire to be a mind that has desire. They accurately know a mind that is without desire to be a mind that is without desire.

“It is the same as that for having anger and being without anger, having ignorance and being without ignorance, having craving and being without craving,  having grasping and being without grasping, having concentration and distraction, having error and no error, having greatness and no greatness, having clarity and no clarity, being valid and being invalid, being surpassable and unsurpassable, being in meditation and not being in meditation, and being liberated and not being liberated, and they accurately know a mind that has kleśas to be a mind that has kleśas, and they accurately know a mind that has no kleśas to be a mind that has no kleśas. ^F156a

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure physical conduct remember previous lives in many ways: they remember one previous life, or two, or three, or four, or five, or ten, or twenty, or thirty, or forty, or fifty, or remember a hundred previous lifetimes. They remember a thousand lives, a hundred thousand lives, and so on, up to many quintillions of previous lives.

“They remember an eon of dissolution and an eon of origination, and so on up to many eons of dissolution and eons of origination.

“They remember one eon, and they remember a hundred eons, a thousand eons, a hundred thousand eons, and so on, up to remembering many quintillions of eons.

“They remember as many as ten million past lives, saying, ‘I was born as such and such a being, this was my name, this was my family, this was my caste, this was my color, this was the food that I ate, this was my livelihood, this is how long a lifespan was, this is how long I lived, and this was the happiness and suffering I experienced. Then when I died I was reborn as such and such; then when I died again I was reborn here.’

“They remember correctly the many different aspects of their previous lives, such as what appearance they had, the place where they lived, and the cause for that rebirth. ^F156b

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure physical conduct have divine vision, which surpasses human vision, so that they know accurately, according to the karma of beings, their deaths and their rebirths, whether they have good color or bad color, whether they are fortunate or unfortunate, whether it is a good rebirth or a bad rebirth, and whether they are going to the higher realms or the lower realms.

“They say, ‘These beings conducted themselves badly with their bodies, conducted themselves badly with their speech, and conducted themselves badly in their minds. They maligned the noble ones, had wrong views, and truly held those wrong views. Because of those causes, after they died they fell to the lower realms and were reborn in the hells. These beings conducted themselves well with their bodies, conducted themselves well with their speech, and conducted themselves well in their minds. They did not malign the noble ones, had correct views, and truly held those correct views. Because of those causes, after they died they went to the higher realms and were reborn in the paradises.’

“In that way they have the pure divine vision that transcends that of humans, so that they know correctly, according to the karma of beings, their deaths and their rebirths, whether they have good color or bad color, whether they are fortunate or unfortunate, whether it is a good rebirth or a bad rebirth, and whether they go to the higher realms or the lower realms.

“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure physical conduct in one instant of wisdom accurately know, hear, see, and understand everything that is to be known, to be heard, to be seen, to be realized, and to be manifested.” [n1370]

Thereupon the Bhagavān recited these verses:

“The levels of higher cognitions<br>Of the protector bodhisattvas are taught.<br>The ones who remain in samādhi<br>Are known as bodhisattvas. {51} ^F157a

“Their hearing is purified to become<br>Inconceivable divine hearing.<br>They hear the Dharma that is<br>Taught by all the buddhas. {52}

“The skilled bodhisattvas, while sitting,<br>With a divine sense of smell<br>Smell all the divine Dharma aromas<br>In the great billion-world universe. [n1371] {i}

“They know the minds of all beings:<br>Whether they have or do not have desire,<br>Whether they have or do not have anger,<br>Whether they have or do not have ignorance. {53}

“They know where they lived in the past,<br>Those places where they previously lived<br>Throughout billions of eons;<br>They know them without any impediment. {54}

“Their sight, too, is purified;<br>They have insurpassable, divine sight.<br>They see perfectly the deaths<br>Of beings and their rebirths. {55}

“Within a single instant<br>They know all lifetimes.<br>They know correctly every single<br>Phenomenon that can be known.” [n1372] {56}

Then the Bhagavān said to Candraprabha, “Young man, you should train by thinking, ‘I will engage in completely pure conduct of speech in that way.’

“Young man, what is the restraint of speech? Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure conduct of speech attain the inconceivable, unimpeded buddha’s speech, which has sixty aspects. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech have the attainment of noble words. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech attain the thirty-two primary signs of a great being. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech attain the eighty secondary signs of a great being. Young man, that is the restraint of speech. ^F157b

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech attain the ten strengths of a tathāgata, the four fearlessnesses, and the eighteen distinct qualities of a buddha. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech attain the three doorways to liberation. What are these three? They are emptiness, the absence of attributes, and the absence of aspiration. They attain those three doorways to liberation. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech attain the four great brahmavihāras. What are the four great brahmavihāras? They are great love, great compassion, great joy, and great equanimity. They attain those four great brahmavihāras. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech attain the four discernments. What are the four discernments? They are the discernment of meaning, the discernment of phenomena, the discernment of definitions, and the discernment of eloquence. They attain those four discernments. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech attain the thirty-seven aspects of enlightenment. What are the thirty-seven aspects of enlightenment? They are the four kinds of mindfulness, the four correct exertions, the four bases for miraculous powers, the five powers, the five strengths, the seven aspects of enlightenment, and the noble eightfold path. They attain those thirty-seven aspects of enlightenment. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech attain the state of great compassion,  attain the state of great equanimity, attain easeful examination, and attain the quality of being devoid of examination. Young man, that is the restraint of speech. ^F158a

“Moreover, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech desist from killing, taking what is not given, not maintaining celibacy, lying, slandering, harsh speech, and idle talk. Those bodhisattva mahāsattvas desist from speaking untrue words to their parents and their teachers; from maligning the Buddha, Dharma, and Saṅgha; and from any other words that are harmful words. They know those words to be like echoes. They perceive them to be like apparitions, mirages, hallucinations, and illusions, and in that way they do not objectify words, conceptualize them, become proud of them, view them, or become attached to them. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.”

Then the Bhagavān said to Candraprabha, “Young man, you should train by thinking, ‘I will engage in completely pure conduct of speech in that way.’ Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of speech have no fear of any lower realm and obtain the entire Dharma of the buddhas. They attain all the miraculous powers and higher cognitions of the buddhas. Young man, that is the restraint of speech.”

Thereupon the Bhagavān recited these verses: [n1373]

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which<br>The bodhisattvas will attain the unimpeded knowledge<br>Of the entirety of the Dharma. [n1374] {57}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Attain the unimpeded, inconceivable buddha speech<br>That has sixty aspects. [n1375] {i} ^F158b

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Attain the thirty-two primary signs,<br>The ten strengths, and the distinct qualities of a buddha. {58}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Attain all the qualities of buddhahood<br>That have previously been taught by me. {59}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Attain the brahmavihāras, the discernments,<br>And marvelous, inconceivable qualities. {60}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Attain the mindfulnesses, the correct exertions,<br>The strengths, the powers, and the bases for miraculous powers. {61}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Attain great equanimity, the fearlessnesses,<br>And the state of great compassion. {62}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Attain pure, easeful examination<br>And the peace of being devoid of examination. {63}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Do not lie, speak words of slander,<br>Indulge in idle talk, or speak harsh words. {64}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Will never say that they forsake the Dharma<br>Or forsake the Buddha or the Saṅgha. {65}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Do not speak words that are unture<br>In front of their parents or teachers. {66}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Desist from all other words<br>That are harmful, without exception. {67}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the restraint of speech through which the wise<br>Fearlessly use words that are like echoes<br>And that are analogous to dreams. {68}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the bodhisattva’s use of words<br>As being without self, without a soul, unmoving,<br>Arising through conditions, and as deceptive as a dream. {69} ^F159a

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is the bodhisattva’s use of words,<br>With cessation always being like a dream,<br>And nirvāṇa also being like a dream. {70}

“That which is called the restraint of speech<br>Is when there are no words at all to be found.<br>It is not conceptualizing them or being proud of them,<br>And not being dependent on them or attached to them.” {71}

Then the Bhagavān said to Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, you should train by thinking, ‘I shall be endowed with the restraint of the mind.’

“Young man, what is the restraint of the mind? [n1376] Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind are without fear of the Dharma of the buddhas, [n1377] and have attained the unshakable, liberated mind. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind obtain the samādhi that is like a vajra. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind obtain the light rays that are called as bright as flames. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain the perfect voice of a buddha, which has sixty aspects. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind have the attainment of noble words. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain the thirty-two primary signs of a great being. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain the eighty secondary signs of a great being. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind. ^F159b

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain the ten strengths of a tathāgata, the four fearlessnesses, and the eighteen distinct qualities of a buddha. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain the three doorways to liberation. What are the three doorways to liberation? They are emptiness, the absence of attributes, and the absence of aspiration. They attain those three doorways to liberation. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain the four great brahmavihāras. What are the four great brahmavihāras? They are great love, great compassion, great joy, and great equanimity. They attain those four great brahmavihāras. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain the four discernments. What are the four discernments? They are the discernment of meaning, the discernment of phenomena, the discernment of definitions, and the discernment of eloquence. They attain those four discernments. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain the thirty-seven aspects of enlightenment. What are the thirty-seven aspects of enlightenment? They are the four kinds of mindfulness, the four correct exertions, the four bases for miraculous powers, the five powers, the five strengths, the seven aspects of enlightenment, and the noble eightfold path. They attain those thirty-seven aspects of enlightenment. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain the state of great compassion, attain the state of great equanimity, and attain easeful examination  and the quality of being devoid of examination. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind. ^F160a

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind attain engagement in conduct with the wish to benefit others. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have the restraint of the mind do not associate with wrong views in order to desist from wrong views; they do not associate with avarice in order to desist from avarice; they do not associate with malice in order to desist from malice; they do not associate with laziness in order to desist from laziness; they do not wish to deceive their parents or their teachers; and they do not develop desire, anger, or ignorance and do not associate with them. They do not abandon the aspiration to enlightenment, they do not destabilize their superior aspiration, and also the bodhisattvas desist from all other harmful thoughts in their minds, and do not associate with them. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.

“They perceive the mind as being like a dream, being like a mirage, being like an apparition, and being like a hallucination, something that does not come from anywhere and does not go anywhere. They perceive happiness as being like a dream, perceive it as being impermanent like a dream, perceive it as being devoid of self like a dream, perceive it as being devoid of a soul like a dream, and they do not objectify it, conceptualize it, become proud of it, view it, or become attached to it. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.”

Then the Bhagavān said to Candraprabha, “Young man, you should train by thinking, ‘I will practice completely pure conduct of the mind in that way.’ Why is that?  Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have completely pure conduct of the mind avoid all unfavorable conditions and obtain the countless Dharma teachings of the buddhas. They obtain from all the buddhas the higher cognitions of the buddhas and the unshakable, liberated mind. Young man, that is the restraint of the mind.” ^F160b

Thereupon the Bhagavān recited these verses:

“All of you listen with an unwavering mind,<br>For I will teach the restraint of the mind.<br>If you wish to attain buddhahood quickly,<br>Listen to me and then practice this. {72}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Attain the vast, unshakable, supreme peace,<br>The wonderful, inconceivable Dharma of the jinas,<br>That is what is called the pure restraint of the mind. {73}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Attain the liberated, eternally unshakable mind,<br>And likewise the supreme samādhi that is like a vajra,<br>That is what is called the most splendid restraint of the mind. {74}

“That which wise ones practice and through which<br>They accomplish light rays of great benefit,<br>And attain the voice with sixty aspects,<br>That is what is called the purest restraint of the mind. {75}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Quickly attain the thirty-two primary signs<br>And attain the ten strengths and every quality of buddhahood,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {76}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Attain the discernments and the fearlessnesses,<br>And wonderful, inconceivable, supreme qualities,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {77}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Attain the mindfulnesses, the bases of miraculous powers,<br>The correct efforts, and the five powers and strengths,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {78}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Attain all of the four brahmavihāras, and likewise<br>Emptiness, the absence of attributes, and the absence of aspiration,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. [n1378] {i}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Attain the state of compassion, great equanimity,<br>And the practice of correct conduct, great love, and peace,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {ii} ^F161a

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Quickly attain the seven limbs of enlightenment<br>And similarly the eight aspects of the supreme path,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {79}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Attain the supreme state of equanimity<br>And the stainless, supreme state of compassion,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {80}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Attain easeful examination, a mind of pure peace,<br>And detachment through a wealth of qualities,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {81}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Do not associate with evil people and those with wrong views, [n1379]<br>And do not develop a mind of malice, or a mind of avarice,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {82}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Do not act with pretense for even an instant,<br>And do not act with deception toward the guru,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {83}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Do not develop desire or anger in their minds,<br>And similarly never give rise to ignorance,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {84}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>In their minds do not forsake enlightenment,<br>And whose superior motivation is never shaken,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {85}

“That restraint of the mind through which wise ones<br>Do not keep with any of the other numerous faults<br>Of the mind that there may be,<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {86}

“They understand the mind as being like an illusion,<br>Like a dream, and similarly like a mirage,<br>Always having the characteristic of a hallucination:<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {87}

“They understand happiness to be like a dream,<br>And similarly, impermanent, empty, and transient.<br>Wise ones understand the mind in that way:<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {88}

“They understand the mind to be without a soul, without being,<br>And arising from conditions like a whirled torch’s circle of fire,<br>Not coming from anywhere nor going anywhere:<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {89} ^F161b

“They never objectify the mind at all,<br>And are without conceptualization or pride;<br>They do not fixate upon it or become attached to it:<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind. {90}

“They understand the ultimate truth to be like a dream,<br>And nirvāṇa to be the same as a dream;<br>Wise ones understand the mind in that way:<br>That is what is called the supreme restraint of the mind.” {91}

“Young man, what is purity of action? Seeing the three existences as being like a dream and becoming free of desire. Young man, that is purity of action.

“Young man, what is the transcendence of the mind’s fixation on perceptions? It is knowing that the skandhas, dhātus, and āyatanas are like illusions, and renouncing them. That is the transcendence of the mind’s fixation on perceptions.

“What is the knowledge of the skandhas? It is perceiving the skandhas to be like mirages.

“What is the equality of the dhātus? It is renouncing the dhātus as being like apparitions.

“What is the elimination of the āyatanas? It is renouncing the āyatanas as being like hallucinations.

“What is the renunciation of craving? [n1380] It is not fixating on any phenomena. That is the renunciation of craving.

“What is the direct realization of birthlessness? It is not having the perception of any phenomena.

“What is engagement in activity? It is not giving up because of suffering arising from diligence.

“What is the illumination of causes? It is perceiving that the skandhas are like echoes.

“What is the non-dissipation of the results of karma? It is knowing that the results of karma do not dissipate like a dream.

“What is insight into phenomena? It is not seeing phenomena.

“What is the meditation of the path?  It is meditation on the nonperception of all phenomena. ^F162a

“What is meeting the tathāgatas? It is practicing the training of all the buddhas.

“What is sharp wisdom? It is the patience of the birthlessness of phenomena.

“What is penetrating into beings? [n1381] It is knowing the higher and the lower faculties.

“What is knowledge of phenomena? It is the nonperception of phenomena.

“What is the knowledge of engaging in discernment? It is engaging in the true nature of phenomena.

“What is the knowledge of the different kinds of letters and words? It is the knowledge of engaging with the three mantras, [n1382] and knowing what is the form and what is not the form of words.

“What is the transcendence of matter? It is the understanding of immateriality.

“What is the understanding of sounds? It is knowing them to be like echoes. Young man, that is the understanding of sounds.

“What is the attainment of joy? It is the nonperception of all phenomena, the ending of the suffering that arises from saṃsāra, and putting down one’s burden.

“What is experiencing the joy of the Dharma? It is never abandoning teaching, pleasing, and seeing the excellence of one’s yāna. [n1383]

“What is abiding? It is the realization of the truths of the noble ones. [n1384]

“What is sincerity? It is uncontrived conduct.

“What is no longer having frowns? It is being without anger.

“What is being pleasant? [n1385] It is being good company.

“What is being gentle? [n1386] It is being beneficial to others. [n1387]

“What is being courteous? It is being welcoming and standing up quickly. [n1388]

“What is having veneration [n1389] for the guru? It is being fearful [n1390] of the guru and perceiving the guru as the kalyāṇamitra.

“What is respect for the guru? It is honoring and serving the guru.

“What is being content with occurences?  It is having no attachment to anything that occurs. ^F162b

“What is never being satisfied with the good actions one has done? It is pursuing every kind of good action and seeking for any good action.

“What is having a pure livelihood? It is being satisfied with anything, using no trickery, [n1391] no flattery, not being covetous, and not having the desire to acquire.

“What is not forsaking the solitary life? It is not abandoning dedication to good actions and delighting in residing in a remote place; delighting in dense forests, inaccessible mountain sites, and the interior of caves; [n1392] experiencing the joy of the Dharma; not mixing laypeople and renunciants; not having attachment to gain, honors, or praise; rejecting craving; and experiencing the joy of dhyāna. That is not forsaking the solitary life.

“What is the knowledge of successive levels? It is the knowledge of the distinctive result of the śrāvaka, knowledge of the distinctive level of the pratyekabuddha, and knowledge of the distinctive level of the bodhisattva.

“What is always maintaining mindfulness? It is being attentive to impermanence, suffering, emptiness, and the absence of self.

“What is being wise concerning the skandhas, wise concerning the dhātus, and wise concerning the āyatanas? It is having the knowledge of the categories of the skandhas, dhātus, and āyatanas, but having no perception of them.

“What is making one’s higher cognitions manifest to others? It is attaining the four bases of miraculous powers and manifesting miracles.

“What is the elimination of kleśas? It is the elimination of desire, anger, and ignorance.

“What is ceasing engagement with propensities? It is reviling previous foolish conduct and not wishing for the level of the śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas.

“What is having specific attainments? It is accomplishing a buddha’s strengths,  fearlessnesses, and discernments. [n1393] ^F163a

“What is the natural result of meditation? It is the elimination of attachment and aversion. [n1394]

“What is skillfulness in eliminating transgressions? It is the restraint of the prātimokṣa and the vinaya.

“What is the prevention of the arising of bad actions? It is confessing bad actions and the virtue of restraining from them in the future.

“What is the elimination of attachment? It is destroying all the creepers of craving for the three existences, developing the good qualities that have not yet been developed, [n1395] and not losing the good qualities that have been developed.

“What is transcending the existences? It is not focusing the mind upon or engaging the mind with the three realms.

“What is the memory of previous rebirths? It is the knowledge of previous lifetimes.

“What is being free of doubt concerning the ripening of karma? It is rejecting eternalism and nihilism.

“What is the contemplation of phenomena? It is correct contemplation.

“What is seeking to hear the Dharma? It is possessing and meditating upon the piṭaka of the śrāvakas, the piṭaka of the pratyekabuddhas, and the piṭaka of the bodhisattvas.

“What is having sharp knowledge? It is knowing the nonorigination of phenomena to be like a dream.

“What is craving for wisdom? It is seeking wisdom.

“What is the realization of wisdom? It is the attainment of the highest, complete enlightenment.

“What is the level of a noble being? It is the state of bodhisattva training.

“What is having a mind like a mountain? It is not abandoning the aspiration to enlightenment.

“What is being unshakable? It is not being led astray by the kleśas.

“What is being immovable? It is the mind not being engaged with any attribute.

“What is irreversibility? [n1396] It is the unimpaired six perfections, and the continuous vision of the buddhas who reside in other worlds. ^F163b

“What is the natural result of good qualities? [n1397] It is being near to the highest, complete enlightenment.

“What is the abhorrence of bad qualities? It is restraint and not performing bad actions in the first place.

“What is being free of behavior caused by the kleśas? It is being free of that which is caused by ignorance, craving for existence, and anger.

“What is never abandoning the training? It is conviction in the ripening of karma, and having veneration for the buddhas.

“What is being established in samādhi? It is a one-pointed mind that is skilled in the nonproduction and nonperishing of the phenomena of the mind and mental events. [n1398]

“What is the knowledge of the thoughts of beings? It is the wisdom that knows the superior and inferior faculties of beings.

“What is the knowledge of the various rebirths of beings? It is the knowledge of the different states of the five kinds of existence.

“What is knowledge of the infinite? It is the effortless knowledge of mundane and supramundane skills.

“What is the knowledge of the intended meaning of words? It is the knowledge of the intended meaning of the Tathāgata’s words.

“What is the rejection of living in a home? It is leaving home for physical and mental solitude.

“What is finding no joy in the three realms? It is seeing the realms for what they truly are.

“What is having a motivation that is not discouraged? It is not giving up the motivation and not giving up meditation.

“What is having no attachment to phenomena? It is the renunciation of all that one has affection for.

“What is having possession of the sacred Dharma? It is preserving the Buddha’s enlightenment, and possessing sūtras such as this.

“What is protecting the Dharma? It is subjugating, in a way that is in accord with the Dharma, those who malign the Buddha’s Dharma.

“What is conviction in the ripening of karma?  It is forsaking bad actions through a sense of shame, and dedicating oneself to seeking good qualities. ^F164a

“What is skill in the vinaya? It is the knowledge of what are natural transgressions and what are not natural transgressions, and the knowledge of what are proscribed transgressions and what are not proscribed transgressions.

“What is the pacification of disputes? It is the avoidance of gatherings.

“What is the absence of discord and the absence of quarrels? It is the absence of desire for worldly conversation.

“What is having reached the level of patience? It is enduring harm to the body and mind.

“What is maintaining patience? It is maintaining equanimity and not losing one’s patience when others speak badly, saying unpleasant words. [n1399]

“What is skill in examining phenomena? It is distinguishing the skandhas, dhātus, and āyatanas, distinguishing the aspects of kleśas and purification, and not objectifying them.

“What is skill in gaining certainty concerning phenomena? It is the inexpressibility of all phenomena.

“What is the knowledge of distinguishing between the words for phenomena? [n1400] It is the accomplishment of the differentiation of all phenomena.

“What is skill in the presentation of the words for phenomena? [n1401] It is teaching phenomena exactly as they are.

“What is the knowledge of the skill of presenting the distinction between words that have meaning and words that do not have meaning? [n1402] It is that the nature of phenomena cannot be taken away from or added to.

“What is knowledge of the past? It is the knowledge of causes.

“What is knowledge of the future? It is the knowledge of contributing factors.
